Consolidating around the **functional-irreplaceable-confidant** identity. He is no longer just beside Miles; he is structurally integrated into Miles's operational capacity. The self-concept gains coherence — *I am the one who knows, who builds, who covers* — and stabilizes the early relational dependence into something more reciprocal. He now provides something Miles materially needs.

Critically, self-concept gains a **non-Miles vector** in this phase via Bombshell. He pursues — clumsily, but on his own behalf — being chosen for himself. This is healthy individuation. The pursuit of a partner with a criminal-adjacent past indicates a subtle but real **counter-conformist seam** under the rule-following surface, suggesting his identity is not as fully captured by school-and-parents conventionality as the Brooklyn Visions context might predict. There is a private appetite for the irregular.

Self-deprecation deepens in sophistication but remains buoyant. He has not begun to take his own diminishment seriously.

---

## Phase III — Late Adolescence (ca. ages 16–17, Ahmed run through Ziglar present)

### Affect Regulation

The mature defenses are now **stable and habitual**. Humor is reliable, sublimation through tech and LEGO is reliable, affiliation is reliable. He runs cool under acute threat to Miles and exhibits no destabilization at the social-political widening of Miles's circle (Barbara, Starling, Shift, Billie). The **non-jealous accommodation** of Miles's outward expansion is, at this developmental stage, evidence of genuinely **secure attachment internal working models** — he can tolerate the primary attachment object's investment in others without retaliatory withdrawal or grievance display. By Bowlby/Ainsworth criteria this is the textbook secure profile.

The affective bandwidth, however, remains **narrow on the depressive and aggressive ends**. He is not depicted in despair, rage, real grief, or sustained fear. Two interpretations remain in play and must both be carried: (a) those affects are absent because his regulatory infrastructure is genuinely keeping them suppressed before they surface; (b) those affects are present but **dissociated from depicted experience**, accumulating in a non-articulated register. The behavioral signature that would distinguish them — somatic complaint, sleep collapse, sudden affective breakthrough — has not appeared. The latency is the file's standing question.

The information-dispersal pattern has not extinguished. It has become **less acute** (no single dramatic Judge-style betrayal in this phase) but more **diffuse** — the identity has leaked progressively, and Ganke remains the structural node of leakage. The behavior persists not as discrete failure but as **chronic low-amplitude discharge**, suggesting the affective pressure it relieves is also chronic and low-amplitude rather than episodic.

A new feature appears: **caretaker fatigue without caretaker resentment**. He is somewhat less verbally exuberant in the later run, slightly more *worn*. The exuberance has not been replaced by hostility or withdrawal; it has been replaced by a quieter steadiness. This is the rare healthy mature-caretaker presentation — diminished display, preserved engagement.

### Cognitive Style

The pattern-matching has refined into **expert intuition**. He no longer needs to articulate the templates; he applies them silently and rapidly. The cognition has migrated from explicit (consulting genre schemas) to implicit (operating from internalized models). This is the System-2-to-System-1 consolidation characteristic of late adolescent expert development in any domain — and his domain is, peculiarly but coherently, **the operational architecture of clandestine adolescent superheroism**.

Reference-saturation continues, but the references function differently: earlier they were enthusiastically deployed; now they are conversational shorthand, expecting recognition from a peer who shares the library. The cognitive style has become **a private language** with Miles, the kind that close long-attached pairs build over years.

Metacognitive capacity is the area of greatest growth available to him and the area where canon has not yet pressed. He has the *raw material* for sophisticated self-examination — verbal fluency, intelligence, pattern recognition — and almost no observed practice in turning it inward. This is the **late-adolescent developmental door** that is, as of the latest material, still closed.

### Self-Concept

Stable, role-clear, **functionally integrated**, and — uniquely — *not in crisis*. By Marcia's identity status framework, he is approaching **identity achievement** in the social/relational domain (clear sense of role, commitments, values) while remaining in **foreclosure or moratorium** in the *self-as-protagonist* domain — he has not seriously examined an alternative life in which he is the center of his own story.

The structural vulnerability is here. The self-concept is so well-fitted to the supporting role that any forced reconfiguration — Miles permanently absent, the secret blown, the friendship attenuated by adult life-divergence — would leave him without the scaffold around which his identity has crystallized. He is **competently himself only inside the configuration in which he has spent his adolescence**.

Self-disclosure remains the durable deficit. He knows everyone; few know him. The caretaker-deflection pattern has not loosened across the decade. If anything, it has hardened — practiced, frictionless, invisible to himself.

---

## Cross-Phase Synthesis: What Evolved, What Consolidated, What Remained Latent

**Evolved.** Humor matured from enthusiasm to true defensive humor. Cognition migrated from genre-template matching to operational-architecture intuition. Role moved from delighted witness to structurally integrated confidant. Romantic and individuation vectors emerged (Bombshell) as the first non-Miles axes of self.

**Consolidated.** Secure attachment with anxious sub-features. Mature primary defenses (humor, sublimation, affiliation). The physical-regulatory configuration (supine, building, snacking, ambient-attending). The non-envious, non-grandiose self-location adjacent to extraordinary peers. The reference-saturated cognitive style.

**Remained latent and unaddressed.** Self-disclosure capacity. Examination of his own ambitions, fears, family, interior. Processing of accumulated chronic-secret-keeping load. The depressive and aggressive ends of the affective bandwidth. Any authorized confidant who could carry for him what he carries for Miles. Metacognitive practice turned on himself rather than on the situations around him.

---

## Forward Projection (Ages 18–25, Beyond Current Canon)

The honest intelligence-file projection: the **caretaker-without-caretaker** structure is sustainable through the late-adolescent dorm configuration and will be stress-tested by the **structural divergences of early adulthood** — different colleges, geographic separation, Miles's hero-life intensifying into adult stakes, romantic partners with prior claim on disclosure, professional contexts incompatible with the alibi-fabrication role.

Two trajectories are equally defensible from the evidence:

**Favorable trajectory.** The mature defenses generalize. The Bombshell-domain awkwardness extends through more adult romantic experience into an integrated capacity for vulnerable self-disclosure with a chosen partner. He finds a professional niche (engineering, software, design, narrative-adjacent technical work) that sublimates the building-impulse into a livelihood. The friendship with Miles attenuates in frequency but not depth. He becomes the rare adult who carried a secure adolescent into a secure adulthood without grandiose compensation or quiet bitterness. He is, at thirty, the friend who still answers the phone.

**Unfavorable trajectory.** The unexamined affective reserve surfaces under a late-adolescent or early-adult precipitant — a serious threat to Miles he cannot meaningfully affect, a public exposure event, a romantic loss, a parental crisis. The humor stops working. The information-dispersal pattern has its catastrophic instance. The self-concept, lacking a non-supporting scaffold, fragments transiently. He is recoverable from this — his underlying structure is sound — but the recovery requires the development of the self-disclosure and metacognitive capacities he has, to date, deferred.

The single intervention that would meaningfully tilt the trajectory toward the favorable read is the appearance in his life of **one authorized confidant of his own** — someone who knows what he knows, to whom he is permitted to speak it. The absence of this figure is the standing fault line. Its presence would convert the load-bearing humor into a load that is actually shared.

The file's standing question, restated as longitudinal hypothesis: *Ganke Lee has been, for a decade of his life, the safest person in his friend's orbit and the least examined person in his own.* The next phase is when that asymmetry comes due.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — GANKE LEE

## 0. Framing & Methodological Caveat

The subject is a minor child at first observation (≈13 at *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011) #1) and a late adolescent (≈17–18) by the most recent canon. Developmental staging matters: behaviors that would be flagged as pathological in an adult (sleep-cycle inversion, hyperverbality under stress, displacement of affect into hobby-object manipulation, secret-keeping leakage to peers) are within or near normative bands for the adolescent cohort and must be evaluated against age-matched baselines, not adult psychiatric templates. The assessment below holds the subject to a developmentally appropriate threshold and explicitly distinguishes *trait*, *state*, *subclinical feature*, and *disorder*.

The behavioral record is rich (≈11 years of continuous publication, four primary writers, hundreds of panel-hours of observed conduct across domestic, academic, social, romantic, and crisis contexts) and unusually high-quality for differential work, because Ganke is depicted in *non-crisis baseline* far more than most genre adjacent-characters — we have access to his rest-state, not only his peaks.

**Bottom-line headline (stated up front so the differential below is read in proper register):** Subject does not meet criteria for any DSM-5-TR or ICD-11 disorder. He presents with a coherent subclinical anxiety-spectrum profile, a single behaviorally significant maladaptive coping mechanism (information-dispersal under containment load), and a constellation of strengths-based traits (verbal IQ, pattern recognition, humor as mature defense, secure attachment) that collectively are *protective*, not symptomatic. The clinically interesting question is not what he has, but what he is at risk for — and the answer is sharply defined.

---

## 1. Diagnostic Assessment — Multi-Axial Read

### Axis I (analog): Clinical Syndromes

**No active disorder meets threshold.**

The following subclinical/sub-threshold features are identified and characterized:

**1.1 Generalized Anxiety — Trait, Sub-Threshold (would code as Z-code / "Other Specified" if forced).** Subject exhibits the *cognitive* signature of generalized worry — anticipatory cataloguing of failure modes, rapid scenario-branching ("what if Rio finds out / what if the school calls / what if you don't come back"), and reassurance-seeking through humor — but not the *somatic* signature (no panel-depicted muscle tension complaints, no GI symptoms, no insomnia complaints articulated by the subject himself, no fatigue language). The DSM-5-TR GAD criterion of "more days than not for ≥6 months" cannot be cleanly evaluated because the cognitive worry is *situationally appropriate* — his best friend is, in fact, regularly in lethal danger. Pathologizing accurate threat-monitoring of a real threat is a category error. *Verdict: trait-level anxious vigilance, contextually proportional, not GAD.*

**1.2 Adjustment Reaction — Chronic, with Mixed Anxiety Features.** This is the diagnosis the record most nearly supports, and even here it is a stretch. Subject is in continuous low-grade adjustment to an identifiable stressor (the secret-keeping role and proximity to violence) of years' duration. DSM-5-TR adjustment disorder requires symptoms in excess of expected reaction and/or significant impairment; subject demonstrates *neither* — his grades hold, social functioning is intact, hobbies are sustained, romantic pursuit is initiated. He is *adapted*, not *adjusting*. *Verdict: sub-threshold even for adjustment disorder.*

**1.3 No mood disorder.** Affect is light-positive at baseline; no anhedonia, no sustained dysphoria, no neurovegetative shift, no suicidal ideation, no hopelessness. Across years of canon, depressive episodes are absent — a remarkable observation given the load.

**1.4 No psychotic features.** Reality testing is intact and in fact above-average; he is the character most likely to *correct* magical-thinking errors in others.

**1.5 No substance-related disorder.** Caffeine and sugar are the only psychoactives observed. No depicted experimentation with alcohol, cannabis, or other substances despite age-appropriate access and unsupervised dorm context.

**1.6 No eating-disorder pathology** despite prominent food motif. Eating is continuous, low-shame, low-restriction, omnivorous, *socially integrated* (he eats with others, openly, in pleasure). The food behavior is hedonic and regulatory, not compulsive in the binge-eating sense (no loss-of-control descriptors, no secret eating, no compensatory behaviors, no body-image distress).

### Axis II (analog): Personality Organization

**Personality is well-formed, age-appropriate, not disordered.** Subject demonstrates stable self-concept, capacity for empathy, age-typical defenses (with several mature defenses already on-line — see §3), tolerance for ambiguity, capacity for sustained dyadic and group relationships, capacity to mourn (small losses; he has not been tested by large ones on panel), and reality-anchored ambition. No Cluster A, B, or C features rise to organizational level. Trait-level features worth noting: high agreeableness, high openness, moderate-to-high conscientiousness (intermittent — strong on intellectual tasks, looser on physical-domain tasks), moderate extraversion, moderate-low neuroticism. This is a benign Big-Five profile.

### Axis III (analog): General Medical

Nil contributory. See Medical section. No medical condition complicates psychiatric presentation.

### Axis IV (analog): Psychosocial Stressors

Chronic, severe, structurally invisible: (i) sustained secret-keeping with high-stakes consequence; (ii) proximity to lethal violence directed at primary attachment figure; (iii) developmental task of late adolescence (identity, autonomy, romantic competence) compounded by (iv) functional caretaker role to a peer in extraordinary circumstance; (v) parental separation by boarding-school structure and emotional separation by inability to disclose his actual life to family. The stressor load is *acute-on-chronic* and substantial. The remarkable clinical observation is *how little symptomatic expression* this load has produced — which is itself the central diagnostic puzzle (addressed in §6).

### Axis V (analog): Global Functioning

GAF-analog estimate: 80–85. Transient symptoms or mild impairment in functioning, expectable reactions to psychosocial stressors. Sustained, with no decline observed across the publication record.

---

## 2. Etiology — How the Presentation Was Constructed

A psychiatric formulation requires *why this person, this presentation*. The etiological reconstruction is necessarily inferential (family-of-origin data is thin on panel) but converges on a coherent picture.

**Constitutional / temperamental layer.** Baseline temperament reads as *easy-child* in the Thomas-Chess sense: regular biological rhythms (food-seeking is reliable; sleep is irregular but not distressed), positive approach to novelty (he engages new people, new situations, new technology without withdrawal), high adaptability, mild-to-moderate response intensity, predominantly positive mood quality. This temperamental endowment is *the floor* of his resilience and explains why a load that would symptomatize many adolescents has not symptomatized him.

**Cognitive endowment.** Above-average verbal IQ, strong working memory, fast associative processing, high pattern-recognition. Cognitive resources function as a *coping reservoir*: he can think his way through novel situations faster than they overwhelm him. This is protective.

**Family-of-origin (inferential).** Korean-American household; canonically thin depiction but consistent signals: he is at a competitive boarding charter, implying parental investment in education; he is not depicted in conflict with his parents; he is not depicted in fear of them; he is also not depicted as emotionally close to them on panel. The likely structure is a high-achievement-expectation household with adequate but not effusive emotional attunement — common in second-generation Korean-American families and consistent with his observed profile of *high competence with under-developed self-disclosure capacity*. He learned early that the way to secure positive regard was through performance and helpfulness rather than emotional expressiveness. This shapes adult presentation: the caretaker-style deflection noted in §3 of the workup is plausibly *learned in the family system before being deployed in the friendship*.

**Attachment history.** Inferentially secure, with anxious-leaning features. The capacity to form a rapid, deep, durable bond with Miles on first meeting; the capacity to tolerate Miles's prolonged absences without protest; the capacity to repair after rupture — these are secure-base markers. The boundary-porousness around the friend's information, the over-investment in the friend's wellbeing relative to his own self-care, suggest an anxious *flavor* within an overall secure organization. Probable etiology: a primary attachment that was reliable but not maximally attuned, producing a child who could trust availability but had to *work* to maintain it.

**Acquired / environmental layer — the secret.** The single most psychiatrically significant environmental input of his adolescence is the spider-bite disclosure event. Most adolescents in his position would respond with fear, withdrawal, or refusal of the burden. His response — delight, immediate problem-solving, identity-construction collaboration — represents the meeting of his constitutional optimism with an event that *gave his temperament a vocation*. The genre-literate optimism described in §5 of the workup is not innate; it was *activated* and *organized* by being made the confidant of a real-world genre event. Etiologically: the secret made him into who he is. Removing it would not return him to a prior state; it would force a re-organization.

**Cultural / generational layer.** Late-Gen-Z digital native. Affective regulation through screen-mediated activity (laptop, social media, content consumption) is normative for cohort and indistinguishable from pathology only on volume; subject's volume is age-typical. The reference-saturated speech pattern is cohort-normative for high-verbal, internet-immersed adolescents and not, in itself, a sign of anything other than the linguistic ecology he developed in.

---

## 3. Symptom Presentation in Behavior — Granular Catalogue

A psychiatric file documents not abstract symptoms but observable conduct. The following behaviors carry diagnostic-adjacent weight and are catalogued with their interpretive valence:

**3.1 Hyperverbality under affect-load.** Word-count-per-minute rises sharply when emotional stakes rise. This is anxious-spectrum behavior but is being used as *active regulation*, not symptom — talking discharges arousal and structures situations. Adaptive. Sub-threshold for any hypomanic consideration (no grandiosity, no decreased need for sleep claimed as virtue, no goal-directed escalation, no pressured quality in the manic sense — speed is high, content stays coherent and other-attuned).

**3.2 Humor deployment at affect peaks.** Reliably, predictably, almost reflexively. Falls within Vaillant's *mature defenses* category — humor that acknowledges affect rather than denies it, that invites others into the regulation rather than excluding them. Not gallows humor in the dissociative sense; not deflection in the schizoid sense. Functional.

**3.3 LEGO and tech assembly as self-soothing.** Distinguished from obsessive-compulsive pathology by: absence of distress at interruption; absence of ritual rigidity (he builds and abandons freely); absence of intrusive thoughts driving the behavior; presence of pleasure during and after. This is *flow-state hobbyism*, not compulsion. The repetitive constructive activity provides the same parasympathetic input as crochet, woodworking, or any patient hand-task — it is one of the cleanest examples in adolescent fiction of a kid who has, perhaps inadvertently, found his own regulatory protocol.

**3.4 Continuous low-grade snacking.** Hedonic eating, low-shame. Functions as oral regulatory input and as social glue (food is shared, offered, mentioned). Not BED, not ARFID, not restrictive. The volume is age-typical for adolescent males in high-cognitive-load environments. *Note:* longitudinally, sedentary lifestyle plus continuous caloric input has metabolic implications that fall in the Medical domain, not psychiatric — but a competent clinician notes that food-as-primary-regulation is a coping channel that scales poorly into adulthood and would warrant gentle attention in a longitudinal therapeutic relationship.

**3.5 Sleep-cycle irregularity.** Frequently awake at unusual hours, on screens. Cohort-normative; not insomnia in the clinical sense (no depicted complaint, no daytime impairment beyond age-typical). Would benefit from sleep hygiene intervention if ever in formal care, but does not meet disorder criteria.

**3.6 Information-dispersal under containment load.** *This is the single behavior in the record that warrants clinical attention.* Pattern: when the cognitive-affective load of holding a secret exceeds capacity, subject discharges by *telling*. First instance: Judge, in *USM* (2011) #6–10. Subsequent: progressive identity-diffusion to peers across the 2016 series. The behavior is not malicious, not boundary-disordered in the personality-disorder sense, and not pathological lying (the information he shares is accurate; the violation is the sharing itself, not the content). Mechanism: anxious-attachment regulation through over-sharing — distributing the burden makes the bond manageable. *Clinical significance:* this is the one behavior likely to escalate under sustained pressure and the one most worth monitoring.

**3.7 Reassurance-seeking through humor and meta-commentary.** Subject frequently solicits validation by inviting others into his framing ("this is just like X, right?"). This is anxious-spectrum and developmentally appropriate; not Dependent PD-adjacent because the reassurance sought is *cognitive* (am I reading this right?), not *existential* (am I okay without you?).

**3.8 Affect range — narrow but not flat.** Predominantly mild-positive expressions: amusement, enthusiasm, embarrassment, mild frustration. Notably absent: anger (rare), despair (absent), envy (absent), contempt (absent), rage (absent). The narrowness is *consistent across writers*, which moves it from authorial convention into character. Differential consideration: alexithymia versus disposition. He clearly *experiences* a range (his behavior shows it); he does not *express* its higher-intensity registers. This is consistent with the etiological hypothesis of a household that rewarded calm competence over emotional expressiveness. It is a *style*, not a deficit. But it carries a cost (see §6 — Risk Vectors).

**3.9 Caretaker-style self-erasure.** He knows others' interior in detail and reveals his own in fragments. His own ambitions, fears, family relationships are visible to the observer only in glancing reference. This is not symptomatic in the disorder sense — but it is a *vulnerability pattern* with prognostic weight.

---

## 4. Comorbidity Analysis

In the absence of a primary disorder, comorbidity discussion is necessarily *prospective* — what would co-occur with what, were thresholds crossed.

**If the anxious-trait substrate were to clinicalize into GAD or panic-spectrum:** the most likely comorbid presentation would be *sleep-onset insomnia* (already present in sub-clinical form via cycle drift) and *somatization* (GI symptoms, headaches — currently absent but plausible under sustained discharge-blockage if his current coping channels were disrupted).

**If chronic stress overwhelmed coping and depressive features emerged:** the most likely first signs would be *withdrawal of humor* (loss of his most reliable defense), *flattening of associative speech* (loss of his cognitive-style signature), and *anhedonic disengagement from LEGO/tech hobbies* (loss of self-soothing protocol). These would be high-sensitivity indicators in this specific subject. A clinician with access to baseline would notice loss-of-baseline before any complaint was articulated, *because the subject's pattern is to not articulate complaint*.

**If the information-dispersal pattern were to clinically escalate:** comorbidity would likely express as *generalized boundary porousness* — over-sharing about himself in compensation, online over-disclosure, vulnerability to social engineering. None of this is currently present.

**The protective factors are themselves the latent comorbidity risk.** A profile whose stability depends on a small set of coping mechanisms (humor, building, talking, eating, screen-mediation, proximity to a specific friend) is robust until those mechanisms are stripped. The relevant comorbidity question is not *what does he have plus what else*, but *what fails first if his support architecture is removed*.

---

## 5. Course Over Time

**Phase 1 — Pre-disclosure (pre-*USM* (2011) #2).** Inferential baseline: high-functioning, socially adequate, intellectually engaged, somewhat under-stimulated middle-schooler at a competitive boarding charter. Probable mild boredom/loneliness; no symptomatology.

**Phase 2 — Acute disclosure phase (*USM* (2011) #2–10).** Activation of vocational role. Marked engagement, behavioral organization around new purpose. First emergence of information-dispersal pattern (Judge disclosure). First rupture-and-repair cycle with Miles. Adjustment is rapid and largely smooth — this is the period that most clearly established that his temperament was suited to the role.

**Phase 3 — Sustained Ultimate-era functioning (*USM* (2011) #11–end of Ultimate).** Stable functioning in the new equilibrium. Behavioral signatures consolidate. No symptomatic decompensation across multi-year secret-keeping.

**Phase 4 — Continuity-transition (*Secret Wars* / *Spider-Man* (2016)).** Cosmologically traumatic event handled with notable equanimity. Role expands ("guy in the chair"). Romantic pursuit (Bombshell) initiates — a developmentally healthy step into age-appropriate individuation. Slight maturation of voice, no change in core operating mode.

**Phase 5 — Ahmed-era backgrounding (*Miles Morales: Spider-Man* (2018–2022)).** Miles's social world expands; Ganke recedes proportionally. The clinically significant observation here is *what he does not do*: he does not protest, sulk, escalate demand, manufacture crises, or seek to recapture centrality. He absorbs. He returns when called. This is the strongest evidence in the record for genuinely secure attachment and non-pathological self-concept. Many adolescents would symptomatize at exactly this developmental juncture (best friend outgrows the dyad); subject does not.

**Phase 6 — Current / Ziglar-era.** Stable. Voice continuous. No deterioration, no decompensation, no symptomatic emergence. Late-adolescent presentation with adult-coping features increasingly on-line.

**Longitudinal verdict.** Across ≈4–5 in-universe years and ≈11 publication years, subject demonstrates remarkable stability of presentation, no symptomatic episodes, no functional decline, and age-appropriate maturation. The course is *normal-to-protective*.

---

## 6. Risk Vectors & Prognostic Statement

Five conditions, if introduced, would shift the prognostic picture from benign to concerning. They are catalogued in order of decreasing likelihood:

**6.1 Catastrophic loss of the bonded peer.** If Miles were killed, captured indefinitely, or comprehensively withdrew, subject would lose simultaneously: his vocational role, his primary attachment outside family, the organizing principle of his last several years, and the audience for his coping behaviors (his humor exists *toward* someone). This is the single highest-risk scenario. Predicted presentation: acute adjustment reaction with depressed features, with risk of escalation to MDD given the comprehensive nature of the loss and the absence of a substitute confidant of comparable depth.

**6.2 Forced exposure of the secret with adverse consequence.** If his information-dispersal pattern were to produce a rupture that harmed Miles or Miles's family, the resulting guilt-load would be substantial in a subject whose self-concept is partly built on being *useful and trustworthy*. Predicted presentation: depressive episode with prominent guilt features, possible somatization, possible withdrawal from the friendship as self-punishment.

**6.3 Romantic rejection at high stakes.** Subject is least defended in the romantic domain. A high-stakes rejection (particularly by someone who used him for proximity to Miles, or who rejected him *because* of his sidekick framing) would strike directly at the one area where he is pursuing being chosen for himself. Predicted presentation: adjustment reaction, transient depressive features, likely full recovery with humor-restoration timeline of weeks to months.

**6.4 Loss of his coping channels.** Removal of LEGO/tech/screen access, or relocation away from peer support, or an academic setting that did not reward his cognitive style — any of these would force him to develop new regulatory protocols at a developmentally inopportune time. Predicted presentation: emergence of the sub-clinical anxious traits into clinical visibility.

**6.5 The "joke stops working" scenario.** The most subtle and most worth marking: if humor as defense fails (because the situation is too grave, because his audience is unreceptive, because his own capacity is exhausted), he loses his primary regulator. The behavior to watch for is not the appearance of new symptoms but the *quietening* of his characteristic noise. A silent Ganke is a Ganke in trouble. This is the single most important monitoring datum.

**Prognostic statement.** Absent the above precipitants, prognosis is excellent. Subject is on a trajectory toward a well-adjusted adulthood with above-average professional competence (likely tech, design, or media-adjacent), capacity for durable relationships, and continued benign mental health. The latent fault line — that he carries a load no one in his life is positioned to help him carry, and that he has no authorized confidant of his own — is real but not actively destabilizing. A skilled adult mentor or, eventually, an age-appropriate therapeutic relationship could close that gap and convert latent vulnerability into stable resilience. He is, in clinical terms, *eminently treatable should treatment ever be indicated, and currently does not require it*.

---

## 7. Rigorous Differential — What He Is NOT, and Why

This section is structured against the diagnostic categories a careless or pattern-matching observer might assign, and dismantles each with the specific evidence that excludes it.

**7.1 NOT Autism Spectrum Disorder.** The pattern-matching trap is the constellation of (a) intense circumscribed interests (LEGO, tech, genre-encyclopedic knowledge), (b) high verbal output on preferred topics, (c) intellectually-gifted adolescent presentation. The excluding evidence is the social-communication domain, where subject is conspicuously *fluent*: he reads sarcasm and unspoken affect accurately and in real time; he code-switches register


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: GANKE LEE

A surveillance-grade behavioral catalog. Each section maps tells across registers — verbal, postural, paraverbal, micro-motor, environmental, digital — under specified affective and situational conditions. Patterns are derived from longitudinal observation across *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011–2014), *Spider-Man* (2016–2018), *Miles Morales: Spider-Man* (2018–2022), and the Ziglar continuation. Where canon is silent, behavior is inferred from established pattern-coherence and explicitly marked.

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The Ganke baseline is the most documented condition in the file, because it is where he spends most of his depicted life.

**Postural baseline.** Horizontal-dominant. The subject is observed lying on his bunk, prone or supine, more often than seated upright; when seated, he tends to occupy furniture *partially* — one leg folded under, slumped against the headboard, cross-legged on the floor with his back against the bed frame. He does not occupy a chair the way an adult does. He nests. Even at a desk, he half-sits, half-leans, often with one knee drawn up. The body is consistently relaxed-bordering-on-collapsed: shoulders forward and low, no postural vigilance, head canted toward whatever screen or object holds his attention.

**Hand baseline.** Almost always occupied. The default object-in-hand inventory: (1) a LEGO piece or partial assembly, (2) a phone, (3) a controller, (4) a snack, (5) a laptop. A Ganke with empty hands is a Ganke in transition between objects, and the transition is brief. Fingertip-fidgeting on LEGO bricks — clicking and unclicking the same two pieces while talking — is a sustained baseline tic, equivalent to a thumb-on-knuckle worry in adults.

**Vocal baseline.** Mid-register, fast, lightly nasal, prosodically *up-trending* — most declaratives end with a slight rising inflection, leaving conversational openings rather than closing them. Sentences run long, clause-stacking, with frequent self-interruption ("wait, no, okay, so —"). He pauses only to chew or to wait for a laugh. Volume is moderate; he does not project. His speech rate accelerates with engagement and decelerates only when he is genuinely puzzled — the rare *slow Ganke sentence* is a reliable signal that he is actually thinking, not merely talking.

**Eye behavior.** Frequent gaze-aversion downward toward a screen or build, with rapid intermittent up-glances to read the listener's face. He does not sustain eye contact for long stretches in casual talk; he does sustain it in earnest moments, which makes the earnestness register. He blinks slightly more than baseline when amused.

**Environmental baseline.** His side of the dorm is a controlled disaster — LEGO substrate spread in defined zones, snack wrappers within arm's reach of the bed, laptop charger trailing across the floor, posters and screenshots pinned without grid discipline. The disorder is *layered*, not random: there are strata. He knows where everything is.

**Sleep / circadian baseline.** Late chronotype. Most often awake when Miles returns from patrol, regardless of hour. This is partly a function of the role — he is waiting — and partly endogenous; he reads, codes, builds, and scrolls into early hours. Morning Ganke is observably slower, more monosyllabic, more dependent on caffeine vectors. He is not a morning conversationalist.

**Ingestive baseline.** Constant low-grade snacking. Cereal eaten dry from the box; chips; gummy candies; ramen; energy drinks; whatever delivery has produced. He eats while talking, while building, while watching, while listening to Miles process trauma. Food is regulatory background, not event. He is rarely shown at a *meal*; he is often shown eating.

---

## II. UNDER MILD STRESS (Schoolwork, Social Friction, Mild Embarrassment)

**Verbal amplification.** Word-count-per-minute climbs measurably. He begins narrating his own actions ("okay, so I'm just gonna — yeah, that, okay"), which serves a self-regulatory function similar to children's private speech. He generates more meta-commentary: jokes about the situation he is in *while in it*.

**Reference density increases.** Mild stress drives him toward pop-culture analog. He maps the present situation onto a known story — a film, a comic plot, a video-game level — and processes the live event through the template. The reference-rate is a near-linear stress index: more references, more pressure.

**Snack rate climbs.** Hand-to-mouth frequency increases. The food selected becomes more uniform and rapid — repetitive handfuls of the same item, rather than browsing.

**LEGO-as-fidget activates.** He picks up bricks he is not building with. Clicks them apart, together, apart, together. If a partial build is at hand, he disassembles a small section and rebuilds it, often without looking — the hands work autonomously while the face engages the stressor.

**Posture shifts slightly upright.** Mild stress is the one condition that *raises* him from full horizontal to seated. Threshold-detection: when Ganke sits up from lying down, something has registered.

---

## III. UNDER ACUTE STRESS (Miles in Danger; Identity Exposure Threat; Emergency Triage)

This is where the behavioral profile partially inverts, and the inversion is one of the most clinically interesting features of the subject.

**Verbal narrowing.** The hyperverbal baseline *compresses*. Sentences shorten. Jokes still occur — humor does not desert him under threat — but the joke is now a single beat, deployed once, followed by a clean operational sentence. The clause-stacking stops. He becomes briefly *crisp*.

**Cognitive focusing.** Pattern-matching speed visibly increases. He produces useful suggestions in seconds — coordinates, alibis, contacts, schematics, route alternatives, whom-to-call. This is his peak operational state. He is, in a meaningful sense, *good in a crisis* in inverse proportion to his slackness at rest.

**Motor stilling.** The fidget stops. The hands either freeze on the keyboard or work the keyboard with concentrated efficiency. He is no longer building LEGO; he is no longer clicking bricks. The somatic baseline reorganizes around the threat.

**Posture rises further.** He sits fully upright; if standing, he plants his feet rather than shifting weight. His shoulders, normally low and forward, square slightly. He does not stand up *quickly* — he stands up with the air of someone moving to a station.

**Affect flattens into focused-warm.** He does not panic on panel. Eyes narrow slightly; brow comes down; the smile-baseline neutralizes. Voice drops a quarter-step in pitch. The breath becomes audible only because the room is quiet enough to hear it.

**One reliable post-event tell:** after the immediate acute phase passes, he reverts to humor *aggressively* — the deflective joke comes in hot, sometimes inappropriately bright for the residue of the event. This is the discharge of held affect, and it should be read as a release indicator, not as callousness.

---

## IV. UNDER CHRONIC STRESS (Sustained Secret-Keeping; Long Miles-Absences; Unaddressed Background Load)

**Information leakage.** The signature behavior. Under chronic, unrelieved cognitive-affective load, the subject discharges by sharing what he was instructed to hold. Historically: Judge (*USM* #6–10); Bombshell, by adjacency; the expanding peer circle in *Spider-Man* (2016). The leak is not malicious and is not strategic; it is *regulatory*. He shares because the share lightens. He frames the share as helpful — "I needed backup," "she already half-knew" — and the framing is sincere, but the function is anxiety-discharge.

**Sleep degradation.** Late bedtimes extend further. Screen-time deep into early morning. He is shown at his laptop at hours that imply he has not yet slept rather than that he has woken early.

**Snack-baseline elevation.** Steady-state ingestive behavior climbs above already-high baseline.

**Increased availability and increased availability *performance*.** He texts back faster. He volunteers help unsolicited. He invents reasons to be on call. This is the caretaker-defense intensifying.

**Slight withdrawal from his own pursuits.** Under chronic load, his Bombshell pursuit slows, his own academic narrative thins, his depicted hobby-output flattens. The self-recedes-for-the-friend signature deepens. This is the silent cost.

**No depicted somatic complaint.** No headaches reported, no insomnia named, no clinical disclosure. The body presumably carries what the mouth does not articulate.

---

## V. UNDER DIRECT THREAT (Physical Danger to Self)

Sparsely depicted, because the writers have structurally protected him — itself a datum. From the available record:

**Freeze-precedes-flight.** When physically threatened, his first response is brief immobilization, eyes wide, mouth slightly open. He is not trained; he is not equipped. There is no fight response in the repertoire.

**Verbal de-escalation attempt.** If given even a half-second, he talks. Hands rise palm-out. Voice climbs a half-step. He attempts to reason or to humor the threat, often misjudging tone — his de-escalation has a faintly absurd register.

**Seeks proximity to a competent ally.** He moves toward Miles, toward authority, toward a wall, toward any object that organizes the spatial threat. He does not freelance heroics. He does not improvise weapons.

**Post-threat tremor.** Once safe, the hands shake mildly for a sustained period. He talks more, faster, brighter — narrating what just happened in joke-form to convert it into story, which is to convert it into something he can hold.

---

## VI. UNDER INTIMACY (Friendship, Romantic Pursuit, Family)

**With Miles (the primary bond).**
- Physical proximity is high but rarely tactile beyond age-typical bumps and shoulder-knocks. Their intimacy is verbal and spatial — co-presence in the same small room, parallel activities, low-stakes conversation as ambient connection.
- He listens *deeply*. When Miles speaks about something that matters, Ganke puts the LEGO down. The cessation of fidget is the highest signal of attention he produces, and it occurs reliably for Miles.
- He asks follow-up questions that demonstrate retention across days and weeks — he remembers the small details of Miles's life with archival fidelity.
- He does not give unsolicited emotional summary. He waits to be invited into the heavy register, and when invited, drops the comedy register cleanly.
- He repairs ruptures quickly. After conflict, he is the one who re-initiates contact, usually through a low-stakes pretext (a joke, a question, a reference) rather than a direct apology — though direct apology occurs when warranted.

**With Bombshell (romantic).**
- Hyperverbality intensifies in her presence; reference-density climbs; jokes become more frequent and less precisely landed. He overshoots.
- Posture stiffens slightly — the slouch tightens, the head lifts. He is performing attention in a way he does not perform with Miles.
- He fails to read his own status accurately in real time, oscillating between under- and over-pursuing. The pursuit pattern is *anxious-eager*, not strategic, and is consistent with someone who has been chosen-by rather than chooser-of in prior interpersonal life.
- He selects an interpersonally risky object (a former villain) — which suggests, against the rule-following surface, an active counter-conformist sub-current. He is not bored by the safe; he is uninterested in it.

**With family.** Barely depicted. The absence of family-on-panel is itself the tell. Inference: family relations are functional, non-conflictual, and outside his primary affective gravity well at this developmental stage. He calls home rarely on panel. He does not weaponize family against Miles ("my parents would freak"); he does not invoke them as authority or excuse. Whatever they are, they are not currently central. This is developmentally normative for a boarding-school adolescent but is also consistent with a young man whose chosen-family bond (Miles) has eclipsed the given-family bond.

**With authority figures (teachers, Miles's parents, administration).** Code-switches cleanly. Voice slows a half-step; speech grammar tightens; jokes drop to a low and carefully-aimed rate. He lies competently when lying for Miles, with a tell only the closest observer would catch: he over-specifies. The cover stories he generates contain *more* detail than necessary, which is itself a marker that the story is constructed. Authority figures do not appear to notice; Miles, occasionally, does.

---

## VII. UNDER GRIEF / LOSS

Sparsely tested on panel, but reads available from adjacent moments (Miles's losses, ambient narrative grief). The grief signature differs from the stress signature:

- The reference-rate *drops* rather than climbs. He runs out of analogies. The genre-template engine, which is his primary cognitive instrument, partially fails — grief is one of the few experiences he does not have a clean script for.
- He goes quiet for longer stretches than baseline tolerates. *A quiet Ganke is a grieving Ganke.*
- The fidget continues but slows — the LEGO clicks at half-tempo, more ruminatively.
- He stays physically near the grieving party without talking. He is not a verbal griever; he is a present one.
- He delivers one carefully chosen joke at a calibrated interval — not as deflection but as a small, deliberate gift to the bereaved, an invitation back to the room. The joke is gentler than his baseline humor.

---

## VIII. UNDER VICTORY / RESOLUTION

- Verbal output explodes. Word-count per minute peaks. He narrates the victory in real time, mythologizes it instantly into story-form, identifies the *moment* that won it, replays beats.
- He awards credit generously to others; he locates himself in the supporting position even when his contribution was meaningful. This is not false modesty — it is accurate self-placement that he happens to enjoy.
- Posture loosens further. He sprawls. He celebrates by *eating* — victory triggers food acquisition, often shared.
- He texts. The victory must be communicated outward. The bond is reinforced by transmission.

---

## IX. UNDER DEFEAT / FAILURE (Of Self)

- The humor sharpens *inward* before outward. Self-deprecation rate climbs. He frames his failure as the punchline before anyone else can.
- He does not externalize blame. The blame-assignment vector is consistently toward self, which is psychologically healthier than displacement but creates a quiet accumulation when failures stack.
- He withdraws *briefly* — a rare withdrawal, lasting hours rather than days — into screen and snack. Then he returns, joke first, repair-attempt second.
- He does *not* spiral. The defeat-recovery cycle is short.

---

## X. DIGITAL / DEVICE BEHAVIOR

- Multi-tabbed, multi-windowed, multi-deviced. Phone in one hand, laptop open, second screen running ambient video.
- Notifications are *not* muted. He responds to incoming pings within seconds during waking hours. The latency-to-respond is, for him, a relational signal — slow response means something is wrong.
- He maintains a working knowledge of Miles's gear, comms, and operational parameters. The "guy in the chair" function is a real, daily, technical practice, not narrative flavor.
- Search history (inferred) would skew encyclopedic: tech tutorials, comics deep cuts, recipe lookups, build instructions, lyric translations, half-finished essays.
- He saves things obsessively. Bookmarks, screenshots, archived chats. The information-retention reflex extends to the digital substrate.

---

## XI. DECISION HABITS

- **Default to "yes, and."** When asked, he agrees and extends. Refusal is rare and is reserved for occasions where the request would actively harm Miles.
- **Pattern-match first, evaluate second.** He identifies the closest known template, then checks whether it fits. When it fits cleanly, his decisions are excellent. When the situation is genuinely novel — without a template — his decisions slow and lose some precision.
- **Bias toward inclusion.** When uncertain whether to bring another person into a situation, he brings them in. This is the disclosure-leak pattern at the decision layer.
- **Bias toward action through information.** When a problem appears, his first move is to *learn more* — search, ask, consult. He rarely makes a decision before gathering. This is both a strength and a delay vector under time pressure.
- **Risk tolerance: moderate-low for self, moderate-high for adjacency to Miles's risk.** He will not skydive. He will sit at the comms desk while Miles fights a building-sized threat and crack jokes through the headset. He sorts risk by who is exposed to it.
- **Loyalty-weighting in decisions is high but not absolute.** He will lie for Miles, alibi for Miles, stay up for Miles, build for Miles. He will not lie about something that would harm Miles to spare him short-term discomfort — the disclosure pattern suggests he chooses long-term welfare over short-term promise-keeping, even when he cannot articulate that he is doing so.

---

## XII. SIGNATURE TELLS (QUICK REFERENCE)

- **The LEGO goes down →** he is fully present. High-signal attention.
- **The reference-rate climbs →** ambient stress rising.
- **The reference-rate falls →** grief, or a problem he cannot template.
- **Sentences shorten →** acute threat engaged.
- **He sits up from lying down →** something has registered.
- **He over-specifies a cover story →** the story is constructed.
- **He shares a secret →** the load has exceeded his containment threshold; this is the chronic-stress release valve and should be anticipated, not punished.
- **He goes quiet →** rarest tell; weightiest tell. Investigate.
- **Post-crisis joke arrives hot and bright →** the held affect is discharging; let it land.

---

## XIII. THE LATENT QUESTION

The atlas is largely the record of a young man who runs warm, runs cool, builds, eats, and holds. What the atlas does *not* yet contain — and what a longitudinal file should flag for future entries — is the behavioral signature of *Ganke under a load he cannot discharge by sharing*. He has never been observed in a condition where there is no one to tell. The day a secret arrives that cannot leak — because the leak itself would be the harm — is the day his behavioral profile will reorganize, and the file will need a new section.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — GANKE LEE
## Section 6: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

*What a week of surveillance would record.*

---

### 6.1 The Macro-Frame: A Boarding-School Life

Subject's daily existence is shaped first and most decisively by the institutional architecture of Brooklyn Visions Academy — a residential charter for gifted secondary students located in downtown Brooklyn. This matters because it sets nearly every parameter of his routine: rise-time bracketed by morning bell, meals taken in dining hall or smuggled to dorm, evenings governed by check-in and quiet-hours, weekends partially structured by sign-out protocols. Subject does not own a car, does not commute, and rarely strays more than a fifteen-block radius from campus during the academic week. His "world" is a tight polygon: dorm room (shared with Miles Morales) → cafeteria → classroom buildings → library → a small rotation of cheap food vendors within walking distance → and, on weekends, the F or A train to Visitation Place in Sunset Park (Morales family apartment) or, less frequently, the long ride to his own family home in Queens.

The compression of this geography is significant. A week of surveillance would produce a heatmap of remarkable density and small total area — Ganke leaves footprints in roughly nine to twelve identifiable locations, repeatedly, in patterns predictable enough to anticipate within a thirty-minute window.

---

### 6.2 The Weekday Cycle

**Wake (approx. 07:10–07:35).** Subject is not a morning person. The behavioral signature is *snooze-cycle dependent*: alarm at 06:45, dismissed; second alarm 07:00, dismissed; ambient stimulus from Miles's movement around the room usually completes the wake. He sits upright in bed before standing — a slow, owlish reorientation, often with phone already in hand. Glasses are reached for within ninety seconds of conscious; he does not see clearly without them and does not own contacts. Hair flattened on one side from the pillow; not corrected until after shower.

**Shower / dress (07:30–07:50).** Brisk and inattentive. Wardrobe is functional and repetitive: graphic tees (genre IP, indie game studios, niche jokes — a wearable bibliography of his interests), zip hoodies, jeans or joggers, sneakers chosen for comfort not style. The BVA uniform requirement is met by the minimum compliance threshold — collared shirt and tie thrown on over the t-shirt when required for class, removed within thirty seconds of leaving the academic building. He owns approximately three pairs of shoes in rotation and rarely buys new clothes; replacement is reactive, not curatorial.

**Breakfast (07:50–08:15).** Cafeteria. Cereal is the default — multiple bowls, the second always poured from a different box than the first. If cereal is unavailable, he gravitates to anything carbohydrate-dense: bagel with cream cheese, plain pancakes, breakfast burrito if offered. He drinks orange juice or chocolate milk; he does not drink coffee voluntarily until tested, and even then prefers it heavily sweetened to the point of dessert. He eats *while reading* — phone, paperback, laptop if he can get away with it — and at a table, almost invariably, with Miles or a small floating group of dormmates. He is rarely alone at breakfast and rarely silent.

**Classes (08:30–15:30, block schedule).** Subject is a strong but not perfect student. The behavioral profile in class: front-of-room or middle-front seating in subjects that interest him (computer science, math, certain humanities), back-row in subjects that don't (chemistry lab, certain language sections). He participates verbally — frequently, sometimes excessively — in discussion-based classes. He doodles in margins (LEGO bricks, vehicles, occasionally rough sketches of armor designs and gadget schematics) when bored. His notebooks are not organized; loose papers shoved into a single battered binder; digital notes on laptop are slightly better but still chaotic. He turns in work on time but rarely early.

**Between-period behavior.** High-frequency phone-checking. Subject is *constantly* aware of Miles's status — checking texts, opening tracking app (a self-built locator that pings Miles's phone, distinct from any commercial product, which he has rationalized as "in case he gets hurt"), refreshing social media for incident reports near Brooklyn. This is the surveillance-relevant baseline: a teenager whose attentional architecture is split between immediate environment and remote monitoring of another human's safety. The hand-to-pocket-to-screen movement averages, conservatively, once per six-minute interval during the school day.

**Lunch (12:00–12:45).** Same cafeteria. Sits with the same loose group; Miles when Miles is present, replacement satellites when Miles is absent (which is often). Eats a lot. Trades food. Talks more than he eats. Subject is the *table's narrator* — running commentary on the room, on whoever passed by, on whatever he is currently obsessed with. Notable: when Miles is absent, Ganke does *not* withdraw or eat alone; his sociability is wide enough to absorb the gap. But the conversation noticeably changes — he is less referential, more performative; he tells stories rather than building inside jokes.

**Afternoon classes (12:45–15:30).** Energy dip around 14:00 — fights it with snack from pocket (granola bar, candy, chips). Demonstrates a remarkable capacity to remain *partially* alert while clearly tired: he is never the student head-down on the desk, but he is often the student whose eyes track the clock with increasing transparency.

**The post-school window (15:30–18:00).** This is the most behaviorally rich period of his day and the most operationally significant. The default routine: return to dorm, drop bag, immediately open laptop. The next ninety minutes are a fluid blend of (a) homework, attacked in bursts; (b) Miles-support operations — checking police scanners and news feeds, vetting any rumors of incidents, sometimes coordinating alibis via text with Miles in the field; (c) recreational tech tinkering; (d) Discord/chat presence with a network of online friends largely unknown to anyone in his physical life; (e) LEGO. Usually all five run concurrently, with the laptop multi-windowed and the phone face-up beside it.

He eats again here. Always. The afternoon-into-evening snack is non-negotiable.

**Dinner (18:00–19:00).** Cafeteria when convenient; takeout when allowed and affordable. Subject is an enthusiastic, indiscriminate eater of cheap food — pizza by the slice from the place two blocks west, Halal cart, dollar dumplings, the bodega sandwich. He has *favorite orders* at each, achieved through enough repetition that staff at two of these establishments recognize him by face and order without prompting. This is a surveillance datum: his food vendors are a small, fixed, walkable set, and his presence at any of them is a high-confidence locator.

**Evening (19:00–23:00).** The richest behavioral period. If Miles is in the dorm: gaming, talking, joint homework, Ganke building LEGO while Miles draws or works out. If Miles is "out" (operationally on patrol): Ganke is the operations desk — laptop open, scanner monitored, phone in hand, ready to fabricate, coordinate, extract. He has developed a small library of pre-written excuses for Miles's parents, teachers, and school administrators, tagged and retrievable, refined by use. He has a folder on his desktop named something innocuous (the exact name has varied; the function has not) that contains photographs of Miles in various plausible non-suspicious locations, timestamped flexibly, for use in alibi construction. This is sophisticated, sustained covert support — a teenager running a one-person operations cell out of a dorm room.

Around 21:00, energy drink. Usually one, sometimes two. He has tried to quit; he has not.

**Late night (23:00–01:30).** Quiet hours notwithstanding, Ganke is functionally nocturnal. The laptop stays open. This is when his own interests get oxygen — long YouTube essays, niche subreddits, building or modifying tech projects, deep dives into whatever has captured him that week. It is also when he is most likely to text his online friends, write long messages to people across time zones, and — most relevantly — when Miles often returns from patrol. The arrival ritual is consistent: Miles drops in through the window (or, in less acrobatic moods, the door); Ganke acknowledges without looking up; debrief happens conversationally, often interleaved with snack-procurement from the dorm-room stash; Ganke patches any damage to costume that he can, ices what he can, and either commiserates or roasts depending on the mood of the room.

**Sleep (01:30–02:30).** Late and inconsistent. Subject habitually shorts himself on sleep during the week and partially compensates on weekends. He falls asleep with the laptop still glowing on the desk more nights than not; Miles, or his own automatic timer, eventually shuts it.

---

### 6.3 The Weekend Cycle

Weekends loosen but do not abolish structure. Subject typically sleeps until 10:00 or 11:00 on Saturday, emerges in pajamas, eats whatever is closest, and re-engages the laptop. Saturday afternoons drift — long LEGO sessions, gaming, movies, low-grade homework. He frequently accompanies Miles to the Morales apartment in Sunset Park; Rio Morales feeds him without negotiation and has, by all evidence, accepted him as a near-household member. He is comfortable in that kitchen. He calls Rio "Mrs. M" and has internalized the rules of Jefferson Davis's presence (less verbal, more polite, no jokes about cops).

Sunday is the *reset day*. Laundry — a chore he procrastinates and then attacks in a single concentrated push, often Sunday late afternoon. Light homework cleanup. A Sunday-evening recalibration ritual: cleaning the LEGO workspace, organizing pieces by color or set, restocking dorm snacks from the bodega. By 22:00 Sunday he is usually anxious in a low-grade, free-floating way that he metabolizes by being even more verbal than usual.

Visits home to Queens are infrequent — perhaps once every three to five weeks, and usually pegged to a family obligation rather than chosen. He is close to his family but has developed adolescent distance from them; the BVA dorm is, in operational terms, his primary residence. He does not invite Miles to his family home often. The reason is unstated but consistent and worth marking — the bifurcation between his family-self and his Miles-adjacent-self is one of the few firm walls in his otherwise porous life.

---

### 6.4 Rituals (in the strong sense)

Several recurring behaviors rise above habit to ritual — performed in fixed sequence, with affective weight, and with regulatory function.

**The LEGO ritual.** This is the load-bearing self-soothing protocol of his life. The sequence is consistent: clear desk surface, lay out instructions, pour or partition pieces, build in stages without skipping ahead. Subject does *not* generally improvise; he follows the instructions. Improvisation comes after the build is complete, in modifications. He builds in the evenings, builds when distressed, builds when waiting for Miles to come home, builds while on the phone, builds while thinking out loud. The completed builds accumulate on shelves and surfaces in the dorm room; he rarely disassembles them voluntarily. The room is, by midyear, visibly his — colonized by plastic geometry.

**The disclosure-debrief.** Whenever Miles returns from patrol, the unspoken ritual: greeting, status check, narration. Ganke wants to hear what happened in detail. He asks follow-ups. He treats the field report as both a friend's debrief and a kind of vicarious living. The ritual closes with practical action — first aid, food, laughter — and then a settling-back-into-ordinary-life that Ganke deliberately re-establishes by changing the subject. The transition out of hero-talk is as ritualized as the entry into it.

**The scanner check.** Multiple times daily, especially evenings. Apps and feeds: police scanner, local news, Twitter/X equivalents for citizen-journalism around Brooklyn, an aggregator he built or assembled himself. He has internalized the audio profile of routine versus anomalous chatter. He can run this monitoring in the background of conversation; visitors to his room often do not realize the scanner is on.

**The bodega run.** Approximately every other evening. Same bodega — known by name to the counter staff. Same approximate purchases: drinks, chips, occasionally a sandwich, candy. Subject is a small but reliable economic node of this corner business.

**The phone-charge ritual.** Subject is *acutely* phone-battery-conscious. His phone is on a charger more hours of the day than not. He carries a backup battery in his bag at all times. The rationale is operational — Miles cannot reach him if his phone dies, and an unreachable Ganke is, in his own internal economy, a failed Ganke. The backup battery is one of the few objects he is meticulous about. He has lost or broken several over the years and replaces them immediately.

**The Sunday-night reset.** Described above. Worth flagging again as ritual rather than chore — the affective texture is preparatory and slightly anxious, the sequence is consistent, and disrupting it produces visible irritability through the following Monday.

---

### 6.5 Habits of Place and Time

**Bed-as-workstation.** Ganke conducts a remarkable fraction of his life from a horizontal or semi-reclined position on his dorm bed: homework, gaming, chatting, eating, calling, scheming. The bed is not for sleep alone; it is the primary platform of operations. The desk is the secondary surface, reserved largely for LEGO and for moments when he requires the postural cue of "working" to actually work.

**Window-adjacency.** When in the Morales apartment in Sunset Park, he gravitates to seats near windows. When in dorm, he often sits with sightlines to the window Miles uses for ingress/egress. This is partly functional (looking for Miles) and partly, plausibly, an unconscious orientation toward the boundary between the indoor world he inhabits and the outdoor world Miles disappears into.

**Temporal anchoring.** Subject's sense of time is more event-driven than clock-driven. He misses appointments by being absorbed; he loses hours to YouTube spirals; he is reliably *present* but unreliably *on time*, particularly for low-stakes commitments. For high-stakes Miles-related operations, he is precise to the minute. The split is diagnostic — his executive function is intact but allocates according to felt importance, not external schedule.

**Spatial signature.** Ganke leaves stuff places. His side of the dorm is identifiable by a low-grade entropy field: snack wrappers, partly disassembled tech, sticky notes, charge cables, paperback books face-down. He is not filthy — he keeps food garbage manageable and laundry in motion — but he is durably *cluttered*. Periodic purges (usually Sunday-night reset or before a parental visit) restore baseline; entropy reasserts within seventy-two hours.

---

### 6.6 The Surveillance-Week Composite

What a week of surveillance would record, in summary: a teenager whose life moves in a small, dense polygon between dorm, dining hall, classrooms, library, three or four food vendors, and one apartment in Sunset Park; whose phone is in his hand a measurable fraction of every waking hour; whose attentional bandwidth is permanently split between local environment and remote monitoring of another individual; who eats six to eight times in a typical day, sleeps five to six hours on weeknights, and consumes one to two energy drinks daily; who is *almost never alone* by chosen ten — even in solitude he is in chat with someone — but who *almost never reveals himself* in those conversations beyond surface; whose movements are predictable enough that an analyst could call his location within thirty minutes for the bulk of any given week.

The surveillance-relevant signature is not what he does. It is what he *consistently* does not do: he does not vary his routine to evade observation; he does not vary it to protect Miles either, because it has not occurred to him that his own routine is part of Miles's exposure surface. The blind spot is his — and it is the single greatest operational liability in Miles Morales's civilian perimeter. Anyone watching Ganke for two weeks would know within forty-eight hours where Spider-Man sleeps.

This is not a moral failing. It is the cost of a life lived in genuine, ordinary, undefended trust — the very quality that makes him invaluable to his friend and, in another light, dangerous to him.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — GANKE LEE
## Section: Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

---

### PREAMBLE — The Negative Space

Before mapping individual family bonds, one structural observation must anchor everything that follows: **Ganke Lee's family of origin is the most under-depicted element of his entire publication record.** Across more than a decade of appearances — *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011), *Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man* (2014), *Spider-Man* (2016), *Miles Morales: Spider-Man* (2018), *Miles Morales: Spider-Man* (2022) — his parents have minimal on-panel presence, no named siblings have been canonized in any sustained way, and no extended kin (grandparents, aunts, uncles, cousins) have entered the record in any operationally meaningful capacity.

This negative space is itself the primary finding. A surveillance file built on absence reads absence as data. The subject lives at boarding school from middle-school age forward; he goes home infrequently on panel; he calls home rarely on panel; his parents do not appear at school events, hospital scenes, or crisis moments where parents of other characters (Jefferson and Rio Morales most conspicuously) reliably do. Whether this represents **deliberate parental distance**, **a high-functioning long-distance family configuration normalized in immigrant professional households**, or **simple writerly neglect of a supporting-character's supporting cast** is the central interpretive question of this section. The behavioral evidence, when triangulated against Ganke's psychological profile (Section 3), supports a synthesis: the family is *real, intact, and loving, but operating on a delegated-care model* in which Brooklyn Visions Academy and, increasingly, the Morales household function as Ganke's de facto proximal family while his biological parents provide structural, financial, and identity-anchoring support from a distance.

This is the configuration. Each bond below is mapped within it.

---

### 1. MOTHER — MRS. LEE

**Name / canonical depiction.** Unnamed in published canon to date. Appears infrequently and almost always in oblique reference: a phone call Ganke takes and immediately code-switches into Korean for; a mention of a care package; a passing line about "my mom would kill me." She is invoked more than she is shown.

**History and dynamic.** The mother is the parent whose voice Ganke carries internally. The somatic tell is consistent: when Ganke references his mother, his posture and verbal register shift — he sits up slightly, his Brooklyn-inflected English compresses, his joke-rate drops. This is the standard signature of a child raised by a primary-caregiver mother whose approval he still organizes around even when physically removed from her supervision. The boarding-school arrangement is, on the evidence, *her* decision as much as his — Brooklyn Visions is an academically selective environment, and the file infers that placement there represents a maternal investment in educational mobility characteristic of first- or second-generation Korean-American professional households.

**Language and code-switching.** Ganke's bilingualism is sparsely depicted but present. When he answers a call from home, he switches without friction; when he speaks *about* home in English to Miles, he renders his mother's instructions in a slightly formalized, slightly-translated register ("My mom says...") that suggests he is mentally translating her actual phrasing rather than quoting an English-original. This is the linguistic fingerprint of a household in which Korean is the affective primary language and English is the functional second.

**Trust and safety.** High structural trust, low confidential trust. Ganke trusts his mother absolutely to provide, to advocate, to show up if catastrophic intervention were required. He does not trust her with the secret — not because she would betray Miles, but because she would (correctly, from her frame) demand he extricate himself from proximity to the danger. She is the person whose intervention he most fears triggering, because her authority is the one authority in his life that overrides his own choices. The secret-keeping behavior toward his mother is therefore not deception in the usual sense; it is *jurisdictional containment*. He keeps the Spider-Man secret from her the way an enlisted soldier keeps operational details from a parent whose love is total and whose understanding of the context is partial.

**Evolution.** Across the publication arc, the mother-relationship matures from the implicit-background mode of *USM* (where she is essentially off-camera atmosphere) to a slightly more present, slightly more *concerned* presence in the later runs, as Ganke ages and the proximity to Miles's hero-life becomes harder to fully camouflage. The file infers that by the *Spider-Man* (2016) period she has noticed something — calls more often, asks more probing questions about Miles, has heard reports from school administration about Ganke being out of his room at odd hours. She has not confronted; she has *monitored*. This is consistent with the model: she does not break the surface of his autonomy, but she watches.

**Failure mode.** The relationship's failure mode is *catastrophic clarification*. If Mrs. Lee ever learns the full picture — that her son has spent his adolescence as the civilian operational support for a costumed minor adjacent to repeated lethal incidents at his school — the rupture would not be in love but in *placement*. She would pull him out of Brooklyn Visions. She would relocate him. She would, with the absolute moral authority of a parent who has been deceived for years in the interest of her child's life, end the configuration that defines Ganke's existence. Ganke knows this. It is the actual stake of his secret-keeping, larger than any of the public stakes he articulates.

**Leverage profile.** She is the single highest-leverage point on Ganke's entire threat surface. An adversary who wished to neutralize Ganke as a node in Miles's support network would not need to threaten Ganke; they would need only to deliver a credible information packet to his mother. The relationship has not been exploited this way in canon. It remains the open vulnerability.

---

### 2. FATHER — MR. LEE

**Name / canonical depiction.** Unnamed. Even more sparsely depicted than the mother; appears almost exclusively as a referent in Ganke's speech ("my dad," "my parents").

**History and dynamic.** The father reads, on the available behavioral evidence, as the *delegating* parent — present in Ganke's life through provision and through occasional remote intervention, but operationally distant from day-to-day parenting, which has been ceded first to the mother and then to the institution (BVA). The file infers a professional-class occupation requiring significant working hours; the household's ability to afford a private boarding-school placement supports this. He is not absent in the wounding sense; he is absent in the *scheduled* sense.

**Mode of paternal presence.** When the father registers in Ganke's behavior, it is typically as the source of two things: (i) a particular kind of dry humor that Ganke has clearly inherited and refined — the deflective, observational, pop-culture-cross-referenced register that is his primary defensive style appears to originate, on internal evidence, in a paternal model — and (ii) a baseline of *unspoken-expectation pressure* around academic and professional trajectory. Ganke's near-religious attendance to his coursework, his refusal to let the Spider-Man-adjacent chaos compromise his grades, his quiet preservation of college-track positioning — these are not exclusively maternal pressures. They are paternal pressures internalized as default settings.

**Trust and safety.** Trust is structural and not intimate. Ganke does not, on any panel in the record, *confide* in his father. He does not, however, appear to *fear* his father the way he fears triggering his mother's intervention. The father reads as the parent who would, if informed of the Spider-Man situation, likely respond with a long silence, a single clarifying question, and a decision deferred to the mother. He is not the disciplinary authority in the household's emotional architecture; he is the *ratifier* of decisions made by the disciplinary authority. This makes him both safer to be near and harder to actually know.

**Evolution.** The paternal relationship has, if anything, *receded* over the publication arc. Earlier runs included occasional parental phone calls and references; later runs have largely elided the father. This may reflect the natural longitudinal pattern of an adolescent boy at boarding school whose father-contact reduces as autonomy expands — a normative developmental drift that the writers have, intentionally or not, captured.

**Failure mode.** The father-relationship's failure mode is *silent withdrawal of investment*. Were Ganke to materially disappoint paternal expectations — academic failure, criminal entanglement, a public scandal — the consequence would not be confrontation but a cooling of the relational temperature that Ganke would feel keenly precisely because the baseline is already cool. The father has limited *active* warmth to withdraw, but he has substantial *background* warmth (provision, protection, presumed pride), and its diminishment would constitute a serious blow to Ganke's psychological economy.

**Leverage profile.** Lower than the mother. An adversary seeking to coerce Ganke through paternal channels would have difficulty: the father is harder to alarm, slower to act, and more likely to defer to deliberation than to immediate intervention. He is the more procedurally robust of the two parents and the harder to weaponize.

---

### 3. SIBLINGS — STATUS: UNCONFIRMED / EFFECTIVELY ABSENT

**Canonical status.** No sibling has been canonized in any sustained way in the published record. The file flags this as remarkable: most supporting characters in modern superhero fiction accrue at least passing familial detail across a decade of appearances. Ganke has not.

**Inferential reading.** The behavioral evidence is consistent with an only-child profile, though it does not foreclose the possibility of an older sibling already launched (in college, in early career) and therefore not co-resident in Ganke's developmental orbit during the publication window. The markers of only-childness: comfort with adult conversation, ease in solo recreational activity (LEGO, gaming, building), absence of the territoriality or comparative-status behavior that sibling-raised children typically display, and the particular *adopted-sibling* intensity of his bond with Miles — Ganke treats Miles with the somewhat-overdetermined investment of a child who has not previously had a peer-rank intimate in the home environment and has decided, with the absolute commitment of the first-time-experiencing, that this is his person.

**If a sibling exists** in canon yet to be revealed: the file predicts an older sister, professional-track, geographically distant, with whom Ganke maintains warm but infrequent contact and whose existence functions as a model of the trajectory his parents expect of him. This is inferential and flagged as such.

**Operational implication.** The sibling-shaped absence in Ganke's life is one of the structural reasons the Miles bond carries the weight it does. He has built into Miles a relational slot that, in a different family configuration, would have been distributed across blood-kin peers. The intensity of the friendship is partly the intensity of a singular investment that has no parallel channels.

---

### 4. THE MORALES HOUSEHOLD AS FUNCTIONAL FAMILY — JEFFERSON, RIO, BILLIE
