This subsection is included under Family & Origin Bonds rather than under social relationships because the behavioral record substantiates it: **the Morales household functions, in the time-on-panel and emotional-bandwidth sense, as Ganke's secondary family of origin during his adolescence.** He is at their kitchen table more often than at his own parents'. He is known to Rio and Jefferson by sight, by voice, by snack preference. He has been folded into the household's rhythms in the way that the close friends of a son become quasi-family in households of a particular warm-immigrant-domestic register, which the Moraleses model strongly.

**Jefferson Morales (Davis).** The relationship is correct, mildly amused, supervisory. Jefferson — a former criminal, a current law-enforcement-adjacent figure depending on era, and consistently a man of high observational competence — *clocks* Ganke. He has, on internal evidence, almost certainly intuited that Ganke knows more about Miles's irregular hours than Ganke admits. He has not pressed. The dynamic between them is therefore an unspoken understanding: Jefferson treats Ganke with the courteous distance one extends to a witness one has decided not to interrogate. Ganke, for his part, is *afraid* of Jefferson in the particular way adolescent boys are afraid of fathers-not-their-own who they suspect see through them. He behaves impeccably in Jefferson's presence — fewer jokes, straighter posture, more "sir" or its functional equivalent.

**Rio Morales.** The warm relationship. Rio reads Ganke as a son's-best-friend in the classical sense and treats him with the inclusive Latina-maternal warmth that the character is consistently written with — feeding him, asking after his parents, expressing concern about his sleep. Ganke responds with what reads as genuine, unforced affection: he eats what she offers, he asks after her in turn, he has clearly absorbed enough of the household's domestic language to function fluently inside it. The Rio bond is the closest Ganke comes to a proximal maternal presence in his daily life, and the file infers that some portion of the emotional labor that would, in a non-boarding-school configuration, be performed by his own mother has been quietly absorbed by Rio without anyone explicitly naming it.

**Billie Morales (younger sister to Miles).** Ganke registers as the goofy older-brother-adjacent figure. He plays with her in the casual way of a sibling-not-quite, with the patient amusement of an only child who finds small children genuinely interesting rather than wearying. The bond is light and uncomplicated.

**Trust profile within the Morales household.** Ganke is trusted by the Moraleses as a positive influence on Miles, a steadying academic peer, a known-quantity friend. He is *not* trusted with the secret of Spider-Man — they do not know that he knows. This is the household's structural blindspot, and Ganke's quiet management of it (never letting slip in Rio's presence, never accidentally referencing operational details in Jefferson's earshot) is one of the most underappreciated demonstrations of his behavioral discipline in the entire record.

**Failure mode.** If the Moraleses learned that Ganke had known about Miles's identity from the beginning and never told them — through the years of their fear, their grief over Miles's near-deaths, their interventions and confrontations with their own son — the rupture would be substantial. Rio would be wounded more than angry; Jefferson would be angry more than wounded. The relationship is recoverable but would be marked. Ganke's continued welcome in the household is contingent on a deception that, if ever surfaced, would re-frame years of warm hospitality as the household having been operationally penetrated by a minor co-conspirator. He carries this knowledge. It is part of his load.

**Leverage profile.** An adversary informing the Moraleses of Ganke's role would not directly harm Ganke physically, but it would *socially expel* him from the household that has functioned as his secondary family. This is a non-trivial threat and forms a secondary leverage axis paralleling the parental one.

---

### 5. THE DEAD

**No documented deceased family.** No grandparent, parent, sibling, or kin death is in the published record. This absence — like the sparse presence of the living kin — is structural rather than incidental.

**The inferential dead.** Standard demographic priors suggest at least some grandparental loss in the background of an adolescent of Ganke's age, particularly if any grandparent remained in Korea where Ganke's exposure to their daily life and death would be mediated through parental report. The file notes that Ganke has shown no grief-behavior on panel that would mark a recent or formative loss; the somatic baseline (light affect, intact humor, no avoidance of mortality-themed conversation) is consistent with a young person who has not yet been close-hand bereaved.

**The proximate dead in his ecosystem.** Ganke's life has been adjacent to substantial death — villains, civilians caught in incidents at or near Brooklyn Visions, the universe-scale losses of *Secret Wars* (which he survived through integration into the prime continuity without on-panel grief-processing of what was lost). His apparent equanimity about these losses is *not* callousness. It is the cognitive-emotional firewall of someone whose proximity to extraordinary events has required developing the capacity to compartmentalize losses that are not directly his. This firewall is one of his significant adaptive achievements and one of his significant latent costs. If it ever fails — if a death lands too close, in the wrong shape, at the wrong moment — the backlog of un-grieved adjacency may surface at unpredictable scale.

**The death that would break the configuration.** The clearest hypothetical: Miles. The death of Miles Morales would not produce in Ganke the publicly performative grief of a romantic partner or a parent, but it would dismantle the architecture his adolescence has been built around. He has organized his identity, his secret-keeping load, his secondary-family attachment to the Moraleses, his after-school hours, his developmental milestones, his sense of being-in-a-story — all of it — around proximity to Miles. The file's prediction is that Ganke would survive such a loss outwardly intact and would deteriorate inwardly over a longer arc than would be evident to observers. He would joke at the funeral. He would help Rio cook the post-funeral meal. He would, in private, build something out of LEGO and not finish it.

---

### SYNTHESIS — Family & Origin Bonds

Ganke Lee's family-of-origin map is characterized by **a distant-loving biological family operating in delegated-care mode**, **a proximal functional family in the Moraleses absorbing the daily-warmth functions**, **a structural absence of siblings producing singular investment in chosen-kin (Miles)**, and **no formative bereavement on record**, with the resulting profile of an adolescent who is *securely loved at distance, warmly received at proximity, and structurally alone with the largest secret of his life across every familial channel he has*.

His parents do not know what he carries. The Moraleses do not know that he knows. There is no sibling to whom he could decompress. There is no deceased loved one whose memory functions as an internal confidant. The architecture of his family bonds is, on close inspection, the architecture of a young man whose primary load has no authorized recipient in any room he was born into or grew up beside. This is the load-bearing absence under the load-bearing humor. It is the family-shaped reason the secret leaks when it leaks — not because his bonds are weak, but because none of them are *positioned* to take the weight, and the weight has to go somewhere.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

A dossier section on Ganke Lee's lateral and vertical bonds outside the family-of-origin. The defining structural fact: Ganke's relational universe is **organized concentrically around Miles Morales**. Every figure in this section is, in some measure, a person Ganke met through Miles, met because of Miles, or met in a context (BVA, the post-disclosure hero-adjacent social ecology) where Miles is the central organizing presence. This is itself a datum — Ganke has not, in a decade-plus of publication, been depicted forming a primary relationship with a person wholly outside the Miles-orbit. He is a relational satellite to a relational planet, and his sky has no other suns.

---

## 1. MILES MORALES — Primary Bond, Co-Author of Identity

**Origin (BVA, pre-bite).** Subject and Miles were assigned as dormmates at Brooklyn Visions Academy in the fall preceding the bite incident (*Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011) #1–2). The pre-disclosure baseline matters: for a measurable interval — weeks, in narrative time — they were ordinary roommates. Ganke's affection for Miles predates Miles's powers. This is the foundation on which everything later structurally rests: Ganke chose Miles before Miles was extraordinary, which means Ganke's loyalty is *not* contingent on the extraordinary.

**The Disclosure (*USM* #2–4).** When Miles returned to the dorm after the bite, displaying powers, Ganke's response was — and this is the single most diagnostic event in his entire publication record — *not fear, not disbelief, not self-protective distance*. It was delight, problem-solving curiosity, and immediate identity-conferral: *you should be a hero, here is the costume, here is the plan*. Within a single conversation Ganke triaged the novel situation, mapped it onto a genre template, generated an action plan, and assigned Miles a role. He effectively *named* Miles as Spider-Man before Miles named himself. This is co-authorship of identity, not friendship-as-accessory.

**Dynamic — operational.** Across all subsequent appearances Ganke functions as:
- **Information node.** News monitor, comms, research, threat-assessment.
- **Alibi factory.** He fabricates and maintains the social cover that keeps Miles's parents, BVA staff, and peers from triangulating his absences. This includes call-and-text scripts, fake homework collabs, fabricated illness, fake noise from the dorm room when Miles is out.
- **Costume and gear consultant.** He is the originator of the costume idea and a continuing contributor to suit/tech discussion.
- **Emotional first-responder.** When Miles returns from a patrol shaken, Ganke's protocol is: snack, joke, listen, only-then-advise. The sequence is stable across writers.

**Dynamic — affective.** Their bond reads as *fraternal-domestic*. They eat in the same bed, talk through walls, sleep in the same room, share screens. The intimacy is the unspectacular intimacy of long cohabitation. There is no romantic charge; there is no rivalry. There is the rare and specific bond of two people who learned how to be young together in a shared 12-by-15 room.

**Evolution.** Three phases:
- *USM phase (2011–2015):* nearly symbiotic; Ganke is Miles's only confidant; the relationship is the spine of Miles's hero-life.
- *Bendis 616 phase (2016–2018):* Ganke broadens (Bombshell, expanded peer group) but remains primary node; his role formalizes as "guy in the chair."
- *Ahmed/Ziglar phase (2018–present):* Miles's social and heroic worlds expand dramatically (Starling, Shift, Billie, Barbara, the broader Web of Spider-People); Ganke is *backgrounded but not displaced*. He occupies less panel time and the same emotional position.

**Trust / safety.** Mutual trust is asymptotic to total. Miles tells Ganke things he tells no one else, including (across runs) his mother, his girlfriends, and his fellow heroes. Ganke tells Miles his crushes, his anxieties (when he names them at all), his hobbies. The safety is unconditional in the sense that neither has ever, on panel, weaponized intimate knowledge of the other.

**Failure mode.** *Leakage.* The disclosure-compulsion is *specifically* a Miles-relationship failure: it has never been Ganke betraying a peer's secret; it has been Ganke unable to hold Miles's secret alone. The pattern began in *USM* #6–10 (telling Judge) and has recurred in attenuated forms whenever the cognitive-affective load of the secret has spiked above his containment capacity. The failure is not malice or carelessness; it is the regulatory overflow of a node carrying too much information with no authorized downstream.

**Leverage.** Anyone who could threaten Miles, Miles's family, or — interestingly — Ganke's own family by way of Miles, could obtain near-total cooperation from Ganke. He is also leverageable by Miles himself: a sufficiently clear, sufficiently kind request from Miles produces compliance even when Ganke disagrees. He has not been depicted refusing Miles anything material.

---

## 2. JUDGE ("Judge") — The First Breach, The Lost Friend

**Origin (*USM* (2011) #1, pre-bite).** Judge was the *third* member of the BVA roommate-adjacent friendship triad: Miles, Ganke, Judge. The pre-disclosure friendship was apparently coequal — three boys, one dorm wing, ordinary-teenager adjacency.

**The breach (*USM* #6–10).** Ganke, under the weight of the secret and operating on a logic of *we need help / Judge is one of us / this is too much to carry*, told Judge that Miles was Spider-Man. Judge's response was not the affirming co-conspiracy Ganke had projected; Judge reacted with discomfort, distance, and an inability to integrate the information. Miles, on discovering the leak, was hurt — at both of them, but the structural rupture was with Ganke.

**Dynamic — what this reveals about Ganke.** He had assumed the disclosure framework that had worked with him would replicate with Judge. This is a critical cognitive signature: Ganke projects his own affective architecture onto others. He assumed Judge would receive the secret the way Ganke himself had received it — with delight, with loyalty, with immediate problem-solving. The misjudgment was not strategic incompetence; it was an empathic short-circuit, a *typical-mind fallacy* applied to a friend.

**Evolution.** Judge fades from the publication record after this arc. He is not retconned, not redeemed, not reintegrated into the inner circle in any substantial way through subsequent runs. He is, in effect, the *casualty of Ganke's failure mode* — the friend lost as the price of the lesson Ganke needed to learn (and has only partly learned) about secret-keeping.

**Trust / safety.** Severed. Ganke and Judge are not on panel as confidants again.

**Failure mode (Ganke's, here).** The same leakage pattern, in its inaugural form.

**Leverage.** None operative; Judge has not been deployed as a threat vector or reapproach point in subsequent canon. But the *latent* leverage is significant: a writer or adversary who reanimated Judge could obtain testimony of the early disclosure pattern that would unsettle Miles's current trust.

---

## 3. LANA BAUMGARTNER ("BOMBSHELL") — The Romantic Disequilibrium

**Origin (*Spider-Man* (2016)).** Bombshell, a former low-tier villain with a complicated criminal past, becomes adjacent to Miles's world via a string of plot intersections. Ganke develops a crush on her that is — by his own admission and by depicted behavior — disproportionate, immediate, and uncharacteristic of his usual measured affect.

**Dynamic.** Anxious-eager; verbally fumbling in a way he is not in any other relational context. With Miles he is fluent; with Bombshell he is *interrupted-by-himself*. He overtalks, mis-times jokes, overthinks gestures. His usual cognitive-template machinery (genre conventions, pop-culture analog) misfires because the genre template for "best friend gets girlfriend" doesn't account for the girlfriend being a reformed criminal who outranks him in lived experience by an order of magnitude.

**What this reveals.** Two things. First, Ganke's *type* — to the extent he has one — is the structurally inappropriate match. Bombshell is older-feeling, harder, more outlaw-adjacent than anyone in his ordinary social ecology. This indicates a counter-conformist substrate beneath his rule-following exterior, a quiet attraction to risk that he does not otherwise express. Second, his defenses thin most visibly in the pursuit of *being chosen by someone independent of Miles*. The Bombshell subplot is the one extant context in which we see Ganke want something for himself, separate from the support role.

**Evolution.** The romantic plotline is treated comedically and is not durably consummated into a stable relationship in canon. It surfaces, fades, surfaces. The unresolved quality is its own datum — Ganke does not (yet) get the thing he wants for himself.

**Trust / safety.** Functional but not deep. Bombshell tolerates and is fond of him without (depicted) reciprocal investment of the magnitude he extends.

**Failure mode.** Self-interruption, over-performance, and a tendency to convert genuine vulnerability into joke before it can land. He cannot, in her presence, sustain the unguarded register he sustains effortlessly with Miles.

**Leverage.** Significant. Threats to or through Bombshell would produce uncharacteristic action from Ganke — potentially including violations of operational secrecy he would not commit for less.

---

## 4. BARBARA RODRIGUEZ — The Negotiated Peace

**Origin (*Miles Morales: Spider-Man* (2018) onward).** Barbara enters Miles's life as a romantic partner during the Ahmed run. Ganke's relationship with her is, in dossier terms, the most diagnostically *negative-space* relationship in the file: it tells us what Ganke is not.

**Dynamic.** Ganke does not become jealous. He does not compete for Miles's time. He does not subtly undermine, ironize, or gatekeep. He extends to Barbara the same wide-circle hospitality he extends to everyone Miles cares about. He shifts from "primary confidant in all matters" to "primary confidant in the matters Barbara is not yet read into," without visible distress at the demotion.

**What this reveals.** The absence of jealousy in a teenage best-friend role displaced by a girlfriend is *clinically* unusual. Most adolescents in his position generate at least subclinical resentment subroutines. Ganke does not. This substantiates the secure-attachment read in the psychological workup: he can tolerate the primary bond being non-exclusive because the bond is not, for him, predicated on exclusivity.

**Evolution.** Their relationship stabilizes as cordial-collegial; she is family-of-Miles, therefore family-of-his.

**Trust / safety.** Moderate-to-high; the trust is mediated by Miles, not direct.

**Failure mode.** Latent — if Barbara were to ask him to keep a secret *from* Miles, his protocols are not tested for that case and would likely fail in Miles's favor.

**Leverage.** Through Miles, primarily, not directly through Barbara.

---

## 5. THE EXPANDED HERO-PEER CIRCLE — Starling, Shift, Billie Morales (adjacent)

**Tiffany "Starling" Toomes, Lonnie "Shift" Lincoln.** These figures enter Miles's life as peer-heroes during the Ahmed/Ziglar era. Ganke's relationship with each is functionally similar: he is *briefed in*, he is *useful when needed*, he is *not central*. He treats them with the same wide-circle warmth he extends to Barbara. With Shift in particular — a figure with a charged family-name and a complex past — Ganke shows no visible suspicion or social-policing impulse; he reads the situation in front of him rather than the genealogy.

**Billie Morales.** Miles's infant sister; Ganke functions as a peripheral uncle-figure, present when family scenes include him. He treats Billie with unaffected fondness. This datum is small but real: Ganke's warmth extends pre-verbally; it is not contingent on being recognized.

**Dynamic across this cluster.** Ganke's mode here is *node-adjacent-to-node*. He is in the network without being a hub of it. He shows no ambition to be more central than he is, and no resentment at being less central than he could be.

**Trust / safety.** Operational trust; affective trust is real but not deep. They would, on present evidence, take a bullet for him in the abstract; they would not (and could not) be his designated confidant.

**Failure mode.** *Invisibility under pressure.* In a sufficiently dense plot, this cluster forgets to check on Ganke. He is structurally vulnerable to being left out of the inner circle's crisis response when the crisis is about him. There is no evidence on the record that any of them has *ever* asked Ganke how he is doing carrying the secret.

**Leverage.** Low individually; high collectively, in that an adversary who positioned Ganke as bait for this group would obtain significant response.

---

## 6. PETER PARKER — The Mentor at One Remove

**Origin.** Peter enters Miles's life as the predecessor-Spider-Man and intermittent mentor across multiple runs (*Spider-Men*, *Spider-Men II*, the post-*Secret Wars* integration). Ganke knows of Peter; Ganke has been on panel with Peter; Ganke is read in.

**Dynamic.** Ganke's relationship to Peter is *worshipful-fan-of-the-myth, casual-in-the-room*. He has consumed Spider-Man as cultural object since before knowing Miles, and meeting Peter activates the genre-literate fan-affect register. In person, however, his usual social fluency holds; he does not freeze. He treats Peter as senior peer rather than as deity.

**What this reveals.** Ganke can integrate his cognitive template ("Spider-Man is a story I know") with the real person ("this is a tired adult man who has lived this") without significant cognitive friction. This is mature cognitive flexibility.

**Trust / safety.** Functional; mediated by Miles. Ganke has never sought Peter as a personal confidant, though Peter is structurally the *one person in the universe* who could meaningfully share Ganke's specific load — being the civilian-adjacent intimate of a Spider-Man. This is a *missed mentorship*. Peter, in the cases where he and Ganke share panel time, has not asked Ganke about Ganke's experience of the role.

**Failure mode.** The unrealized configuration. Ganke does not seek what he most needs; Peter does not offer what he is uniquely positioned to give. The mutual non-recognition is one of the quietest losses in the file.

**Leverage.** Through Miles, primarily.

---

## 7. JEFFERSON DAVIS & RIO MORALES — The Borrowed Parents

**Origin.** Miles's parents. Ganke is integrated into the Morales household as a fixture from the earliest *USM* arcs onward — present at meals, at holidays, at hospital scenes, at family crises.

**Dynamic.** Rio treats Ganke as a second son with measurable warmth — feeds him, includes him, addresses him directly. Jefferson, more reserved, extends a comparable if less verbalized inclusion. Ganke, for his part, performs the role of *the good friend the parents like*: respectful, polite, verbose-but-not-cloying, helpful in small domestic ways, available for the social functions of being a son's best friend (vouching, alibis — though the alibis are, of course, false in service of Miles's secret).

**What this reveals.** Ganke maintains an ethically vexed posture toward the Morales parents: he loves them, he is loved by them, *and he lies to them continuously*. The lying is in service of Miles's autonomy and safety, but it is sustained, layered, and high-stakes. He metabolizes this without depicted moral distress — another datum on the resilience side of the ledger, and a small one on the avoidance-of-self-interrogation side.

**Trust / safety.** High but asymmetric. The parents trust him completely; he holds back from them the single most consequential fact in their son's life.

**Failure mode.** A direct, sincere, unanswerable question from Rio — *is Miles safe? are you telling me the truth?* — is the scenario in which Ganke's defenses are least rehearsed. He has not been depicted breaking under such a question. He has also not been depicted truly receiving one.

**Leverage.** Massive. Any adversary who positioned Ganke between Miles's secret and the Morales parents' welfare would obtain near-total compliance.

---

## 8. BROOKLYN VISIONS ACADEMY — The Institutional Allies

**Faculty and administration.** Ganke's relationship to BVA's institutional structure is *good-student in good standing*. He is not a disciplinary case; he is not academically struggling; he is not on any administrative radar. This near-invisibility is itself the achievement — it is the cover that permits him to function as Miles's logistics arm. He performs ordinary studenthood with sufficient competence that no one asks the second question.

**Peer ecology.** Ganke is broadly liked, has multiple casual friendships outside the Miles-circle (referenced but not deeply depicted), and operates as a low-status-but-socially-fluent figure in the BVA social ecology. He is not popular; he is not bullied; he is *known*. This is the optimal location for a clandestine support operator.

**Trust / safety.** Functional, surface-level. He has no deep BVA relationships outside the Miles-circle.

**Failure mode.** Should institutional attention turn on him — an investigation, a formal questioning, a teacher who notices the patterns — he has no rehearsed protocols and no institutional ally to fall back on.

**Leverage.** Modest. Threats to his academic standing or to his BVA enrollment would distress him; they would not turn him.

---

## 9. THE ABSENT MENTOR — A Structural Vacancy

The file must name what is *not* in it. **Ganke has no mentor of his own.** No adult in his published life occupies the role for him that Peter occupies (intermittently) for Miles, or that Aaron — for ill — occupied. No teacher has been depicted recognizing him as a particular kind of mind. No older relative outside the unmapped family-of-origin has been shown taking him under wing. No hero-adjacent adult (Peter, Jessica Drew, anyone) has positioned themselves as his guide.

The structural consequence: *the load-bearing humor bears alone*. The information-dispersal failure mode predicted in the psychological workup is, in significant part, a function of this vacancy. A confidant of his own — an adult who knew the secret and could receive his processing of it — would resolve the single largest latent fault line in his psychology. No such figure has been written in.

**This is the file's central recommendation for understanding the subject's trajectory.** Every other relationship in this section is, in some way, sufficient. The unfilled one is the one that matters most.

---

## SYNTHESIS

Ganke Lee's relational architecture is **wide, warm, well-distributed, and topologically dependent on a single primary edge** — the Miles-edge. He does friendship in the way he does LEGO: many small, well-chosen pieces, patiently assembled, structurally interlocking, with one keystone brick whose removal would collapse the figure. He is generous with affection across the network, secure enough in the primary bond to share it without contraction, ethically compromised in steady-state by the lies he tells the parents who love him, and *unmentored* in a way no other supporting figure in his immediate cohort is unmentored.

His allies are his because Miles is his. His chosen family is the Morales family by adoption. His mentor is the one chair in the room that has never been filled. The day someone — Peter, Rio if she ever learns the truth and forgives him, an as-yet-unwritten adult — sits in that chair and asks Ganke how *he* is doing, the file predicts a long exhale that has been held since *USM* (2011) #2.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

## Preamble: The Shape of the Category for This Subject

A standard intelligence file at this depth typically opens this section with a roster of operational adversaries and intimate partners running to the dozens. Subject GANKE LEE's roster is, by contrast, extraordinarily thin — and the thinness is itself the most important datum. Across more than a decade of continuous publication appearance (2011 through present-continuity), Subject has accumulated:

- **Zero personal enemies** in the operational/superhuman sense. He has been threatened collaterally, never targeted individually.
- **Two structural rivals**, both low-intensity, both ambient rather than declared.
- **One serious romantic-intimate attachment** (Lana Baumgartner / Bombshell), one earlier proto-romantic confusion (the Judge episode, more friendship-failure than romance), and a sustained pattern of *non-pursuit* that itself merits clinical attention.

The category, in other words, is structurally underpopulated relative to his proximity to a high-target principal. This is not accidental and not solely a function of writer-convention; it reflects an *interpersonal operating mode* in which Subject genuinely does not generate enemies — he absorbs friction through humor before it crystallizes into opposition — and in which his romantic appetite is real but bottlenecked by self-presentation anxieties documented elsewhere in this file. What follows is exhaustive on the persons present and explicit about the gaps.

---

## I. RIVALS

### 1. Judge (Devin "Judge" — early BVA cohort, *USM* 2011 #6–10 arc and recurring)

**History.** Judge enters the file as the third leg of the original Brooklyn Visions Academy social triad: Miles, Ganke, Judge. Pre-bite, the three are coequal — three boarding-school adolescents bonded by proximity, shared classes, and the leveling intimacy of dorm life. Judge predates the spider-bite event in Miles's life by weeks-to-months of continuous companionship. Subject's relationship with Judge is, in the pre-disclosure period, *uncomplicated friendship of the second rank* — closer than acquaintance, less central than the Miles bond.

**Dynamics — the rivalry that wasn't supposed to be.** The Judge-Ganke relationship transitions into rivalry the moment Subject discloses Miles's secret to him (*USM* 2011 #6–7). The disclosure is, from Subject's interior, an act of *inclusion* — Judge is in the friend-group, Judge deserves to know, sharing the load makes the load bearable. From Miles's exterior, it is a betrayal. From Judge's interior, it is a *promotion*: he has been let into the inner circle and given access to the most important fact in the room. The rivalry that develops is therefore asymmetric and largely unrecognized by Subject himself: Judge begins to compete, subtly, for proximity to Miles-as-Spider-Man — to be the *useful* friend, the *trusted* friend, the friend who proves himself worth the disclosure. Subject does not perceive a contest because Subject does not understand his bond with Miles as contestable. This is a documentable blind spot.

**Evolution.** The rivalry is short-lived in story-time because Judge largely exits the principal narrative within the same arc, but its residue is durable in Subject's behavioral record: every subsequent disclosure event (Bombshell learning, peer-group diffusion in *Spider-Man* 2016 #234-area) carries the structural imprint of the Judge episode. Subject has, observably, learned the *shape* of the failure without fully internalizing the *mechanism* — he continues to under-weight the political consequences of bringing a third party into a two-party secret.

**Trust / Safety.** Mutual non-hostility; functional zero. Neither party has weaponized the other. The relationship is dormant rather than ruptured.

**Failure mode.** Subject's failure mode with respect to Judge is *the original disclosure leak* — the prototypical instance of his recurring boundary-porousness around Miles's identity. Judge's failure mode (in the limited evidence available) is *receptivity without discretion* — he accepted the information without contesting whether he should have it. The two failure modes are complementary and reproducible.

**Leverage.** Judge holds, in principle, irrecoverable leverage over both Subject and Miles: knowledge of the secret identity, persisting across continuities to the extent the character persists. He has not exercised it. This is a *dormant leverage condition* — strategically the most dangerous kind, because it is undefended against and untracked by either holder.

---

### 2. Brooklyn Visions Academy Administrative Apparatus (institutional rival, ambient)

**History.** BVA functions in Subject's file as a *standing institutional adversary* in the soft sense: a system of rules (curfew, room inspections, attendance, behavioral codes) that Subject's role as Miles's cover-fabricator places him in chronic, low-grade violation of. From *USM* 2011 onward and continuously through the Bendis and Ahmed runs, Subject is the operational author of an ongoing program of small institutional deceptions: signing Miles in for class he is not at, fabricating illness, intercepting dorm checks, redirecting RA inquiries.

**Dynamics.** The institution does not know it has a rival; Subject does not consciously frame it as such. But the *cognitive load* of running a sustained low-grade deception operation against a competent residential institution is non-trivial, and the institution's investigative pressure — periodic, ambient, never resolved — is one of the principal continuous stressors on Subject's nervous system.

**Evolution.** Stable. Subject has not been caught in any documented terminal way. The deception apparatus has matured (he is better at it in 2018+ than in 2011) without ever being formalized or interrogated by him.

**Trust / Safety.** Subject's relationship to institutional authority is *compliant on surface, evasive in substance*. He performs the good student because he largely is one academically, which buys him cover for the operational deceptions. He is not anti-authoritarian; he is *selectively authoritarian-adjacent in service of a higher loyalty*.

**Failure mode.** Documentation trail. Subject communicates extensively by text, by laptop, by digital channel; the surveillance footprint of his Miles-coverage is enormous and, in principle, recoverable by anyone with administrative access to BVA's networks. He does not appear to operate with operational-security discipline. He is a civilian running a years-long counter-institutional information operation on consumer-grade tools.

**Leverage.** The institution, were it ever to catch up, holds expulsion-level leverage over Subject — and through him, over the integrity of Miles's secret. This vector has never been seriously stress-tested in canon.

---

### 3. Latent Peer Rivalry — the Expanded Hero-Adjacent Circle (Starling, Shift, Barbara Rodriguez, Billie)

**History.** Through the Ahmed run (2018–2022) and into Ziglar, Miles's social and operational world widens substantially. Each new entrant — Starling as hero-peer, Shift as adopted-brother figure, Barbara Rodriguez as romantic partner, Billie as actual sibling — represents a potential displacement of Subject from his structural niche as Miles's primary confidant.

**Dynamics.** Subject does not enter rivalry with any of these figures. This is, given baseline human and especially adolescent psychology, *anomalous*. Most "best friend" archetypes in this position generate at least one observable jealousy event per new entrant; Subject generates none on panel. He greets Barbara warmly. He treats Shift as additional family. He does not compete with Starling for hero-adjacent proximity.

**Evolution.** Subject's role narrows in proportion to the circle's expansion — he becomes one node among several rather than the singular confidant — and he absorbs the narrowing without protest or retaliation.

**Trust / Safety.** High in all directions; no documented friction.

**Failure mode.** The absence of overt rivalry is, paradoxically, a forward-looking risk. Subject is metabolizing displacement *without expressing it*, which means there is no pressure-release on whatever residual anxiety the displacement generates. His humor and his sublimation activities (LEGO, tech) likely absorb it; the question of what happens when they stop absorbing it is unanswered.

**Leverage.** None of these figures hold leverage on Subject. The reverse is also true. The cluster is *non-leveraged* — which is rare and a credit to Subject's interpersonal mode.

---

## II. ENEMIES

### 1. The Null Set, with Footnote

**There are no personal enemies in Subject's file.** This is the headline finding and it bears repeating, because in a category that for most files in this proximity runs to dozens of named adversaries, Subject has accumulated zero. He has been threatened collaterally — present during home invasions of Miles's apartment, present during super-incidents at BVA, present when various antagonists have targeted Miles's known associates — but he has never been *individually* selected for adversarial attention by a competent threat actor.

**Why this is significant.** Subject possesses what is arguably the single most valuable piece of intelligence in his city: the civilian identity of a major super-operative. He is unprotected, unenhanced, predictable in location (dorm room), and accessible. He is a soft, high-value target by every metric of operational threat assessment. He has never been taken. He has rarely been seriously menaced. The intelligence-community read of this pattern would be one of two things: (a) he is genuinely off the threat-actor radar, which implies that Miles's identity-protection has held more robustly than any of his interpersonal choices would predict; or (b) he has been assessed by threat actors and *deprioritized* — perhaps because his role as a civilian non-combatant places him under norms that even villainous actors largely respect, perhaps because the operational cost of compromising him is higher than the intelligence yield.

**Subject's own threat-awareness.** Low and stable. He does not vary his routine. He does not screen visitors. He does not maintain operational security on his communications. He responds to acute threats when they arrive but does not prepare for them. This is consonant with the *genre-literate optimism* documented in his personality profile: he operates on the implicit premise that the story will not single him out, and so far the story has not. This is not a defensible posture; it is a *fortunate* one.

**Footnote — collateral exposures of record.** Subject has been in proximity to: the Roxxon corporate apparatus during multiple Miles-adjacent incidents; the Assessor and various Ahmed-run antagonists; the broader rogues' gallery during *Spider-Geddon* and *Clone Saga*–adjacent events. In none of these has he been individually targeted, named, surveilled-on-panel, or used as leverage against Miles. The collateral exposure record is extensive; the targeted-adversary record is empty.

---

## III. LOVERS & INTIMATES

### 1. Lana Baumgartner ("Bombshell") — *Spider-Man* (2016) #6 onward; primary romantic attachment of record

**History.** Lana Baumgartner enters Subject's life as a former minor-league villain rehabilitated into the Miles-adjacent civilian periphery. She is age-peer, working-class, brassy, verbal, and possesses powers (concussive blasts) that place her firmly in a category of person Subject has, until this point, only known through the mediation of Miles. The first meeting is in mixed company; Subject's interest is immediate, visible, and uncharacteristically *self-disclosing*. This is the only relationship in the file in which Subject's well-documented avoidance of personal vulnerability is overridden by appetitive motivation.

**Dynamics.** The relationship runs hot-and-fumbling rather than steady. Subject's mode of pursuit is *anxious-eager*: over-prepared verbal openings, deflective humor when she responds in kind, visible thrown-ness when she takes him seriously. Bombshell is not playing — her interest, when it surfaces, is genuine and direct, which is precisely the input Subject is least equipped to process. He is fluent in joking with women and rusty at being chosen by one. Their interactions in the 2016 run trace a pattern: he initiates with comedy, she responds with directness, he over-corrects toward sincerity, she meets him there, and then external plot (Miles's hero-life, her own complications) interrupts before the relationship can stabilize.

**Evolution.** The relationship plateaus rather than develops. By the Ahmed run, Bombshell is largely off-panel from Subject's life; the romance does not formally rupture so much as it is *attenuated by ambient circumstance*. The file does not record a breakup event. It records a fadeout. This is itself diagnostic — Subject did not consolidate the relationship when he had momentum, and the relationship's center of gravity drifted out of his orbit.

**Trust / Safety.** Mutual goodwill, asymmetric investment. Subject invests more than Bombshell. She has never weaponized the relationship, never threatened disclosure of what she has been told (she knows Miles's identity by inference if not direct disclosure), never used Subject instrumentally. The trust is *clean but light*.

**The pursuit-of-the-counter-conformist read.** Subject is, in every visible institutional context, a rule-follower: academically diligent, parentally compliant, socially safe. His one significant romantic pursuit is of a person with a criminal record, concussive powers, and a self-presentation that defies every category his upbringing would recognize. This is not coincidence. The Bombshell attraction is one of the few datapoints in the file pointing to a *suppressed counter-conformist register* in Subject's personality — a region of want that his daily presentation does not express. He is drawn to someone who lives openly the way he does not allow himself to live: loudly, transgressively, on her own terms. The romantic pursuit is, in part, a covert pursuit of a self he has not enacted.

**Failure mode.** Subject's failure mode with Bombshell is *insufficient escalation*. He brings the relationship to the threshold of becoming primary and does not cross it — partly because the plot does not let him, partly because his caretaker-default orientation toward Miles is structurally prior to any romantic pursuit. He will, every time, drop the romantic plot to take a call from his principal. Bombshell's failure mode is *availability drift*; her life moves and Subject does not move with it.

**Leverage.** Bombshell holds soft leverage: she knows enough about Subject's interior to hurt him if she chose, and enough about Miles to compromise the operation if she chose. She has done neither. The relationship is a *demonstrated trust without enforcement* — which is the strongest form trust can take.

---

### 2. The Judge Episode as Proto-Intimacy Failure (annotated)

It is worth noting, in the intimate-relationships category, that Subject's first major emotional rupture in the published record is *not* a romance — it is the Judge disclosure. The behavioral signature of that event is *intimacy-coded*: Subject shares the most important secret in his life with a person whose company he values, framed as drawing them closer, and is then surprised when the third party (Miles) experiences this as betrayal. The grammar is the grammar of romantic indiscretion — the sharing of privileged information as a gesture of bonding — displaced onto a friendship. It suggests that Subject's intimacy circuitry, at the time of the event, was not well-differentiated between friend-bonding and romance-bonding; both expressed as *information-sharing under affect*. This is developmentally age-appropriate (he was very young in the original *USM* sequence) and largely outgrown by the Bombshell period, but it remains a feature of his interpersonal style: he bonds by telling.

---

### 3. The Pattern of Non-Pursuit

Across roughly a decade of publication, Subject has *one* documented romantic pursuit. He is constantly socially present. He attends parties, school events, gatherings. He has opportunity. He does not act on it. The Bombshell pursuit is the exception that defines the rule.

**Read.** This is not asexuality or aromanticism — the Bombshell evidence is clear that romantic and presumably sexual appetite are present. It is *self-presentation anxiety married to caretaker default*. Subject does not believe, on the available evidence of his own behavior, that he is the kind of person who gets chosen — and his daily operating mode (in service of Miles) provides a continuous, legitimate, totally absorbing alternative to the work of being chosen. Caretaking is psychically cheaper than courtship. He has chosen the cheaper option, repeatedly, without framing it as a choice.

**Forward risk.** If Miles's life ever durably stops requiring Subject's caretaker function — graduation, geographic separation, Miles's marriage, the eventual normal attenuation of late-adolescent best-friendships into adult acquaintance — Subject loses his structural alternative to pursuing his own romantic life. The collapse of the caretaker role would expose the under-developed pursuit muscle. Whether he develops it on the timeline of the collapse, or whether the collapse precedes the development and leaves him in a period of loneliness, is the central forward-looking question in this category.

---

## IV. SYNTHESIS — THE CATEGORY AS DIAGNOSTIC

Subject's Rivals/Enemies/Lovers file is, at the population level, a portrait of a person who *does not generate friction* and who *does not pursue intimacy outside the bonded primary*. The enemy column is empty because his interpersonal mode does not crystallize opposition. The rival column is thin and largely unconscious — he is in rivalries he does not perceive and exits them without escalation. The lover column contains one real entry and a long pattern of non-pursuit.

The category's chief intelligence value is *negative*: the absence of enemies, despite catastrophic exposure, is the single most striking pattern in the file, and either reflects an unusually effective civilian camouflage or an unusually generous threat-actor environment, both of which are unstable conditions. The Bombshell relationship is the closest the file comes to documenting Subject as a person with appetite separate from his caretaker function, and it was not consolidated; the question of whether Subject can re-enter that register without external prompting is open.

The load-bearing humor holds. The romantic and adversarial worlds beyond Miles remain, by Subject's choice and circumstance, lightly populated. Both gaps are, in different ways, things to watch.


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Preamble: A Civilian in a Powered Ecosystem

Subject possesses no superhuman attribute. No bite, no serum, no exotic radiation, no inherited gene-line, no mystic patronage, no technological augmentation worn on the body. He is, in the strictest sense, the *control variable* in Miles Morales's social environment — the baseline human against which everyone else in the inner circle (a Spider, a former concussive-blast meta, a teleporter, a shapeshifter, an interdimensional traveler) is implicitly measured. The entire interest of this section, therefore, lies in mapping what an unaugmented adolescent has built — by talent, repetition, and necessity — into a functional support apparatus for a costumed operative. That apparatus is real. It is granular. It has signature, range, and failure mode. The dossier treats it as the operational toolkit of a *non-combatant intelligence asset embedded in a single-principal protective detail*, because functionally that is what it is.

---

## 1. Cognitive Substrate

The base layer beneath every other capability is a particular cognitive architecture: **fast associative pattern-matching coupled to a deep, indexed reservoir of narrative and systems templates.**

**Working memory and information throughput.** Subject reliably tracks multi-thread conversations involving real-time tactical updates from Miles in costume, ambient school/social context, and his own parallel research on a laptop or phone. He has been depicted in *Spider-Man* (2016) maintaining comms while simultaneously fielding a parent-phone-call cover story and continuing a separate text thread — a three-channel split that most adolescents would collapse into one. This is not meta-human bandwidth; it is *trained* bandwidth, the product of years of screen-mediated multitasking refined under operational pressure.

**Pattern-matching mode.** Subject thinks in templates. Presented with a novel situation, his first cognitive move is to retrieve the nearest analog from his reservoir — superhero comics convention, video-game logic, film-narrative structure, anime-trope, internet-meme cycle — and use it as a working hypothesis. The spider-bite disclosure event is the foundational example: confronted with a friend developing impossible abilities, he did not freeze, denial-respond, or recurse into disbelief. He triaged it inside one conversation by reaching for the *available template* ("you are now a superhero; you need a costume; here is the costume") and beginning execution. This is the same cognitive move a triage nurse makes — rapid categorization over rapid analysis.

**Limits of the template style.** The same move is his most reliable failure. Templates are summaries; reality is granular. When Miles's life departs from comics logic — when consequences metastasize in ways no genre convention prepares for — Ganke's first read is usually wrong, and he course-corrects only after observation overrides the template. The disclosure leak to Judge is partly this: in the template, the best friend's wider circle *should* know; in the actual life, that diffusion endangers a family. Genre-literate optimism is a worldview AND an analytical bias.

**Indexed retrieval.** What he knows, he knows accessibly. He does not appear to "search" memory; references arrive at conversational speed. This implies the underlying corpus is well-organized — likely the byproduct of his hobbyist activities (catalogued LEGO sets, structured fandoms, codebases with naming conventions), which are themselves rehearsals of indexing as a habit of mind.

---

## 2. Technical Competence

Subject's technical skillset is the most operationally consequential of his abilities. It is also, on the record, the most under-documented in its acquisition — he simply *is* competent at this, across writers, without origin story for the skill.

**Coding and software.** He scripts, modifies, and configures at a level sufficient to: build and maintain communications between himself and a costumed operative; spoof or alibi digital traces (school absence records, location data on parental check-in apps, social-media presence to suggest Miles was somewhere he was not); manage media-monitoring feeds (police scanner adjacent, news aggregator, civilian incident-report streams) in real time. Estimated skill level: **competent generalist hobbyist, not professional engineer.** He can stitch existing tools together and customize, not build novel systems from scratch. The signature is *bricolage* — clever recombination — rather than original architecture.

**Hardware.** Light. He manages devices rather than fabricates them. There is no indication he machines, solders at scale, or designs original circuitry. The contrast with peers in the broader Spider-canon (Ned Leeds–type fabricators, Peter Parker-type engineers) is deliberate to characterization: Ganke operates in the *software layer of the support role*, not the hardware layer.

**OPSEC discipline.** Mixed. Technically capable of operational security; behaviorally inconsistent at applying it to himself. He will scrub Miles's digital traces meticulously and then casually mention something compromising aloud in the dorm. The discipline is *project-bounded* — he is rigorous within a defined task and porous in the connective tissue between tasks.

**Growth curve.** Demonstrably present. Earliest *USM* (2011) depictions show him as a sharp kid with a laptop; by the Bendis 2016 run he is running structured comms; by the Ahmed run he is an assumed-competent quartermaster of Miles's civilian cover. He has not gained new categories of skill so much as **deepened existing ones into reliability under pressure** — a real form of growth, often underestimated.

---

## 3. Domain Expertise / Encyclopedic Knowledge

**Genre and pop-culture literacy.** Comprehensive across comics, film, anime, video games, internet culture, and adjacent fan ecosystems. Functions as a working reference library on demand. This is consequential in two ways: (i) it is the substrate for the template-thinking mode above; (ii) it is the *language* of his bond with Miles — the shared dialect through which they negotiate everything from tactical problems to emotional ones.

**Construction systems.** Deep expertise in LEGO as a system: piece nomenclature, set numbers, build sequences, modification tactics, market and rarity awareness. This is not a frivolous datum. The LEGO obsession is a *trained systems-thinking competency* — discrete components, assembly logic, error correction mid-build, satisfaction at structural closure. It generalizes. A mind that finds LEGO satisfying for the reasons Ganke does is a mind oriented toward modular problem decomposition.

**Limits.** He is not a polymath in the academic sense. There is no evidence of deep expertise in the sciences, languages beyond his apparent English/Korean range, classical history, finance, or other domains outside his hobby-cluster. His knowledge is *culturally fluent*, not *broadly scholarly*. He would lose a quiz bowl on chemistry; he would dominate one on superhero continuity.

---

## 4. Social and Interpersonal Skills

This is the under-discussed power-set, and arguably the most refined.

**Code-switching.** Demonstrated across registers: dorm-banter with Miles; deferential-competent with school administration; warm-with-managed-disclosure with Miles's parents (a relationship that requires *constant* low-grade deception while preserving genuine affection); fumbling-earnest with romantic interest; collegial with the wider hero-adjacent circle. The register shifts are clean and unforced, which signals a high degree of automaticity — he does not appear to consciously prepare these transitions.

**Cover-story fabrication.** Documented repeatedly. He generates plausible alibis on demand for Miles's absences. The signature of his cover stories is *low-spectacle plausibility* — boring, school-adjacent, mundane — which is correct tradecraft. Flashy lies attract scrutiny; tedious ones do not.

**Reading rooms.** Reads sarcasm, unspoken affect, and group dynamics with accuracy. This rules out the autism-spectrum reading (per the prior section) and establishes that his social engine is properly calibrated, not just hyperverbal.

**Limits.** His own self-disclosure capability is *atrophied or chosen-against*. He can read others but does not reciprocally project his own interior. Whether this is incapacity or strategy is unresolved in the canon; the effect, either way, is the same — he is socially powerful in the outward direction and socially opaque in the inward one.

---

## 5. Humor as Functional Capability

Worth isolating because it operates at performance level beyond ordinary peer baseline.

**Mechanism.** Rapid associative retrieval (pop-culture template) plus accurate read of the moment's affective temperature plus willingness to absorb the social cost of a missed joke. The output is a near-continuous low-grade comedy line that performs three simultaneous functions: (i) regulates his own arousal under stress; (ii) regulates *Miles's* arousal under stress, which is the operationally critical function; (iii) maintains group cohesion by signaling that the situation is survivable.

**Signature applications.** The humor mode is most reliably deployed at moments of *high stakes adjacent to him but not impacting him directly* — Miles in danger, a hero conversation in his dorm room, a reveal moment. It thins in two situations: when he himself is the affective stakes (romantic vulnerability with Bombshell), and when physical intervention is required that he cannot provide.

**Limit.** It is a regulatory tool, not a tactical one. It changes the temperature of a room; it does not change the contents. Over-reliance has a known degradation curve — when the joke stops landing, it tends to *keep being deployed*, which is the diagnostic signature of humor-as-defense rather than humor-as-skill.

---

## 6. Operational Role: "Guy in the Chair"

The role is overtly named in the Bendis 2016 run as conscious nod to the broader contemporary Spider-mythos. In Ganke's hands it has the following observed components:

- **Comms node.** Maintains voice/text channel during Miles's operations when conditions allow.
- **Information triage.** Monitors news, scanner-adjacent feeds, and social media for incident reporting; surfaces relevant items.
- **Civilian cover.** Manages the school/parental layer — physical alibi, presence-suggestion in the dorm, intercept of administrative inquiry.
- **Tactical sounding board.** Miles thinks out loud at him; Ganke reflects, refines, occasionally redirects. Notably, Ganke does NOT typically generate the tactical plan — Miles leads, Ganke iterates.
- **Emotional decompression chamber.** Post-operation, Miles processes with him. This is the most consequential of the support functions, and the one most uniquely Ganke-specific; the tech functions could in principle be performed by other peers in the circle, but the *decompression* is bonded.

**Range of operation.** Strictly local. He works from the dorm, occasionally from the library or home. He has not been depicted as a field operative; he does not travel to incident sites; he does not provide overwatch from rooftops. His coverage is a single-room information-management cell, not a deployed unit.

**Latency profile.** Fast on familiar problems (cover stories, comms reconnect, reference retrieval). Slower on novel adversaries or situations outside the template library. Acceptable for the operational tempo Miles requires; would be inadequate for a higher-tier hero workload.

---

## 7. Physical Capability

Minimal and worth stating explicitly for the sake of completeness.

- No depicted athleticism. No combat training. No marksmanship. No driving on record.
- Manual dexterity sufficient for LEGO assembly and keyboard work; no indication of fine-motor exceptionalism.
- Stamina low; consistently shown horizontal at rest.
- No depicted self-defense capability of any kind. Were he ever to be physically targeted as leverage on Miles, he would be entirely dependent on outside intervention — a vulnerability the canon has, notably, never exploited.

The body is a non-resource. The mind is the entire toolkit.

---

## 8. Growth Over Time

Across the publication arc (2011 → present), three growth curves are visible:

**(a) Voice maturation.** Earliest depictions are middle-school silly; the voice now reads as recognizable late adolescent. Vocabulary and reference set have updated with him. Operating mode unchanged.

**(b) Operational reliability.** Earliest disclosure-leak behavior (telling Judge) has not been *eliminated* — see Ahmed-era diffusion of Miles's identity through his social circle — but the *quality* of cover-story work, comms-discipline, and tactical sounding-board contribution has tightened. He is more useful per unit of presence than he was in 2011.

**(c) Romantic and social independence.** Earliest version was almost entirely defined relative to Miles. Bombshell pursuit and his sustained academic/hobby life signal a slow gain of independent identity-mass. The growth is real but slow; he remains more *Miles-adjacent* than self-defined in canonical depiction.

**Not growing:** his self-disclosure aperture, his physical capability, the depth (versus breadth) of his technical skill, and the disclosure-leak fault.

---

## 9. Signature Applications

Three sequences canonically isolate his abilities at their most characteristic:

1. **The costume.** Identifying, sourcing, and assigning narrative meaning to the black Halloween Spider-suit. This is the signature *symbolic* intervention — he gave Miles a visual identity that has endured across continuities. The template-mind operating at peak: he saw the available object and recognized its mythic fit.
2. **The disclosure triage.** Receiving the spider-bite reveal and immediately operating as if the new reality were managed. The signature *cognitive* intervention — composure under categorical surprise.
3. **The cover-story routine.** Iterated across years, the ongoing low-grade alibi maintenance to parents and school. The signature *operational* intervention — patient, dull, effective, invisible when it works.

---

## 10. The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

The disclosure leak is not an isolated bug. It is the **inverse face of his single strongest skill** — affiliation-through-information-sharing. The same engine that makes him the best support node in Miles's circle (give him a fact, he integrates and deploys it usefully) is the engine that, under chronic load and without an authorized confidant of his own, *redistributes* facts he was instructed to retain.

Read structurally: every capability above runs on **information flow** as its medium. Pattern-matching needs input. Cover stories need shared knowledge. Comms need open channel. Humor needs reference exchange. The decompression-chamber function for Miles is literally an information-offload mechanism. Ganke's entire operational identity is built around being *the place information moves through.* Asking him to be the place information *stops* is asking the channel to be the dam. He can do it most of the time. The leaks are the system's predictable overpressure relief.

The symptom is the signature. The signature is the symptom. His powers and his pressure point are the same mechanism viewed from opposite sides — and any future writer interested in destabilizing him will need only to load the channel beyond its rated capacity and watch where it vents.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT: GANKE LEE

## Preface: Defining "Operations" for a Civilian Asset

Ganke Lee is not an operator in any conventional sense — no field deployments, no combat training, no agency affiliation, no offensive capability. But the subject *runs operations* nonetheless, and has done so continuously since approximately age thirteen. What he runs is a sustained civilian counter-intelligence cell of N=1, embedded inside a boarding-school dormitory, whose mission is the protection of a single asset's secret identity and the maintenance of that asset's operational tempo. Measured by uptime, mission-criticality, and consequence-of-failure, it is one of the longer-running unbroken support operations in his peer cohort's universe. Measured by tradecraft hygiene, it is uneven — competent in execution, porous in compartmentalization. This section maps how he actually *runs the desk*.

---

## 1. Decision-Making Architecture

**Primary cognitive mode: template-matching against a deep genre/systems library.** Ganke does not reason from first principles under time pressure; he reasons by retrieving the nearest analog from a vast internal index — comics, films, anime, video-game logic, science-fiction novels, LEGO instruction-set procedural reasoning, computer-science design patterns — and adapting. The retrieval is fast (sub-second on panel), the adaptation is iterative, and the failure mode is the well-known cost of pattern-matching: occasional false-positives where the template overrides the novel particulars of the situation. He has been observed multiple times to greet a genuinely unprecedented event with "okay, this is the part where —" and proceed to act on the template rather than on what is actually in front of him. This is corrected, when corrected, by Miles physically interrupting or by the situation refusing to conform.

**Decision speed.** Fast on tactical questions (what do we tell your mom, what story do we run, what build is the suit). Slow-to-stalled on strategic questions involving his own life trajectory — what he wants for himself outside the support role is consistently un-decided, deferred, joked around, or substituted with what is good for Miles. This asymmetry — high tactical decisiveness, low personal-strategic decisiveness — is one of the most stable features of his operational profile.

**Risk tolerance.** Asymmetric and counterintuitive. On Miles's behalf: conservative — pushes for plans, alibis, fallback positions, lower exposure. On his own behalf: notably *less* conservative — he tells Judge against orders, he pursues a former villain as a romantic interest, he commits low-level rule-breaking at BVA (after-hours laptop use, snack contraband, unauthorized comms) without significant deliberation. He treats his own skin as cheap and Miles's skin as expensive. This is consistent with the caretaker self-concept derived in the psychological workup.

**Authority response.** Compliant on the surface, routinely non-compliant in execution. He does not argue with rules; he routes around them. Resident advisors, teachers, Miles's parents Rio and Jefferson — Ganke maintains a faultless social interface with each while running an active deception layer underneath. He is, in tradecraft terms, a *cover-identity natural*: his presented self (cheerful, harmless, hobbyist, slightly goofy) is so coherent and so disarming that almost no adult in the record has ever subjected him to real scrutiny.

---

## 2. Operating Tempo and Daily Pattern

The dossier-relevant baseline week, reconstructed from cumulative depiction:

- **Pre-dawn / late-night window (roughly 23:00–02:00):** peak operational activity. Laptop open, headphones half-on, lights low. This is when Miles returns from patrol; this is when Ganke is awake to receive, debrief, and patch. Ganke's circadian rhythm has effectively been re-shaped to mirror a vigilante's. He compensates with caffeine and naps.
- **Morning class block:** functional but visibly under-slept; tells include slow blinking, propped-head posture, increased snacking in defiance of school policy.
- **Afternoon / between classes:** social maintenance — peer conversations, news-feed monitoring on phone, intermittent texts to Miles for location-check.
- **Evening dorm window (19:00–23:00):** the operational headquarters. Tech work, monitoring, building (LEGO or code), alibi-construction if Miles is out.
- **Weekends:** more elastic; longer stretches of recreational depth (full LEGO build sessions, gaming, deeper genre consumption), but also longer windows of availability when Miles needs cover for extended patrols.

**On-call posture is permanent.** There is no observed period in which Ganke is unreachable to Miles for more than the duration of a class. Phone is always within arm's reach. Notifications are not silenced. This is not casual friendship availability; it is the discipline of a duty officer, internalized so completely that he no longer experiences it as a discipline.

---

## 3. Tradecraft Inventory

### 3.1 Cover and Alibi Construction

Ganke is the primary fabricator of cover stories for Miles vis-à-vis (a) BVA administration, (b) Miles's parents, and (c) other students. His method is recognizable across instances:

- **Minimum viable lie.** He prefers the smallest possible deviation from truth — "he's in the bathroom," "he's grabbing food," "he had a family thing," "he's at the library" — rather than elaborate constructions. This reflects sound tradecraft instinct: small lies are sustainable, big lies collapse under follow-up questions.
- **Pre-emptive seeding.** He frequently establishes the cover *before* it is needed by mentioning, hours earlier, that Miles is tired / not feeling great / planning to study late. This creates a plausible context the later absence slots into.
- **Mirroring affect.** When delivering a cover to Rio Morales (a more discerning audience than BVA staff), he lowers verbal output and matches her concerned-mother tone; when delivering to a teacher, he raises cheerfulness and offers more verbal volume. He calibrates the delivery to the receiver — instinctive social engineering, not learned.
- **Single point of failure.** He maintains no written record of which lie was told to whom, when. He runs the entire alibi register from memory. This has been depicted as functional but is an unhardened system; under sustained adversarial questioning by anyone willing to cross-check, it would fracture.

### 3.2 Communications and Comms Discipline

- **Primary channel:** personal smartphone, standard consumer platform, text + voice. No depicted use of encrypted messaging, burner devices, or signal-isolated hardware. This is a meaningful security gap — Miles's roommate's commercial messaging history is, in principle, the single richest unsecured artifact of Spider-Man's civilian identity in existence.
- **Secondary channel:** laptop-based monitoring of police scanners, news feeds, and social-media searches for Spider-Man sightings. He functions as Miles's real-time situational-awareness layer during active operations.
- **Comms discipline failures:** he speaks Miles's secret aloud in semi-public spaces (dorm hallways, lunch tables) more often than tradecraft permits, mitigated only by lowered volume and the assumption that no one is listening with intent. He has been depicted multiple times catching himself mid-sentence, which indicates the discipline is *learned* rather than native; he has improved over years, but it remains a category of recurrent slip.
- **Op-sec strength:** he does not photograph Miles in costume. He does not post about him. He does not joke about him on social media in any decoder-able way. The high-visibility public channels are clean. The leaks are interpersonal, not digital.

### 3.3 Compartmentalization

This is Ganke's structural weakness as an operator and has been documented since the disclosure-to-Judge incident in *USM* (2011) #6–10. He does not naturally hold *information segregation* as a value. His instinct is to share with trusted persons; trust is, for him, a binary admission to the inner circle rather than a graduated permissions ladder. Over years he has learned to grit through this — secrets stay contained more reliably as he matures — but his historical record is one of slow concentric leakage rather than airtight containment. By the time of the 2016 series and after, his circle of secret-keepers has stabilized at a manageable but non-trivial number, and each addition has been a Ganke-driven event, not a Miles-authorized one.

### 3.4 Tech and Fabrication

- **Hardware capability:** modifies suits, props, and comms gear. Costume iteration on the original black suit is partly his — he is shown discussing and tweaking design in dorm-bench fashion. Not a professional engineer; a competent hobbyist who reads documentation, watches tutorials, and iterates by trial.
- **Software capability:** scripting and basic monitoring tools; able to spin up search/alert systems on standard frameworks. Not a black-hat hacker; no depicted intrusion into hardened systems. His tech is the tech a sharp seventeen-year-old with too much free time and serious motivation can plausibly produce.
- **Fabrication mode:** *assembly*, not invention. He combines off-the-shelf components and existing knowledge into new functional combinations. This is the LEGO operational signature transposed onto every domain: he does not design pieces, he assembles them. The cognitive style is consistent across hobbies and operational tasks.

### 3.5 Counter-Surveillance and Threat Assessment

Weak. Ganke does not check his six. He does not vary routes (he barely has routes — he barely leaves the dorm). He does not assess whether unfamiliar adults in proximity to Miles are surveillance assets. His threat-assessment is reactive (something happens, he responds) rather than proactive (scanning the environment for pre-attack indicators). The hardened-target work is Miles's; Ganke is the soft node and would be the obvious abduction lever if a sophisticated adversary identified the relationship — which makes it a quiet mercy of the publication record that he has been kept structurally safe.

---

## 4. Resources, Finances, Infrastructure

**Financial baseline.** Middle-class Korean-American family of origin, sufficient to fund private boarding-school tuition at BVA; not depicted as wealthy. Ganke's discretionary spending — LEGO sets (some in the multi-hundred-dollar range), tech components, snacks, gaming — implies a reasonable allowance and no economic anxiety. He is not depicted budgeting, working a job, or worrying about money. This is *consequential*: his ability to be on-call full time for Miles is partly a function of not needing to allocate hours to wage labor.

**Material assets.**
- Laptop (primary operational instrument).
- Smartphone.
- Substantial LEGO collection (functioning as both hobby and regulatory infrastructure — see §6).
- Eclectic media library, physical and digital.
- Modest electronics-tinkering kit.
- The dorm room itself — co-occupied with Miles — which serves as the de facto operations center, safe house, costume cache, and debrief space.

**Spatial infrastructure.** The Brooklyn Visions dormitory room is the single most important piece of operational real estate in his life. It is where the suit is stored, where Miles enters and exits in costume via window, where comms are run, where alibis are workshopped. The fact that this room is *shared* — that Ganke has no privacy from Miles and Miles has no privacy from Ganke — is the architectural precondition for the entire support operation. It is also, in tradecraft terms, a catastrophic single point of failure: one room search, one roommate swap, one administrator with a key, and the whole operation is compromised.

**Human resources.** Effectively none. Ganke has no second-tier confidant of his own; no mentor; no professional contact who knows what he is actually doing. He is a one-person desk with no relief shift and no oversight. This is the latent-fault-line architecture identified in the psychiatric workup, expressed structurally.

**Family infrastructure.** Backgrounded in canon. Parents present, supportive, geographically Brooklyn-proximate, functionally non-interfering with his life at school. They are not part of the operation and do not know its existence.

---

## 5. Patterns of Action — The Standard Plays

Over a decade of appearances, certain operational patterns recur with enough frequency to be flagged as standard plays:

**The Cover-and-Snack.** Miles slips out the window; Ganke immediately re-orients to the laptop or LEGO build, opens snacks, and is positioned as visibly *being here this whole time* if anyone enters. Plausible deniability through performed mundanity.

**The Talk-Down.** Miles returns shaken from a fight or moral conflict; Ganke runs an extended, low-key, joke-laced conversational debrief that functions as informal psychological first aid. He does not pretend to advise on the heroism specifically; he advises on the human inside the costume. This is consistently one of his most effective operational outputs.

**The Reference Strike.** When Miles faces an unfamiliar threat or scenario, Ganke produces — often within seconds — a relevant analog from genre literature, complete with how-it-was-resolved-there. Hit-rate is mixed; the analogs are sometimes useful, sometimes distracting, but the *function* (rapid framing of the unknown as a solvable structured problem) is regulatory as much as informational.

**The Bridge Call.** When Miles is missing past an established window, Ganke initiates contact — texts, then calls, then escalates. He has not yet been depicted having to make the next call (to Rio, to police, to anyone else), but the escalation ladder visibly exists in his head.

**The Cover-Story Cleanup.** When a Miles-cover gets challenged (a teacher who saw something, a parent who asks an unexpected follow-up), Ganke runs interference — adds detail, redirects attention, offers competing harmless explanations. Functions as a verbal fog generator.

**The Leak.** The signature negative-pattern, depicted enough times to be a play rather than an accident: under sustained internal pressure, Ganke discloses to a person he trusts, frames the disclosure as practical necessity, and presents the result to Miles as a *fait accompli* with a defense already prepared. Pattern is so consistent it can be predicted from the precursors (extended sole-burden period + Miles increasingly unavailable + presence of a trusted peer with relevant adjacent knowledge).

---

## 6. The LEGO Protocol as Operational Infrastructure

Worth a dedicated subsection because it is not decorative. The LEGO practice functions as:

- **Regulatory baseline.** Hand-occupied, attention-narrowed, low-stakes structured activity. It is his nervous-system reset.
- **Wait-state activity.** When Miles is out and Ganke is on-call, the build provides a parking pattern for cognition that does not consume the bandwidth he needs to remain alert to comms.
- **Cognitive metaphor.** The procedural assembly mode — instructions, discrete steps, verifiable subassemblies — is the same cognitive style he applies to alibi construction, tech modification, and problem decomposition.
- **Status object.** Completed builds displayed in the dorm signal hobby identity to outsiders, reinforcing the cover-self of "harmless hobbyist roommate."
- **Sleep-deprivation tell.** Quality and completion rate of builds reportedly degrade in periods of acute operational tempo. An observer with longitudinal access to his shelves could read his stress level off the half-finished sets.

The protocol is one of the more elegant self-designed regulatory systems in his peer cohort, and he did not consciously design it. It self-assembled around an existing hobby because the hobby happened to be load-bearing.

---

## 7. Signature Operational Tells

For the surveillance file proper — the micro-behaviors that mark him in a crowd, a transcript, or a recording:

- **Verbal:** hyper-referential speech, sentences that begin with "okay so" or "wait wait wait," frequent comparative constructions ("this is literally like —"), reflexive humor as a transition between affect-states, mid-sentence self-interruption when he notices he is over-sharing.
- **Postural:** horizontal default — he gravitates to bed, couch, floor. When upright, he leans. He is rarely depicted standing centered and balanced.
- **Manual:** something almost always in his hands — controller, brick, phone, food. Idle hands appear to make him uncomfortable.
- **Ocular:** eyes flick to phone within seconds of any pause in conversation. Glasses adjustment when uncertain.
- **Caloric:** eats during conversations, eats during stress, eats during recreation. Eating is the universal accompaniment, not an event.
- **Sleep-deprivation tells:** propped head, slow blinking, extended pauses before responding to direct questions.
- **Disclosure-pre-tremor:** when about to leak — i.e., to share something he was told to keep — he tends to verbal-escalate first (faster speech, longer sentences, more references) before delivering the substantive disclosure. Audible if you know to listen.
