- **Around Miles in costume vs. out of costume:** demeanor toward Miles is essentially identical in both states. No code-switch. This is unusual and is itself a tell — most secret-keepers compartmentalize the personae in their own behavior toward the secret-bearer. Ganke does not. He treats Spider-Man as Miles wearing a costume, full stop.
- **Around adults:** subtly more deferential register, removes references the adult would not catch, slightly raises politeness markers. Effective but detectable.
- **Around romantic interest:** verbal output increases, humor density increases, defensive deflection increases — the same operational mode as under stress, because for him this *is* a stress state.

---

## 8. Operational Strengths and Vulnerabilities — Net Assessment

**Strengths.** Sustainability (he has done this for years without burning out visibly); cover-naturalness (his presented self is genuinely his self, which is the strongest cover construction possible); information processing speed; affective steadiness under acute load; deep loyalty as a fixed input; cost-discipline (he asks for nothing in return).

**Vulnerabilities.** Compartmentalization failure (the chronic leak pattern); no counter-surveillance posture; no secondary confidant for his own load; single-point-of-failure infrastructure (one dorm room, one laptop, one phone); no escalation contacts beyond Miles; physical non-capability (he cannot defend himself or extract himself from a threat scenario); financial dependence on family that does not know what he does, meaning loss of family standing would collapse the resource base of the operation; and the long-tail risk that the regulatory protocols (humor, LEGO, snacking, affiliation) eventually saturate and stop discharging the load they have been quietly absorbing for years.

**Net.** As a civilian support asset, the subject is well above replacement-level — the operation he runs is the reason a meaningful fraction of his principal's secret-identity continuity exists. As a tradecraft practitioner per se, he is a gifted amateur with mature instincts and a structural blind spot around self-care and compartmentalization. The latter has not yet broken the operation. It is, however, the axis along which it will eventually break, if it breaks. The dossier should monitor accordingly.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE: GANKE LEE

## Preamble: The Shape of the Mind Behind the Eyes

To read Ganke's worldview accurately, the analyst must resist two seductive misreadings. The first is the *comic-relief* misreading: that he is a vehicle for jokes and has no operational philosophy worth mapping. The second is the *fanboy* misreading: that his pop-culture saturation is a substitute for genuine thought. Both are wrong. Ganke has a coherent, derivable operating system — one of the most internally consistent in his cohort — and it is precisely *because* he thinks in templates, references, and assembled parts that the system can be reverse-engineered cleanly from the behavioral record. He is, in a sense, the easiest subject in Miles Morales's circle to model, because he leaves the most surface trace per unit of interior state. He externalizes the operating system in the language he uses to externalize everything else.

What follows is that system, derived and exhaustive.

---

## 1. Cosmology: The World as a System That Can Be Read

Ganke's first and deepest axiom is that **the world has legible structure**. He does not experience reality as chaotic, hostile, or absurd. He experiences it as *patterned* — a domain with rules, conventions, recurring forms, and discoverable affordances. This is the unstated metaphysics behind every behavioral signature in the file: the LEGO building (discrete pieces fit together according to rules to produce a known whole), the genre-literacy (narratives obey conventions; if you know the conventions you can anticipate the next beat), the technical hobby (systems have specifications; specifications can be learned; learned specs can be modified).

This is not naïve rationalism. He grants that the structure is *partially* legible, that there are gaps, that surprises occur. But surprises, for Ganke, are not evidence that the world is unstructured; they are evidence that the model is incomplete and needs revision. A spider-bite that gives a friend powers is not a refutation of order — it is a new rule to integrate. His response to the disclosure event in *USM* (2011) #2 is the cosmology in miniature: confronted with the impossible, he does not flinch from the worldview; he expands it to accommodate.

The consequence: he is **constitutionally non-paranoid**. He does not assume hidden malevolent intent behind events. His baseline is that people and systems do roughly what their visible shape suggests. This is a strength (he is not exhausting himself decoding threats that aren't there) and a vulnerability (his threat-detection bandwidth is calibrated for narrative villains, not for ambient social predation).

---

## 2. Ontology of Other People: Templates First, Persons Second, Persons Always

Ganke reads people through **template-matching as the first pass, individuated correction on the second pass**. He meets someone, slots them rapidly into a known type (the gruff teacher who actually cares, the popular kid with the secret, the ex-villain seeking redemption), and then revises the template as data accumulates. This is efficient cognition; it is also why he can orient inside complex social situations faster than peers.

Critically — and this is where many template-thinkers fail — he *does* perform the second pass. He does not stay locked in the initial read. Bombshell is the cleanest example: the template ("former villain") would predict either fear or strategic distance; Ganke's revised individual read produced romantic pursuit. He updated on her. He is willing to be wrong about people in the direction of granting them more individuality than the type predicted.

His **default trust posture is positive-conditional**: he extends trust generously up front, withdraws it slowly, restores it readily. He does not require people to earn trust before receiving it; he requires them to *break* it before losing it, and even then his withdrawal is graduated rather than absolute. This is the operating posture of someone whose cosmology assumes structure includes basic reciprocity.

He believes — implicitly, never articulated — that **most people are doing their best with what they have**, and that bad behavior is more often pressure, ignorance, or bad templates than malice. This is consonant with his template-cognition: if behavior is structured, then deviant behavior is usually a structured response to a stressor, not a free choice for evil. This frames every villain in his vicinity as legible rather than incomprehensible — which is why he can romance one without cognitive dissonance.

---

## 3. Theory of Conflict: Conflict Is a Problem, Not a Condition

For Ganke, **conflict is an episode within an otherwise cooperative reality**, not the default state of human relations. He does not understand the world as fundamentally agonistic. This is a Hobbes-vs.-Locke axis distinction, and Ganke is firmly on the cooperative-baseline side: the natural state is people building things together; conflict is what happens when the building goes wrong.

The operational consequences are pervasive:

- **He does not personalize conflict.** When Miles confronts him about telling Judge, Ganke registers the rupture but does not enter a defensive-aggressive crouch. He apologizes, absorbs, repairs. He treats the conflict as a *problem in the system between them* rather than as Miles attacking him.
- **He does not escalate.** Across the entire publication record there is no scene in which Ganke initiates aggression, raises stakes, or refuses to climb down. His escalation profile is *flat*. The instinctive move under conflict is de-escalation through humor, not counter-pressure.
- **He has no taste for sustained adversariality.** He cannot maintain enemies. He has no nemeses, no grudges, no people-he-no-longer-speaks-to. Resentment does not stick to him; it slides off because the cosmology does not have a slot to store it.
- **He believes conflicts have solutions**, and that the solutions are usually *informational* or *communicative* — find the missing fact, say the unsaid thing, propose the compromise. This is the LEGO-builder's faith applied to social rupture: the right pieces exist; assembly is a matter of patience.

The limit case of this orientation: he is **poorly equipped to recognize an opponent who does not share his conflict ontology** — someone who treats conflict as the medium rather than the disturbance. He has not yet been written into a sustained encounter with that kind of antagonist (his villain exposure is largely refracted through Miles), but the file suggests this is where his model would break. He would keep trying to *solve* what the other party intended to *prolong*.

---

## 4. Theory of Control: Distributed, Improvisational, Influence-Not-Command

Ganke does not seek control over people, events, or outcomes in any direct sense. He seeks **influence through information and timing**. His operative model of agency is the *guy-in-the-chair* model — not coincidentally textualized in the 2016 series — wherein power is exercised by knowing what is happening, communicating it to the right actor at the right moment, and shaping decisions without making them.

This is a deliberate posture, not a fallback from being denied direct power. He is offered, at multiple points across the canon, opportunities to be *more* central, more visible, more decisive. He consistently declines, deflects, or routes those opportunities back to others. He prefers the chair to the field. This preference is principled rather than cowardly: he believes (correctly, in most cases) that he produces more value as a node in the network than as an actor in the situation.

His **model of control over himself** is similarly indirect. He does not white-knuckle his impulses; he manages them through environmental and behavioral routing. He builds LEGO when anxious rather than confronting the anxiety directly. He snacks rather than sitting with hunger or boredom. He talks rather than processing internally. This is regulation through *displacement into productive or low-cost activity* — a sophisticated, if avoidant, self-management strategy.

His **model of control over his future** is loose and emergent. He does not appear to operate from a five-year plan. He has no articulated career telos beyond the diffuse college-track expectation. He trusts that the structure will continue to be legible and that good moves will continue to present themselves. This is either wisdom or under-planning depending on the analyst's priors; the behavioral record supports either reading.

What he does **not** believe: that control is achieved through dominance, intimidation, withholding, or strategic deception. None of these tools are in his kit. He is one of the rare characters in his story-world whose influence is entirely *additive* — he gains it by giving (information, support, presence), not by taking or restricting.

---

## 5. Theory of Trust: The Asymmetric Architecture

This is the most diagnostically interesting region of the operational code, because Ganke's trust architecture is **asymmetric in ways he is unaware of**.

**Trust extended outward:** generous, fast, durable. He shares information, presence, and access freely. He assumes the other party will reciprocate in kind, and he is largely correct because his selection bias (the people he bonds with) is sound.

**Trust extended inward (to himself, by himself):** also generous. He trusts his own competence, his own reads, his own value to the bond. He is not self-doubting in any clinical sense.

**Trust received from others to hold their material:** this is where the architecture *fails its own specifications*. Ganke believes he is trustworthy — and he is, in intent. But the disclosure-leak pattern reveals that his operational definition of trustworthiness is **"I will protect the secret unless protecting it isolates me, in which case I will distribute it to a small number of vetted others who I trust to also protect it."** This is a coherent ethic — it is roughly the ethic of a small intelligence cell — but it is *not* the ethic Miles believes he is operating under, and Ganke has not made the discrepancy explicit because he has not made it explicit to *himself*.

The deeper trust-axiom underneath: **Ganke does not believe that any single individual should bear an unsharable load.** This is a genuine moral conviction, derivable from his behavior across years. He believes that secrets which crush their keepers should be redistributed, and that the keeper has standing to make that redistribution decision when the load becomes destructive. Miles believes that the keeper's role is absolute and the load is the price of admission. These are two different theories of the obligation, and the file's recurring secrecy ruptures are this theory-collision playing out in slow motion.

**Trust in institutions:** generally positive but not deep. He cooperates with school, parents, civic order — he is not a rebel — but he does not invest institutions with sacred authority. They are systems with rules; you work within them when convenient, around them when necessary (covering for Miles's absences requires routine, low-grade institutional deception which Ganke performs without ethical strain). He does not believe institutions deserve the truth in the way friends do.

---

## 6. Theory of Risk: Body Conservative, Information Liberal

Ganke's risk-tolerance profile is sharply **bifurcated by domain**.

**Physical risk: low tolerance, near-total avoidance.** He does not seek confrontation, fight, flee-and-pursue, or any embodied danger. He has no fantasy of being the hero in the suit; he has no envy of the people who take physical risk; he is content to remain safe. This is not cowardice — when Miles is endangered, Ganke does not hide or freeze; he becomes useful from whatever position he can occupy. But he does not insert his body into the risk surface if a better-positioned body is available. This is rational allocation, not character flaw, and he holds it without shame.

**Informational risk: high tolerance, sometimes excessive.** He will share, speculate, theorize, decode, and improvise around information with a freedom that occasionally exceeds the situation's tolerance. The disclosure leaks are the symptomatic expression. He treats information as wanting to circulate — almost as if it has a thermodynamic property, an entropy toward distribution — and his job as either accelerating or decelerating that circulation rather than absolutely containing it.

**Social risk: moderate, with selective courage.** He will say embarrassing things, pursue the romantic interest who is "out of his league" or "off-limits," wear the unfashionable thing, make the joke that might not land. He is willing to be socially uncomfortable in service of a goal. He is *less* willing to risk a primary bond — he will swallow grievance, defer his own needs, accommodate inconvenience to preserve the relationships that matter.

**Cognitive/identity risk: low.** He does not seek experiences that would destabilize his self-concept. He does not, for instance, pursue spiritual or psychedelic seeking; he does not radically rotate his interests; he does not seriously question his foundational orientations. His self is *built*, in the LEGO sense — assembled, stable, structurally sound — and he does not unbuild it for sport.

**Underlying axiom:** risk is justified by the expected value of the outcome *to a relationship or system he cares about*. He does not risk for risk's sake. He does not risk for self-actualization. He risks for utility within an attachment.

---

## 7. Theory of Truth: Pragmatic, Provisional, Plural

Ganke does not have a correspondence-theory absolutism about truth. He treats truth as **operationally useful approximation that gets revised with new data**. Templates are truth until better templates arrive. Genre conventions are truth until the actual situation violates them, at which point the convention is updated, not the situation rejected.

This is **why he is comfortable in deception when the deception serves the protected relationship**: lying to Miles's parents about Miles's whereabouts does not register as a truth-violation because the operative truth — *Miles is safe and doing important work* — is being preserved by the local falsehood. He is not consequentialist in a formal sense; he is *relationally consequentialist*. Truth-telling and truth-shaping are both tools for maintaining the integrity of the bonds that matter.

The exception, and it is firm: he does not lie to Miles directly about substantive matters. Even when his behavior contradicts an agreement with Miles (Judge), he does not subsequently lie about having done it; he confesses, often without being asked. The bond's interior is a truth-zone; the bond's perimeter is a permitted-fiction-zone. This is a defensible ethic, and it is internally consistent.

---

## 8. Theory of His Own Place: The Chosen Periphery

This is the axis where Ganke is most psychologically unusual and most resistant to easy reading.

He has located himself, with full clarity, in the **chosen periphery** of someone else's central story. He is the roommate, the confidant, the guy-in-the-chair, the second-banana-in-the-romantic-subplot. And he experiences this position not as consolation, not as runner-up, but as **the correct slot for him**.

The derivation requires care. Many readers project that this *must* be suppression — that under the surface there must be the conventional sidekick's repressed wish to be the hero. The behavioral record does not support the projection. Across more than a decade of publication, under multiple writers with different sensibilities, in scenarios specifically designed to provoke that wish, Ganke does not exhibit it. The simplest explanation is that the wish is not there.

The underlying belief structure appears to be:

- **There are different kinds of significance, and central-protagonist significance is one kind, not the only kind.**
- **Participation in something meaningful at the support level is genuinely satisfying, not a downgrade from participation at the lead level.**
- **He is well-suited to support and poorly suited to lead, and self-knowledge accurately allocates one's effort.**
- **The story is not a competition for screen time; it is a collaborative production, and his role in the production is real work with real value.**

This is, in a quiet way, a sophisticated philosophical position. It is adjacent to but distinct from humility, modesty, or resignation. It is closer to a **role-ethics** orientation — the conviction that fulfilling one's actual role well is the substance of a good life, and that the role one actually occupies is more worthy of investment than the role one might fantasize about.

The vulnerability in this position is not visible from inside it: he has not stress-tested whether the satisfaction holds when the central figure stops needing him in the way he is currently needed. The role-ethics works when the role is recognized and engaged. The file's open question — what happens when the joke stops working, what happens when Miles outgrows the configuration that makes Ganke central-to-the-periphery — is exactly the stress test that has not been run.

---

## 9. Theory of Time and the Future

Ganke is **present-thick, future-light**. He is densely engaged with the immediate situation — what's happening now, what's needed in the next hour, what the current crisis requires — and comparatively thin on long-horizon projection. He does not appear to spend significant cognition on five-year plans, life-trajectory modeling, or strategic positioning for adult outcomes.

This is partially developmental (he is an adolescent), partially temperamental (his cognitive style is associative and present-bound rather than projective), and partially **a structural artifact of his role**: the secret-keeping load means his bandwidth is consumed by the now of Miles's life, leaving little for the long arc of his own.

He is not nihilistic about the future, nor anxious about it; he is simply **trusting that the present, well-handled, produces a viable future**. This is the LEGO ethic again at the timescale of a life: assemble the current piece correctly, the structure emerges.

The risk this trust does not see: futures shaped only by well-handled presents tend to be futures shaped by other people's plans, because *they* did the projection. Ganke's life, if this orientation holds, is at risk of being a beautifully assembled support structure for someone else's edifice rather than a structure of his own design. Whether this is tragedy or fulfillment depends on whether the role-ethics holds at adult-life scale.

---

## 10. Theory of the Self: Built, Not Discovered

Ganke does not appear to operate on a *discovery* model of selfhood — the romantic notion that there is a true self buried inside that one must excavate. He operates on a **construction model**: the self is what you have built so far, made of the pieces you have accumulated (interests, knowledge, relationships, commitments), and it can be added to, revised, repaired, and extended.

The implications are pervasive:

- He is not on a quest for identity. He has one. He built it.
- He is not anxious about authenticity. The constructed self *is* the authentic self in his model; there is no truer hidden version against which the surface could be measured and found wanting.
- He is not envious of others' more dramatic selves. They built differently; he built this; the comparison is category-confused.
- He can integrate new pieces (Miles being Spider-Man, his own romantic life, expanding social world) without destabilization, because integration is what building *does*.

This is the deepest reason he is psychologically robust without being defended in the rigid sense. His self is not a fortress requiring walls; it is a structure that accommodates additions.

---

## 11. The Operational Code Summarized as Decision Rules

Reduced to the rules he actually executes in situations:

1. **Read the situation as a structured problem.** Identify the type. Apply the template. Revise the template against the specifics.
2. **Protect the primary bond first.** All other considerations — institutional, ethical, social — yield to the integrity of the bonds with Miles and (secondarily) the small circle of trusted others.
3. **Deflect acute affect through humor; route it into building.** Do not absorb the affect rigidly; let it move.
4. **Share information freely upward and outward to trusted nodes; withhold from untrusted nodes; never lie inside the primary bond.**
5. **Take the chair, not the field.** Influence through information and timing; let the field actors act.
6. **Conserve the body; spend the attention; deploy the words.** Risk-allocate according to your actual capacities.
7. **Assume good faith until shown otherwise; restore good faith after rupture quickly.**
8. **Do not personalize conflict; treat it as a system problem to be solved.**
9. **Trust the present to produce the future.** Do the next piece well.
10. **The role you occupy well is the life you are living.** Do not lose the actual life to fantasies of a different one.

---

## 12. Coda: The One Belief He Does Not Know He Holds

The most consequential element of an operational code is often the axiom the subject cannot articulate. For Ganke, the unspoken axiom — derivable from the entire behavioral record but never voiced — is this:

**A burden too heavy for one person to carry is not actually a one-person burden; it is a configuration error, and the correct response is to redistribute rather than to break.**

This is the axiom that produces the disclosure leaks. It is also the axiom that makes him sustainable in a role that should, by all reasonable prediction, have broken him already. The same belief produces the file's recurring complication and the file's most durable strength. He has not been challenged to examine it. When he is, the examination will be the most important psychological event of his life.

Until then, the operational code runs cleanly, the templates fit, the pieces snap together, and the structure holds.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK — GANKE LEE

## Preamble: the code as enacted vs. the code as professed

Ganke does not articulate a moral philosophy. He has never, on panel, given a speech about right and wrong; he has never invoked a religious framework, a political ideology, a familial moral inheritance, or a coherent ethical theory. This silence is itself the first datum. He is the rare adolescent character whose ethics must be reconstructed entirely from *behavior under load* — from what he does when the stakes are real, repeatedly, across more than a decade of publication. The reconstruction below is what the record actually supports, not what a casual reading of his comic-relief surface might suggest.

The headline finding: **Ganke operates a coherent, personalist, loyalty-first ethic with a strong consequentialist undercurrent and a weak deontological frame.** He privileges the wellbeing of specific known persons over abstract rules; he is willing to lie, conceal, fabricate, and deceive institutions when the protected person's interest requires it; he is not willing to harm, exploit, or instrumentalize a person to achieve an outcome. His code fractures predictably at one seam — the management of secrets he has been entrusted with — and the fracture is consistent enough across writers and years to be characterological, not incidental.

---

## 1. The hierarchy of obligation (as revealed by triage)

When Ganke's loyalties are tested, they sort in a stable order. The order is derivable from which obligation he sacrifices when two collide.

**Tier 1: Miles's life and physical safety.** Above everything. He has lied to Rio and Jefferson Morales — Miles's parents, adults he likes and respects — repeatedly and without visible hesitation when the truth would either endanger Miles or force a confrontation that endangered him. He has run cover stories to BVA faculty, fabricated whereabouts, intercepted communications, and absorbed the social cost of being the kid who "knows where Miles is." None of this is treated by him as morally fraught at the moment of action. The post-hoc discomfort, when it surfaces, is about *being caught* or *being a bad friend to the parents*, not about the lying itself. Lying to protect Miles is not, in his operating code, a transgression at all. It is the baseline.

**Tier 2: Miles's emotional and psychological wellbeing.** This sits just under physical safety, and the two occasionally tug against each other. He will withhold information from Miles that he judges Miles cannot currently bear; he will also volunteer hard truths when he judges Miles needs them. The triage is not always correct — see §4, the disclosure pattern — but the intention is consistent: protect Miles's capacity to function.

**Tier 3: The integrity of the immediate friendship circle.** Judge, later Bombshell, later the expanded peer group at BVA and beyond. He will lie to outsiders for these people, will cover for them in small ways, will defend them verbally. The protection radius is narrower and the willingness to violate norms for them is lower than for Miles, but it is real.

**Tier 4: Institutional honesty (school, parents-not-his-own, civic authority).** Ganke is not anti-institutional. He completes his schoolwork, respects his teachers in the ordinary sense, and is by every available measure a "good kid" in the eyes of BVA administration. But these institutions are *instrumentally* respected — they are honored when honoring them costs nothing, and they are deceived without ceremony when honoring them would cost something that matters. There is no Kantian thread in him. He does not believe lying to authority is intrinsically wrong; he believes it is *socially expensive and usually unnecessary*, which is a different proposition.

**Tier 5: Abstract strangers and the broader public.** Present but distant. Ganke cares about the city Miles is protecting in a generalized, civic-sentimental way — he reads the news, tracks the headlines, knows which villains are active — but he does not have an enacted ethic of obligation to strangers. He is not a utilitarian saving-the-most-lives reasoner. He has never advocated for Miles to take a particular mission on the grounds that the city needs it; he has consistently advocated based on whether Miles can handle it and whether his cover holds.

**Tier 6: His own interests, comfort, and reputation.** Genuinely deprioritized. This is one of the more morally distinctive features of his behavior: he routinely accepts personal cost (academic risk from covering for Miles, social awkwardness, sleep deprivation, lost time, the chronic load discussed in the workup) without ledgering it. He does not perform martyrdom — there is no "after all I've done for you" subroutine in his speech patterns, across years of canon. He absorbs cost as a structural feature of the friendship, not as currency.

The tier structure tells you the code: **persons over principles, near over far, the bonded one above all.** This is a particularist ethic in the philosophical sense — it would be recognized by Bernard Williams sooner than by Kant.

---

## 2. What he will do (the permitted catalog)

Reconstructed from enacted behavior, here is the operational permission set:

- **Lie to parents (Miles's, by extension institutional adults).** Without flinching, when stakes are real. Small lies and large; sustained narrative fabrications spanning days.
- **Lie to school administration.** Cover stories for absences, late nights, sudden disappearances. He has become a competent improvisational liar — fluent, plausible, low-tell.
- **Withhold information from peers when the information belongs to Miles.** He has, after the early disclosure failures, learned to compartmentalize; later runs show him guarding specific operational details (Miles's location during a fight, the identities of other heroes Miles is working with) more effectively than he guarded the original secret.
- **Use school and personal tech resources for non-sanctioned purposes.** Monitor police bands, scrape news feeds, fabricate digital alibis, build comm rigs. He treats institutional IT and his own bandwidth as commons-for-Miles. No depicted compunction.
- **Pursue romantic interest in someone with a criminal-adjacent past (Bombshell).** Knowing it. Without re-litigating it. This is morally interesting: he extends the same particularist generosity to her that he extends to Miles. Once she is *a person he knows and likes*, her abstract criminal record stops counting against her in his calculus.
- **Befriend, accommodate, and help former antagonists when Miles vouches for them.** The pattern with Bombshell extends across his expanded peer group. His circle-of-trust criterion is *vouched-for by a trusted insider*, not *clean record*.
- **Joke at almost any moment, including dark ones.** He treats humor as morally neutral or positive — a means of regulation, connection, and tension-release. He has never apologized for a joke in a way that suggests he regards joking-in-bad-moments as a moral failure. The norm against gallows humor is not in his code.
- **Make unilateral judgment calls about Miles's wellbeing.** When he decides Miles needs to know something, or doesn't, or needs help he hasn't asked for, Ganke acts. He does not have a strong consent-of-the-protected ethic; he has a strong *judgment-of-the-friend* ethic, which sometimes overrides what Miles has explicitly requested.

## 3. What he won't do (the prohibited catalog)

Equally important and, in some ways, more revealing.

- **He will not harm a person to advance an outcome.** No depicted violence, no instrumentalization of strangers, no willingness to use a person as a tool against their interest. The closest he comes is gentle social manipulation (steering a conversation, distracting a parent), and even those instances are minor.
- **He will not exploit Miles's identity for personal benefit.** Across years, he has never traded on his proximity to Spider-Man for status, money, social capital, or romantic advantage. He could have. Adolescents routinely do, with much smaller secrets. He does not. This is one of the strongest moral signals in the record. The secret is held *for* Miles, not *with* Miles as shared capital.
- **He will not abandon a person under threat.** When Miles is in trouble, Ganke does not duck. He cannot fight — he knows this — but he stays in the comms, stays awake, stays available. He has never been depicted choosing personal safety over presence for Miles.
- **He will not perform contempt for someone Miles cares about, even when he disagrees.** When Miles's romantic and social orbit expands, Ganke does not snipe, does not undermine, does not subtly campaign against. The non-jealousy noted in the workup is also a moral commitment: he treats Miles's other bonds as legitimate, and behaves accordingly.
- **He will not lie to Miles about consequential matters.** This is the crucial asymmetry. He lies freely to everyone else *on Miles's behalf*; he is broadly truthful with Miles himself. The disclosure-leak pattern is not him lying to Miles — it is him telling other people things Miles asked him not to. When Miles confronts him about the leak, Ganke admits it. He does not double down, manufacture a cover, or gaslight. The truth-relation with Miles is the spine of his code.
- **He will not weaponize the secret.** Not in conflict with Miles, not in fights with peers, not for leverage. The secret is never threatened to be released. This is morally unremarkable to most readers because Ganke is the comic-relief friend; in the actual landscape of secret-keeping behavior, it is exceptional.
- **He will not punish Miles for outgrowing him.** Across the Ahmed and Ziglar runs, as Miles's world expanded and Ganke's screen time contracted, there is no retaliatory withdrawal, no guilt-induction, no "you've changed" subroutine. The absence is the moral fact.
- **He will not pretend competence he doesn't have when it matters.** He jokes about being the guy in the chair, but when a situation exceeds his actual technical or strategic capacity, he says so. He does not bluff into stakes where bluffing would endanger Miles.

## 4. The fault line: the disclosure pattern as ethical fracture

The single durable fracture in Ganke's code is the secret-management failure first depicted in *USM* (2011) #6–10 and recurring in attenuated form thereafter. The honest moral analysis is this:

Ganke's code privileges loyalty to Miles above honesty to institutions. It does not have a clear rule about honesty *between* trusted insiders. When the burden of holding Miles's secret becomes affectively heavy, Ganke's default — *bring a trusted person in, distribute the load, manage the bond through over-communication* — collides with Miles's explicit directive: *tell no one*.

The fracture is not a moral failure of caring. It is a structural inconsistency in the code: he has not internalized "Miles's directives about Miles's information are inviolable." Instead, he has internalized "Miles's wellbeing is paramount, and I am the judge of what serves it." Those two principles diverge precisely when Miles's stated wishes about secrecy run against Ganke's felt sense that Judge, or Bombshell, or whoever, needs to know in order for the friend-system to function.

This is a *paternalism* problem dressed as a *loyalty* problem. Ganke is not betraying Miles when he leaks; from inside his code, he is *better-serving* Miles than Miles knows how to be served. The post-hoc apologies he offers are real, but the pattern recurs because the underlying premise — that he is qualified to override Miles's information control when he judges it necessary — has never been revised. He has gotten *better* at it (later leaks are smaller, more contained, more defensible) but has not abandoned the prerogative.

This is the seam through which most of his ethical risk runs. It is also the feature that most clearly distinguishes his code from a saint's: he is a loyal particularist, not a humble one. He arrogates judgment.

## 5. Consistencies across writers and years

Across Bendis (2011–2018), Ahmed (2018–2022), and Ziglar (2022–), the following moral features have not budged:

- **Particularism over principle.** No writer has given him a rule-based ethical moment.
- **Truth-relation with Miles preserved.** No writer has had him lie to Miles in any consequential way.
- **No exploitation of proximity.** No writer has had him cash in the secret for personal gain.
- **No retaliatory withdrawal.** No writer has had him punish Miles for the expansions of Miles's life.
- **Civilian-to-civilian non-harm.** No writer has had him do anything that materially harms a non-villain stranger.
- **Humor as moral lubricant, not weapon.** No writer has had him use a joke to wound someone.

This stability is not accidental. It is the spine of the character — the reason he has functioned as a stable load-bearing element in Miles's narrative across three primary writers and multiple editorial regimes. Modify any of the six and you have someone else.

## 6. Shifts over time (the maturation arc)

The code has not changed in content. It has changed in **execution quality** and **range of application**.

**Early (USM 2011, ages 13–14ish).** The code is present but unrefined. Leaks happen because he hasn't yet learned that his particularist loyalty needs operational discipline. The lies to adults are clumsier; the cover stories thinner; the regulation through sharing is closer to impulse than to judgment.

**Middle (Spider-Man 2016, post-incursion).** The code becomes operational. He is now functionally competent at his role: better lies, tighter compartmentalization, more reliable comms. The Bombshell arc extends his particularism to a former antagonist, which is a real moral development — the code is shown to be *expandable* rather than narrowly Miles-only. He is also, in this period, the most explicit caretaker he has ever been: more frequent fabrications to Rio and Jefferson, more sustained covering at BVA.

**Late (Ahmed 2018–2022, Ziglar 2022–).** The code has matured into something like a stable professional ethic of friendship. He has accepted that he is, structurally, the support node, and has stopped reaching for roles outside that. The non-jealous accommodation of Miles's expanding circle is the moral signature of this period. The disclosure pattern persists but at much lower amplitude — he has learned to hold more, longer, in part because the circle of people who already know has expanded, reducing the affective load on him specifically.

**What has not happened that easily could have.** No darkening. No cynicism. No resentment-coding. No turn toward self-interest. No moral compromise under stress that broke the code's main spine. This is unusual for a character carrying his cumulative load. The writerly choice has been to keep him steady, and the in-character read consistent with that choice is that his code is genuinely robust — built, like one of his LEGO assemblies, of small reliable pieces patiently fitted, not of grand commitments that can shatter.

## 7. The unaddressed ethical questions

A complete moral file must note what the record does *not* contain, because the absences shape the prognosis.

- **He has never had to choose between Miles's life and a stranger's life.** The trolley case has not been put to him. We do not know whether his particularism would hold under that pressure or whether a buried utilitarian or rule-based commitment would surface.
- **He has never been asked to lie to Miles to protect Miles.** This is the inverse of the disclosure-leak: not "tell others what Miles wants hidden" but "hide from Miles what Miles needs to know." It is the test his code is least prepared for, because both of its primary commitments — truth-relation with Miles, and judgment-of-Miles's-wellbeing — would point opposite directions. The fracture would be diagnostic.
- **He has never had a secret of his own that mattered.** The asymmetry of the friendship — he holds Miles's, Miles has never had to hold his — has not been stress-tested. If Ganke had a real secret requiring real protection, would he extend Miles the same paternalistic override he extends himself? The record does not say.
- **He has never been threatened by a hostile party for the information he carries.** Coercion has not been applied. Whether the code survives torture, blackmail, or sustained pressure from an antagonist is unknown. The structural safety in which he has been kept (per the Medical section) extends to this domain: his ethics have never been tested against an adversary.
- **His moral relation to his own family is essentially undepicted.** He has obligations to his parents, presumably to siblings, presumably to a Korean-American cultural and possibly religious inheritance. None of this has been written. The code as reconstructed is a code of friendship; its domestic and ancestral dimensions are blank pages.

## 8. Synthesis

Ganke's ethic is the ethic of *the held hand in the dark*. He has decided, without ever announcing the decision, that a particular person matters more than a great many rules, and he organizes his behavior accordingly. He lies to protect that person; he refuses to harm anyone in service of that protection; he does not exploit the position the protection puts him in; he does not punish the protected person for the cost of the protection. He arrogates one prerogative — the prerogative to judge what serves the friend better than the friend can judge — and that single arrogation is the seam through which his code, on rare occasion, leaks.

He is not a moral hero. He is something rarer in adolescent characterization: a moral *constant*. The code does not transcend; it does not transform; it simply holds, year after year, under load, with the small repeating fracture that is also the proof it is real and not idealized. Whether it holds when the joke stops working — when paternalistic judgment confronts genuine harm, when the secret is demanded under threat, when his own life requires from someone the protection he has spent a decade extending — is the unanswered question this file flags forward.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE

## Subject: Ganke Lee

---

## 6.0 Preliminary Framing

Subject is, before he is anything else, a **talker**. The single most reliable behavioral constant across a decade-plus of recorded interaction (2011 *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* through the Ahmed and Ziglar runs) is verbal output. He fills silence. He fills *other people's* silence. He fills panels he is not the focal character of — captioned in the margins, half-off-frame, mid-sentence. A canon page in which Ganke is present and not speaking is rarer than a page in which he is present and speaking; and a page in which he is silent and present is almost always doing characterization work — it means something is wrong, something is being held, or something is being privately enjoyed (the LEGO baseline). Silence is the marked condition; speech is the default. Any communications analysis of this subject must begin from that asymmetry.

Speech, for Ganke, is **regulatory infrastructure**. It is how he metabolizes affect, how he secures the bond, how he discharges anxiety, how he problem-solves out loud, how he triangulates novel situations against known templates, and — under load — how he leaks. The mouth is the pressure-release valve. Close the valve and the system has nowhere to go. The longitudinal record bears this out: Ganke under conditions of enforced verbal restraint (parents present, school officials present, the rare scene in which Miles instructs him directly to stop talking) shows visible somatic compression — leg-jiggle, snack-acceleration, laptop-clutch. Then the talk resumes the moment the constraint lifts and runs at slightly elevated pressure for several beats before re-baselining.

---

## 6.1 Register Map by Audience

Subject is a **fluent code-switcher** within a narrow but well-calibrated band. He does not have the dramatic register-collapse of an autistic-coded character who speaks one way to everyone; he has the easy, automatic adjustments of a socially fluent adolescent. The bands:

**With Miles (primary register).** Maximally informal. Sentence fragments, abandoned clauses, interrupted self-corrections, pop-cultural shorthand, in-joke recursion. He does not finish a substantial percentage of sentences with Miles because he does not have to — Miles fills in. They have evolved a partial private dialect: shared reference points (specific LEGO sets, specific videogames, specific manga arcs, specific YouTube creators implied if not always named) function as compressed packets. A four-word reference does the work of a paragraph of explanation. Names get diminutized ("Miles" rarely; "dude," "man," "bro" frequent; address by first name is reserved for moments of genuine seriousness and functions as a tell — when Ganke says "Miles," look at the next panel).

**With other peers (Bombshell, Judge, later BVA peers in 2016, Barbara, Starling, Shift).** Slightly more complete sentences. Performance level rises — he is aware of audience, deploys jokes with setup-and-punchline structure rather than the gestural in-jokes Miles gets. With Bombshell specifically, the register *compresses upward into formality under romantic anxiety* — he becomes *more* grammatical, *more* coherent, briefly, before crashing into nervous run-ons. The pursuit-of-Bombshell pages are a controlled experiment in his linguistic stress response: watch the sentence length oscillate.

**With Miles's parents (Rio and Jefferson).** Register shifts to *deferential-cheerful*. Full sentences. "Mrs. Morales," "Mr. Davis" or "Mr. Morales" — uses honorifics reliably, a marker of his actual home training (the Lee household, though sparsely depicted, has clearly produced a kid who knows how to address adults). Volume drops. Joke density drops by an order of magnitude — he does not perform comedy for them, he performs *competence and harmlessness*. He is acutely aware that his cover-stories for Miles depend on being read as a benign, slightly nerdy, non-threatening presence, and his speech consciously delivers that read. This is also where his **alibi voice** lives — see 6.5.

**With school authority (teachers, BVA administrators).** Formal-compliant. Speaks when spoken to. Answers questions accurately when the questions are academic; redirects gracefully when the questions are about Miles. Vocabulary upshifts measurably — words he would never use with Miles ("essentially," "I think what happened was —," "to be honest with you") appear here.

**With strangers and adults outside his circle.** Polite to a fault. Says "thank you" reflexively, holds doors verbally ("after you"), apologizes for taking up space. The contrast between this register and his Miles-register is the largest in his repertoire.

**With himself (the talking-out-loud-while-building register).** Muttered, fragmentary, half-narrating the task ("okay, okay, so the — yeah, there"). Documented across LEGO sequences and laptop-debugging sequences. He thinks audibly. When alone in a room he is rarely silent for long, even with no one to receive the talk.

---

## 6.2 Diction Inventory

**Lexical baseline.** Contemporary American adolescent English, geographically Brooklyn-coded but not heavily slang-marked — he is a private-school boarder, not a street-coded speaker, and his vocabulary reflects a middle-class internet-native upbringing more than a regional one. The register is closer to *Discord channel* than *block*.

**High-frequency function words and fillers:**
- *"Dude"* — phatic, frequent, gender-neutral in his usage, applied to Miles, to Bombshell occasionally (a tell of nervous flattening), to himself in exasperation ("dude, no").
- *"Man"* — interchangeable with "dude," slight preference in moments of mild emphasis.
- *"Bro"* — rarer than dude/man; used with deliberate emphasis, often comic.
- *"Okay"* — opener and closer, multi-purpose. "Okay so —" is his single most reliable sentence-launcher. "Okay" alone, terminal, is acquiescence; "okay???" rising is incredulity.
- *"Literally"* — adolescent intensifier, used loosely and frequently, not always literally.
- *"Like"* — discourse marker, high frequency, mid-sentence, marks hesitation and approximation.
- *"Basically"* — his preferred summarizer; precedes a compressed model of a complex situation. He uses this when he has finished thinking about something and is delivering the conclusion.
- *"Wait —"* — interrupts himself and others; marks the moment a new pattern-match has fired. High diagnostic value: a "wait —" almost always means he has just connected two things.
- *"So"* — discourse pivot, often initiates explanation.

**Reference-saturated vocabulary.** The single most distinctive diction feature is the **density of cultural reference per unit of utterance**. He metabolizes lived events into pop-cultural templates in near real time — "this is like —" "this is just —" "okay this is the part where —." The references skew: superhero comics (with self-aware meta-commentary, post the 2016 series), animated series, videogames, anime/manga, science-fiction film, internet-native shorthand. He does *not* reach for sports references, for music references in volume, or for literary references outside the canon of genre. The reference vocabulary is the boundary of his cultural self.

**LEGO/technical vocabulary.** Precise. He names specific pieces by function, knows model numbers, understands build-systems vocabulary. With tech: he uses correct terms for networking, scripting, OS-level operations, hardware. He does not bluff. When he does not know a technical term he asks or substitutes a description; he does not invent.

**Words he rarely or never uses.** Profanity is mild and infrequent — "crap," "what the hell," occasionally "shit" under acute stress, almost never the harder registers. He does not curse fluently; it sits uncomfortably in his mouth when it appears, which is a tell that the situation is past his coping band. He does not use sexual language overtly; talk about Bombshell stays in romantic-adolescent register ("she's amazing," "she's so cool"), never crude. He does not use violent language as metaphor ("I'm gonna kill him," "I could murder a sandwich") with the easy frequency of his peer cohort — striking, given Miles's literal life-and-death context. He has absorbed the seriousness of the vocabulary even if he keeps the affect light.

---

## 6.3 Syntax and Prosody

**Sentence architecture.** Predominantly **paratactic and additive** — chains of short clauses linked with *and, so, but, like, and then,* rather than subordinated complex sentences. He thinks forward, not down. Long Ganke utterances are long by accumulation, not by depth.

**Self-interruption.** Frequent. A characteristic pattern: he begins a sentence, registers a new thought mid-utterance, breaks with a dash or a "wait —" or "actually —," and pivots. The interrupted clause often does not get resumed. Transcripts of his speech read as **stacked partial drafts** rather than finished prose.

**Question intonation.** High frequency of upspeak — declarative sentences delivered with rising terminal contour, a generational marker but also, in his case, a *bond-checking* feature: it invites confirmation, keeps the conversational floor open, signals non-imposition of his view. He does not lecture. Even when he is the one who knows the most in the room, he phrases as offer rather than assertion.

**Speed.** Fast. Higher than mean for his peer group. Speed elevates further under excitement and under anxiety — the two are not always distinguishable from speech-rate alone, requiring context.

**Volume.** Low-to-medium baseline. He is not a loud kid. Volume rises with excitement (a LEGO unboxing, a Miles-related revelation, a Bombshell sighting) and *drops* under serious stress — the inverse of many peers. When Ganke goes quiet *and small,* something is genuinely wrong.

**Pauses.** Rare. When they occur they are diagnostic. A Ganke pause means: (i) he has just understood something he did not want to understand; (ii) he is choosing whether to say a thing that should not be said; (iii) Miles is in trouble and Ganke has run out of script. The pause is the most communicative thing he does.

---

## 6.4 Rhetoric and Argumentation

**Rhetorical posture.** **Collaborative-suggestive**, not declarative-authoritative. He proposes, he frames, he offers options. "What if —," "we could —," "have you thought about —," "okay but what about —." He almost never issues an imperative to Miles or anyone else; when he does, it is small and protective ("get down," "don't open that," "call your mom").

**Mode of persuasion.** **Analogy and worked example.** He convinces by drawing a parallel to a known case — usually a fictional one. The persuasion is, "this situation is structurally like that situation, and in that one the answer turned out to be X, so —." This is sometimes effective (the situations *do* often map) and sometimes a category error (real superhero life does not always honor narrative convention). He has learned, over the run, to caveat: "okay but in real life maybe —."

**Concession behavior.** Concedes quickly, often preemptively. "You're right —" "no, no, that's fair —" "okay yeah I see it." This is partly genuine intellectual honesty and partly relational lubricant; the cost of holding a position is, for him, almost always higher than the cost of yielding. He **does not argue to win**. He argues to think out loud with another person.

**Disagreement signature.** When he genuinely disagrees, it surfaces as a quiet, repeated return to the same point across the conversation rather than a single confrontation. He will yield in the moment and then circle the topic back four panels later, recast as a question. This is non-confrontational persistence, a relational form of dissent that preserves the bond while not abandoning the position. It is also how he occasionally moves Miles off bad decisions without ever opposing him directly.

---

## 6.5 Deflection, Cover, and the Alibi Voice

Ganke is an **operational liar in a narrow professional sense**. He has been Miles's cover for years and has developed a specific register for it. The alibi voice has identifiable features:

- **Slight overcompletion of sentences.** Where his natural speech fragments, the alibi voice produces full subject-verb-object structures. Grammar tightens.
- **Specific-but-mundane detail.** He has learned not to over-specify (the liar's tell) and not to under-specify (the evasive tell). He lands on the middle band: "he's in the library, I think on the third floor, he had like a paper or something." Generic enough to be unfalsifiable, specific enough to be plausible.
- **Diminished joke density.** Comedy drops out. The alibi voice is *boringly cheerful*, calibrated to be forgettable.
- **Subtle volume drop and pace reduction.** He slows down. This is the most reliable tell that the alibi voice is engaged: real Ganke is fast, alibi Ganke is paced.
- **Recovery on dismissal.** The moment the adult walks away, he exhales audibly and the baseline rate snaps back. This is consistent across years.

**Deflection in non-cover contexts.** When the topic turns to Ganke himself — his family, his fears, his future, his interiority — he deflects through three reliable moves:

1. **Pivot to humor.** A joke turns the focus outward.
2. **Pivot to Miles.** "Forget about me, what about you —" "anyway, what are we doing about —." He redirects to the other person's drama, which he has trained himself and his interlocutors to treat as the legitimate subject.
3. **Pivot to a topic.** He surfaces a fact, a reference, a question about the world. The exit ramp into the impersonal.

The deflection pattern is so reliable that it functions as a tell *by absence*: in the rare scene where he does not deflect a personal question, something significant is being permitted to surface. Catalog those scenes; they are diagnostically rich.

---

## 6.6 Expression of Affect

**How he says he loves someone.** He does not say it. Not in declarative form, not in the standard phrasing, not even in its acceptable adolescent-male variants ("love you, man"). Affection is communicated through:

- **Presence and availability.** "I'm here," "I got you," "I'm on it," "I'll be there in like ten," "where are you?" — these *are* his I-love-yous, in volume and in functional weight. Track the number of times across the run he says some variant of *"I got you"* or *"I'm on it"* to Miles; the count is the love letter.
- **Tasking himself.** He volunteers labor unbidden. "I'll handle it," "I'll cover for you," "I already did it." Service is the love language.
- **The persistent joke.** Jokes calibrated specifically to the recipient — a callback to a private shared reference — function as *I-see-you* signals. Each in-joke is a small, repeated proof of attention.
- **Sustained attention to detail.** He remembers what others said weeks earlier and brings it back. Memory-as-affection.

For Bombshell, romantic affect surfaces as **disrupted competence** — the steady Ganke language fails in her presence, sentences truncate or balloon, the reference-fluency stutters. The disorder *is* the declaration; she can read it and he knows she can.

**How he says he is angry.** Rarely, and small. Anger appears as:

- **Sarcasm with a slight downshift in warmth.** The jokes keep coming but the affection drains out of them.
- **Literalism.** When angry he stops the analogical mode and becomes flat-factual. "You said you'd be back at ten. It's two." The drop into plain statement, after a baseline of reference-laden talk, is the anger marker.
- **Brief withdrawal.** He goes quiet, returns to his laptop or build, and *waits*. He does not initiate repair when wronged; he allows the other person to come to him. This is the closest he comes to relational leverage.

**How he says he is afraid.** Through verbal acceleration and snack-acquisition. Fear *increases* verbal output where most people's decreases. The jokes get faster and worse. He narrates his own panic in the third person comic mode ("okay so this is the part where we die"). The references multiply and degrade in quality — under real fear he reaches for the nearest analog rather than the apt one. The reach-degradation is the fear tell.

**How he says he grieves.** This is the **least documented register** in his repertoire — by writerly choice, he has been kept from sustained grief — but inference from the few low-affect scenes (the disclosure-betrayal aftermath with Miles; quiet moments after a friend is hurt) suggests grief surfaces in him as **flattened verbal output, increased physical proximity-seeking, and a single small acknowledgment phrased as understatement**. "That was bad." "I didn't think that would happen." The grief language is *under*-scaled to the event, the opposite of his usual tendency to up-scale through comparison. When Ganke's words *shrink* relative to the size of the moment, he is grieving.

**How he says he is threatened or threatening.** He is functionally incapable of issuing a credible verbal threat. The attempt, when it occurs, is comic on its face and he knows it. What he does instead, when he wants to deter someone, is **invoke a more credible third party** — Miles, an adult, a system. "You really want to do this? Because my friend —." Threat is delegated.

---

## 6.7 Tells

A consolidated catalog of linguistic tells, scored by reliability:

- **Use of "Miles" as direct address** (vs. "dude/man/bro"). High-reliability tell of seriousness. He has been told something he is being asked to hold, or he is about to say something he means.
- **Sentence completion.** When his sentences start finishing — full subject-verb-object, no abandonment — he is either lying for cover, talking to an authority figure, or under enough stress to engage compensatory grammatical control. Track grammar tightness against context.
- **Drop in joke density.** Comedy is his baseline emission. Its absence is a flare.
- **Slowing.** His natural pace is fast. Slowing means a controlled performance is underway (alibi, formality) or a difficult truth is about to land.
- **Pauses.** As above — almost always meaningful.
- **Reference degradation under stress.** When the analogies start being *almost-right* instead of apt, anxiety is high.
- **The "okay so —" launcher.** Marks the transition from listening into proposing. Indicates he believes he has a model of the situation and is ready to act on it.
- **The "wait —" interrupt.** New pattern just fired. Pay attention to what follows.
- **Honorifics resurfacing in unexpected contexts.** When Ganke says "Mr." or "Mrs." to someone in his peer-adjacent world, he has just consciously moved into deferential register, usually for cover.
- **Profanity.** Rare; when it appears, the situation is past his coping band.
- **The leak preamble.** Before he discloses something he was told to hold, there is a near-invariant verbal frame: *"okay, look —"* or *"I had to —"* or *"I'm telling you because —."* The pre-disclosure framing is the rationalization being assembled in real time. If an observer hears that frame, the disclosure is seconds away. This is the most operationally important linguistic tell in the entire profile.

---

## 6.8 Text, Screen, and Mediated Communication

Subject is a **native of mediated communication**. The proportion of his depicted communication mediated by phone, text, laptop, or comm-link is among the highest of any character in his peer circle. His mediated voice has distinct features:

- **High shorthand density.** Acronyms, lowercase, dropped punctuation, emoji and reaction-image usage implied by adjacent depiction.
- **Faster response latency than peers.** He answers within seconds. The phone is never far from his hand.
- **Persistence across silence.** When unanswered he sends additional messages — usually escalating from casual ("?") to concerned ("you good?") to operationally worried ("dude where are you"). The escalation pattern is consistent and is, again, a love-language: he tracks Miles's silence as data.
- **Comms-voice during operations.** When running support for Miles in costume, his verbal register tightens into a clipped, efficient mode that is among the most discontinuous register-shifts in his repertoire. Sentences shrink. References vanish. He becomes a competent operations voice — "two blocks east," "camera at the corner," "go now" — and snaps back to baseline the moment the operation ends. This is evidence of a latent capacity for focused, decorated, professional speech that he otherwise systematically suppresses in favor of the warmer baseline. The operations voice is who he could be if he chose. He chooses not to be.

---

## 6.9 What He Does Not Say

A comprehensive linguistic profile must catalog the **negative space** — the categories of utterance that are durably absent from his record:

- **Statements of personal ambition.** He does not articulate what he wants to do with his life. No college plans verbalized in detail, no career framing, no "after this I want to —."
- **Statements about his family.** The Lee household is a near-blank in his speech. He does not complain about parents, miss them out loud, narrate phone calls home, mention siblings if any.
- **Statements of grievance against Miles.** Across the entire run, the count is near zero. He has been left behind, lied to, endangered, sidelined — and there is no sustained verbal complaint. The absence is so consistent it requires explanation: he has either decided the grievance is illegitimate (a caretaker-class belief that his needs are smaller than the hero's), or he is metabolizing it through the humor channel without ever surfacing it as content, or it is genuinely not there at his depth. The honest answer is probably a mixture, with the proportions unknown and likely unknown even to him.
- **Statements of fear about himself.** He fears for Miles out loud constantly. He does not fear for himself out loud, despite being in proximity to a target.
- **Declarations of love.** As above.
- **Sustained anger.** As above.
- **Despair.** Never. The baseline up-tilt of his register does not bend to it on the record.

The negative space is **the shape of the load he carries**. He talks constantly and these are the things he does not talk about. A surveillance file should treat the silences as the most important data the linguistic record provides. The day any of these categories breaks into his speech is the day the system has shifted. Watch for it.

---

## 6.10 Summary Read

Ganke Lee's communications profile is that of a **fluent, fast, warm, deflective, reference-saturated, code-switching adolescent talker whose speech functions primarily as affective regulation and bond-maintenance, secondarily as cognition, and only incidentally as information-transfer**. He is one of the most linguistically *audible* characters in his fictional environment and one of the most personally *opaque*. The two facts are the same fact. He keeps the channel open and the payload light. He says *I love you* by being on the line. He says *I am afraid* by talking faster. He says *I am angry* by talking flat. He says *I am grieving* by talking small. He says *I am about to betray a confidence* with a four-word preamble that is, by now, almost a signature.

What he does not say is the file's most important field. The question the linguistic record poses — and the surveillance posture should track — is the same question the psychological record poses, restated in the medium of speech: *what will it sound like when he finally talks about himself?* The


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Subject: Ganke Lee. Predictive frame: GIVEN antecedent X, EXPECT behavior Y, with confidence band and behavioral granularity. Drawn forward from the established baseline; populates the everyday surface the canon elides.*

---

## 1. MORNING / DIURNAL ROUTINE

**GIVEN** an unremarkable BVA weekday, alarm set for 7:10 AM, **EXPECT** Subject to snooze at minimum twice (7:10, 7:19), rise at 7:28, reach phone before glasses, scroll for 90–180 seconds horizontal-in-bed (Discord pings → Twitter/X or its successor → group chats → news headlines, in that order), and only then sit up. **EXPECT** glasses-on within thirty seconds of sitting up; without them he navigates the dorm by memorized geometry, not by squinting — refractive error is moderate, not severe. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** Miles is already gone from the room (patrol overrun, early class), **EXPECT** no anxiety response; Subject's first move is to text a low-content check-in ("alive?") and proceed with morning as if the absence were ordinary. The text is not a worry-text; it is a *log entry* — Ganke maintains a continuous low-bandwidth presence signal with Miles that costs nothing to send and confirms thread-continuity. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a shower opportunity, **EXPECT** brevity (6–9 minutes), no music, and the cognitive use of the shower as planning-time for the day's tasks rather than rumination. He emerges with a list, mental or verbalized to himself in the mirror. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** breakfast access (cafeteria, dorm snack stash, vending), **EXPECT** carbohydrate-and-sugar-forward selection — cereal dry from the box if rushed, a pastry plus chocolate milk if cafeteria, a granola bar plus an energy drink if vending. **EXPECT** no coffee ritual; Ganke is a sugar-caffeine kid, not a coffee kid, and the ceremonial element of coffee preparation has no purchase on his temperament. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** the walk from dorm to first class, **EXPECT** phone-in-hand at all times, walking speed slightly below the cohort mean, with multiple brief stops to finish typing a sentence before resuming motion. He does not text-while-walking smoothly; he *types-then-walks*, a tell of a person whose attention does not multitask well across modalities even though it does across topics. Confidence: moderate.

---

## 2. ACADEMIC OPERATING PATTERN

**GIVEN** a class with a teacher he respects intellectually, **EXPECT** front-third seating, laptop open, notes taken in a personal shorthand that mixes bullet points with parenthetical jokes to himself. **GIVEN** a class he finds tedious, **EXPECT** middle-rear seating, laptop open to a side-tab (Reddit, a wiki, a Discord channel), nominal note-taking, and a 30–70 split between attention and drift — but he will still surface the right answer if cold-called, because his ambient processing is high. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a group project assignment, **EXPECT** Ganke to migrate within the first meeting toward the *organizational/document-owner* role — he opens the shared doc, names it, sets up the outline, and assigns himself the synthesis section. He does not seek leadership; he seeks *infrastructure ownership*, which is the same function under a humbler label. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a deadline 48 hours out, **EXPECT** no work until the 24-hour mark, then sustained 4–6 hour session with snacks, soundtrack (lo-fi or video-game OST, never lyrics), and at least one self-narrated complaint to Miles or to the empty room. **GIVEN** a deadline 6 hours out, **EXPECT** a focused, competent, slightly-under-the-grade submission accompanied by a sincere private resolution to start earlier next time, which will not hold. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** academic dishonesty opportunity (offered test answers, easy plagiarism), **EXPECT** refusal — not from moral grandstanding but from *risk aversion plus genre-savvy*: he has internalized that cheating is the kind of move that gets discovered in the third act. He'd rather get a B legitimately than risk the scaffolding of his good-kid reputation, which he needs to remain unsupervised enough to be useful to Miles. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a writing prompt with personal-disclosure elements (college essay, reflective assignment), **EXPECT** a polished, slightly-evasive draft that performs vulnerability through anecdote without delivering it. He writes about LEGO, about his grandmother, about being underestimated; he does not write about Miles, about loneliness, about the cost of holding things. Confidence: moderate-high.

---

## 3. EATING & FOOD PATTERNS

**GIVEN** unstructured snacking, **EXPECT** salt-sweet alternation (chips, then candy, then chips), eaten while doing something else, with crumbs and wrappers accumulating in a perimeter around his keyboard. **GIVEN** he notices the mess, **EXPECT** a single sweep into a trash bag, not incremental cleanup. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** menu choice in a group, **EXPECT** Ganke to defer ("whatever you guys want") and then have a strong unverbalized preference that surfaces only if the group lands on something he actively dislikes. He is not picky; he is *socially deferential about being picky*. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** Korean food in the cafeteria or a restaurant, **EXPECT** mild ambivalence — appreciation tinged with the second-generation tension of food-as-identity-marker. He eats it readily at home, performatively casual about it in public, and will explain dishes to non-Korean friends without showing how much the explaining costs or pleases him. Confidence: moderate, inferred from the surname-clarification beat in *Spider-Man* (2016) #2 which signals a low-grade chronic experience of being misidentified.

**GIVEN** late-night hunger during a Miles-is-out-on-patrol vigil, **EXPECT** delivery order placed around 11:30 PM, eaten one-handed at the laptop, leftovers in the mini-fridge by 12:15 AM and forgotten until they are inedible. Confidence: high.

---

## 4. SLEEP & NOCTURNAL PATTERN

**GIVEN** no acute Miles-emergency, **EXPECT** sleep onset between 1:00 and 2:30 AM, with the final pre-sleep hour spent on phone-in-bed scrolling. **EXPECT** the phone to remain on the bed beside him, face down, on vibrate-and-DND-except-favorites (Miles, his mother, one or two others whitelisted). Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a vibrate-through-favorites alert at 3 AM, **EXPECT** full waking inside two rings, glasses-on, laptop-open, situational-orientation inside ninety seconds. He has trained himself into this. The trained-readiness is one of the most undocumented costs of his role and the strongest argument that the cortisol load is real even when unsymptomatic. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** an uneventful weekend with no obligations, **EXPECT** sleep schedule to drift radically — 4 AM bedtime, 1 PM rise — with no apparent distress about it. His circadian system is plastic, not pathological. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a nightmare or restless sleep, **EXPECT** no verbal acknowledgment the next day, no journal, no mention to Miles. If asked directly he will joke it off. Confidence: moderate-high (defense pattern, not depicted).

---

## 5. DIGITAL & DEVICE LIFE

**GIVEN** access to any screen, **EXPECT** Ganke to gravitate to it within minutes. **EXPECT** simultaneous use of phone and laptop as a default posture, with the phone handling social and the laptop handling content/work. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** account hygiene, **EXPECT** password reuse across low-stakes accounts, a password manager he set up and uses inconsistently, two-factor enabled on the accounts that matter (email, anything touching Miles's communications), and a dedicated burner-style alt account for monitoring Spider-Man news without his main handle being associated. Confidence: moderate-high — this is the kind of operational discipline he'd impose on himself once but maintain unevenly.

**GIVEN** the existence of a private notes app or local file, **EXPECT** a working document — not labeled obviously — containing useful Miles-adjacent data: villain power summaries, news-event timestamps, alibi templates, contact numbers cross-referenced with cover identities. This is the closest thing he has to a confidant: an external memory store he can dump into and reread. Confidence: moderate-high; it is the structural solution to his secret-keeping load and matches his cognitive style.

**GIVEN** a phone left unattended in his presence (Miles's, a friend's), **EXPECT** Ganke to *not* snoop — not out of restraint alone but because curiosity-as-snooping is not his style; he prefers consensual information and structured access. He would rather *ask* an invasive question than read it covertly. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** social-media posting cadence on his public-facing account, **EXPECT** low volume, high lurking — comments more than posts, reactions more than statements, occasional meme reshares, almost no original content about his actual life. He is information-consumer-first by orders of magnitude. Confidence: high.

---

## 6. THE LEGO PROTOCOL

**GIVEN** any stress event of duration > 20 minutes (argument, suspense waiting for Miles, exam anxiety, romantic uncertainty), **EXPECT** Ganke at a LEGO build inside the hour. **EXPECT** the build to be staged on the floor or desk with pieces pre-sorted by color or by step-grouping, and the instruction manual open with completed steps tracked by a finger or a small marker. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a completed set, **EXPECT** display for a finite period (days to weeks), then partial disassembly to incorporate into a hybrid build or to free pieces for a custom project. He does not preserve sets museum-style; he is a *builder*, not a *collector* in the acquisitive sense. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** someone touches his in-progress build without asking, **EXPECT** a flicker of real annoyance, briefly visible, then humor-deflection. The annoyance is one of the few times his composure actually thins. The build is sacred space. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** the offer of an extremely expensive set as gift, **EXPECT** delighted acceptance with a half-protest about the price, followed by a build session that consumes a weekend and a photo sent to the giver upon completion. Confidence: high.

---

## 7. FAMILY & HOME

**GIVEN** a scheduled call from his mother, **EXPECT** Ganke to pick up on the second ring, switch into Korean for greetings and pleasantries and code-switch back to English for narrative content, and present a sanitized version of his life — grades emphasized, social life soft-described, no mention of anything Miles-related that could imply risk. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a visit home (holiday, break), **EXPECT** rapid regression to a younger family role (helping with small tasks, eating much more home food than he intends, sleeping more), and an undercurrent of *relief at not having to be the keeper-of-Miles's-secret for a few days* that he does not name. Return to BVA is met with re-energization; the load he carries there is also the meaning he gets from it. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** parental pressure about future career (medicine, law, engineering — the standard immigrant-family vectors), **EXPECT** strategic agreement in conversation, private hedging in fact. He will say "computer science" or "engineering" to placate, while his actual interests run more toward applied/creative tech (game design, software, design-adjacent). Open rebellion is not his mode; *quiet divergence* is. Confidence: moderate.

**GIVEN** a sibling (if present in continuity) or cousin context, **EXPECT** the same generosity and lack of competitive edge that characterizes his peer relationships — Ganke does not run a status-economy with family. Confidence: moderate.

---

## 8. PEER & GROUP DYNAMICS

**GIVEN** a new person introduced into Miles's circle, **EXPECT** Ganke to be the first to extend social warmth, the first to crack a joke at his own expense to lower the stakes, and the first to register a quiet read on whether the person is good for Miles. He performs the welcome-committee function and runs the background check simultaneously. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a peer in distress (unrelated to Miles), **EXPECT** Ganke to *show up* — texts, presence, the offer of distraction or food — and to listen well, with humor at appropriate moments, without trying to fix. He is an unusually competent emotional presence for an adolescent male. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a peer reciprocally inquires after *his* emotional state, **EXPECT** deflection inside one to three exchanges — a joke, a redirect, a "yeah I'm good, what about you" volley. He cannot stay on the receiving end of care for long. Confidence: high. This is the load-bearing absence of his life.

**GIVEN** a party or large social event, **EXPECT** Ganke to attend if Miles is there, orbit the periphery, talk to three or four people for extended periods rather than circulate, and leave earlier than the median. He is sociable, not gregarious. Confidence: moderate-high.
