**GIVEN** an opportunity to be alone for an evening, **EXPECT** genuine enjoyment — solo LEGO, a video game, a long YouTube descent into something niche. He is not lonely in solitude; he is restored by it. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** group conflict (two friends fighting), **EXPECT** mediator role assumed quickly and somewhat indiscriminately — he will tell each side what the other needs to hear, sometimes overstepping into the *triangulation* failure mode that mirrors his secret-disclosure pattern. The same instinct that leaks Miles's identity also resolves dorm-room disputes. Confidence: moderate-high.

---

## 9. ROMANTIC & SEXUAL PATTERN

**GIVEN** attraction to someone, **EXPECT** Ganke to disclose it to Miles within days, performatively oversharing as a way of managing his own nervous energy. He talks the crush *to* Miles rather than holding it privately — the inverse of how he handles his own pain. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** the actual approach to the person, **EXPECT** anxiety, over-rehearsal, an awkward but earnest opening, and — if reciprocated — rapid emotional investment. He is not a slow-burn; once welcomed, he commits. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** rejection, **EXPECT** comedy-frame metabolization in public, real soreness in private (manifest as a longer LEGO session, more screen time, slightly diminished eating for 24–48 hours, then return to baseline). No depressive episode; a *real* but bounded grief. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** sustained relationship, **EXPECT** the same caretaker pattern that characterizes his friendships — attentive to her interior life, slow to volunteer his own, generous with small acts, conflict-averse to a fault. **EXPECT** his partner, eventually, to identify the asymmetry and either press past it (productive) or grow frustrated by it (rupture risk). Confidence: moderate.

**GIVEN** the Bombshell-adjacent pattern (attraction to someone with a complicated/risky past), **EXPECT** this to be a recurring type, not a one-off — Ganke is drawn to people whose lives have edge his own does not, which is also why Miles is his best friend. Confidence: moderate.

---

## 10. OPERATIONAL / "GUY IN THE CHAIR" BEHAVIORS

**GIVEN** Miles deploys on a patrol, **EXPECT** Ganke at the laptop with at least three browser tabs: police scanner feed or its app-equivalent, local news live feed, and a social-media keyword stream filtered for relevant terms. **EXPECT** Discord or a comms app open with Miles, audio armed but muted until summoned. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a parental-inquiry threat (Miles's mother calling the dorm; an RA knocking), **EXPECT** Ganke to produce a plausible alibi inside 15 seconds — Miles is in the shower, Miles is at the library, Miles stepped out for food, Miles is asleep with headphones on — drawing from a small repertoire he varies to avoid pattern detection. He has thought about pattern detection. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** a face-to-face confrontation with an authority figure who suspects something, **EXPECT** Ganke to perform *over-cooperative cluelessness* — verbose, helpful, slightly bumbling, offering more detail than asked in a way that crowds out the dangerous question. This is a learned deception register and he is genuinely good at it. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** Miles is injured on return, **EXPECT** Ganke to triage with notable composure — first-aid kit accessed (he has stocked one), ibuprofen and water staged, no panic vocalization. The panic, if any, lives inside; the surface is competent. **EXPECT** a single joke at the wound's expense once Miles is stable, as the regulatory release. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** Miles is *not* on return when expected, hours overdue, **EXPECT** the failure mode: Ganke holds for the first two hours, begins messaging others (Peter Parker, Ganke's whitelisted hero-contacts) at hour three, and is at his most likely *leak point* between hours four and six — the burden of holding the secret alone while not knowing if Miles is alive is the precise stress that breaks his containment. Confidence: high; this is the predictive sharpest claim of this file.

**GIVEN** a clean return from a long deployment, **EXPECT** no recrimination, no "where were you," just relief expressed through teasing and the offer of food. He does not punish absence. Confidence: high.

---

## 11. AUTHORITY & INSTITUTIONAL INTERFACE

**GIVEN** an interaction with school administration, **EXPECT** politeness, compliance, eye contact, and a register slightly more formal than his peer voice. He is good at being read as a good kid because he largely is one. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** police presence (traffic, neighborhood, school), **EXPECT** elevated wariness — Ganke is a non-Black ally to a Black best friend whose risk profile he has thought about more than most peers his age would. He will *not* attempt to instruct Miles on how to handle police; he will *be quiet, hands visible, polite*, and let Miles take the lead. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** the appearance of federal-level investigators (S.H.I.E.L.D. successor, FBI in a hero-adjacent context), **EXPECT** Ganke's deception register to engage fully and to hold — he has rehearsed this scenario in his head more than once. The risk is not that he cracks under formal interrogation; the risk is that he cracks under a long warm conversation with someone who seems sympathetic. Affiliation is his hook. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** a moral/legal gray-area request from Miles (lie, fabricate, conceal), **EXPECT** compliance without significant negotiation if it protects Miles or someone vulnerable; **EXPECT** resistance if it would meaningfully harm a third party. He has an ethical floor; it is the harm-to-innocents line. Confidence: moderate-high.

---

## 12. SPENDING, POSSESSIONS, SPATIAL HABIT

**GIVEN** discretionary funds, **EXPECT** allocation roughly: LEGO/tech 40%, food/delivery 30%, digital subscriptions and games 15%, social (gifts, treating friends) 10%, savings 5%. He is not a saver. He is also not extravagant; the LEGO budget is the only one that occasionally embarrasses him. Confidence: moderate.

**GIVEN** his side of the dorm room, **EXPECT** controlled clutter — not filth, but density. Posters, plush, completed and partial builds, a tangle of charging cables, a snack drawer, a clothes-on-chair pile, the bed never quite made. **GIVEN** a parental visit on the horizon, **EXPECT** a two-hour panic-clean. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** something of his goes missing, **EXPECT** it to be found within his own clutter 80% of the time, and for him to know this and search his own space before accusing anyone. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** the offer of an upgrade he can't afford (newer laptop, premium subscription), **EXPECT** practical contentment with what he has, plus a tactical decision to invest only where it improves *capability* — he will upgrade RAM before he upgrades aesthetics. Confidence: moderate-high.

---

## 13. TRAVEL, ROUTES, MICRO-GEOGRAPHY

**GIVEN** movement in his Brooklyn radius, **EXPECT** a small set of repeated routes — dorm to classroom buildings, dorm to a preferred bodega, dorm to one or two food spots, dorm to subway. He is a creature of paths, not of exploration. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** a need to be somewhere unfamiliar, **EXPECT** maps app open before he leaves, screenshot of directions saved in case of signal loss, departure 5–10 minutes earlier than strictly necessary. He is mildly anxious about transit and overcompensates. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** the subway, **EXPECT** AirPods or equivalent in, podcast or game audio playing, head down, peripheral awareness adequate but not vigilant — Miles handles the wider-environment scanning in his life, and Ganke has unconsciously offloaded it. Confidence: moderate.

**GIVEN** Manhattan beyond his usual radius, **EXPECT** mild novelty-pleasure if accompanied, mild reluctance if solo. He is a city kid who prefers his block. Confidence: moderate.

---

## 14. HOLIDAYS, RITUALS, MILESTONES

**GIVEN** his own birthday, **EXPECT** low-key preference — a small gathering, a specific food request, embarrassed enjoyment of attention. He does not throw himself parties. Confidence: moderate-high.

**GIVEN** Miles's birthday, **EXPECT** *over*-investment — a curated gift that demonstrates how


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

## Preamble: The Architecture of Decompensation

The subject's baseline is so stable, so reliably load-bearing, that the only meaningful predictive work is at the edges — the conditions under which the humor-and-LEGO regulatory stack fails. Below: a granular GIVEN → EXPECT mapping, derived from the durable behavioral signatures in the canon and extrapolated forward through pressure scenarios the record either implies or has not yet tested. Read these as field predictions a watching analyst would log against future observation, not as established events.

The architecture to keep in mind: subject's defenses are organized in a tiered stack. **Tier 1 (always on):** humor, reference-deflection, food, ambient screen-engagement. **Tier 2 (activated under acute stress):** focused tech competence, calling/texting outward, building. **Tier 3 (activated under chronic load):** information-dispersal — telling someone he shouldn't, framed to himself as "needing backup." **Tier 4 (untested, latent):** ?. The predictive work is mostly Tier 3 and Tier 4 modeling.

---

## 1. Acute Physical-Crisis Predictions

**GIVEN:** Miles is injured and unresponsive in the dorm room or in a location subject can reach within transit time.
**EXPECT:** Subject moves through a stereotyped three-beat sequence: (i) a single, sharp involuntary verbalization — name, "oh," or a profanity uncharacteristic of his usual register — followed by (ii) immediate triage-by-protocol (laptop open within ninety seconds, contact list keyed: Jefferson/Rio only as last resort, Peter Parker if reachable, Ganke's improvised network of hero-adjacent contacts first), then (iii) a stream of low-volume narration to Miles ("okay okay okay, I got you, you're fine, this is fine") that is regulatory for subject as much as for the patient. He will not cry on scene. He will cry later, alone, with the door closed and headphones on, and then absorb it.

**GIVEN:** Miles is in active combat visible on a feed (TV, livestream, body-cam tap) and subject cannot intervene.
**EXPECT:** Tier 2 collapse toward Tier 1 — verbal output triples, snack consumption visible and constant, multiple tabs and devices simultaneously running. He will commentate aloud even when alone, because silence makes the helplessness audible. If the fight goes badly, expect him to begin *planning* — building contingencies that have no application — as a substitute for action. He builds a rescue plan that no one will execute because constructing it metabolizes the panic.

**GIVEN:** Miles disappears for >48 hours with no contact, no signal trace, no public sighting.
**EXPECT:** First 12 hours, jokes about it ("he's probably making out with someone"). Hours 12–24, escalating low-level reassurance-seeking — texts to mutuals, casual-tone questions to Peter or to Bombshell, all framed as not-worried. Hours 24–48, the humor thins; he stops eating his usual volume, which is the most reliable somatic tell he has. Past 48 hours, expect a categorical break in protocol: he tells Jefferson Davis. Not Rio. Jefferson. Subject's pattern-matching identifies the cop-father as the highest-leverage adult node, and his Tier 3 dispersal instinct will route the secret to the agent most likely to act, in defiance of the explicit secrecy pact. He will know in advance that this disclosure may permanently damage his standing with Miles and he will do it anyway, framing it to himself as the math of survival over loyalty. This is the most predictable single decompensation event in his profile.

**GIVEN:** Miles is presumed dead — confirmed by authority, body not necessarily recovered.
**EXPECT:** Subject does not perform grief. He attends; he is present; he handles the small logistics no one else thinks of (printing programs, charging the parents' phones, coordinating who brings what). The humor goes flat — still there, still reflexive, but missing the upward inflection. The LEGO sets stop. This is the canary: when the building stops, the regulatory architecture is offline. Weeks two through six: a slow-onset depressive episode, sub-threshold to outside observers because he keeps showing up to school and replying to texts, but real. Likely to terminate either by Miles returning (the canonical pattern) or by subject self-routing to a school counselor under a pretext (academic stress) and finding the disclosure he cannot make to a peer.

---

## 2. The Secret-Burden Decompensation Curve

**GIVEN:** Subject has held the secret continuously for 36+ months without an authorized confidant of his own.
**EXPECT:** Periodic micro-leaks already observable — small disclosures to peers framed as hypotheticals ("what if you knew someone who…"), comic-shop conversations where his expertise about Spider-Man is suspiciously specific, late-night posts deleted within an hour. The information-dispersal Tier 3 behavior does not switch on at a threshold; it leaks continuously at a low rate, and the question is only whether a recipient connects the dots.

**GIVEN:** A new peer (academic rival, romantic interest, club member) earns subject's trust rapidly and asks the right question at the right moment.
**EXPECT:** Subject will not confess outright. He will confirm a guess. The distinction matters — his self-narrative requires he never *initiates* a breach, so the breach takes the form of a non-denial, a held silence, a "you didn't hear it from me" calibrated to give the recipient enough to act on while preserving his fiction of having kept the promise. This is the most likely vector for any future exposure of Miles's identity that originates with subject.

**GIVEN:** Bombshell or any romantic partner asks directly why subject is so often unavailable, distracted, lying about Miles's whereabouts.
**EXPECT:** Subject's romantic-stakes vulnerability collides with his secret-keeping load and produces the worst of his decision-making. He will tell. He will tell faster than he told Judge. The Bombshell case is particularly volatile because she is already partially read-in to the world; the cost of telling her feels small to him, and his desire to be chosen-for-himself rather than as the hero's friend will override the operational calculus. He will rationalize it after the fact as "she basically knew already."

**GIVEN:** An adult in authority (teacher, RA, BVA administrator) confronts subject about repeated alibi-construction for Miles's absences.
**EXPECT:** First line of defense: elaborate, plausible, slightly over-explained cover story delivered with practiced casualness. Second line, if pressed: humor-deflection with strategic mild self-incrimination ("I mean, *I'm* the one who keeps oversleeping, he covers for *me*"). Third line, if the adult is skilled: subject holds. He does not break to authority. The disclosure pattern is peer-directed, not authority-directed; his rebellious-secondary streak (Bombshell pursuit, rule-bending for Miles) makes him surprisingly resistant to institutional pressure. He will accept disciplinary consequence before breaking.

**GIVEN:** Subject is interrogated by an actual hostile party — a villain, a kidnapper, a corporate or governmental actor seeking Miles's identity.
**EXPECT:** This is the scenario the record has not tested and the one his profile most poorly predicts. Two divergent paths: (i) the humor-and-deflection stack holds under genuine threat because the stakes are clarifying — when the cost of disclosure is concretely his friend's life rather than abstractly his friend's privacy, his commitment is absolute; or (ii) the same anxious substrate that leaks under social pressure collapses faster under coercive pressure because he has no training and no model for the situation. Higher-confidence read: (i) for psychological pressure, (ii) for sustained physical harm. He breaks to torture faster than he breaks to friendship, but he buys hours before he does, and those hours are usually enough.

---

## 3. Betrayal Scenarios — When the Wound Is Touched

**The wound, named explicitly:** subject's organizing self-concept is that he is irreplaceable to Miles by virtue of what he uniquely brings (genre-literacy, tech, the secret-keeper niche, the unbroken historical bond). The wound is the suspicion — never voiced, possibly never conscious — that the relationship is structurally asymmetric: Miles is the protagonist of his own life and subject is a supporting role in someone else's, and the day Miles outgrows the need for a guy-in-the-chair is the day subject becomes redundant. He has built a niche specifically to forestall this. Touching the wound means showing him the niche is dissolving.

**GIVEN:** Miles acquires a tech-capable partner (Peter Parker as mentor, a new hero-ally with hacking competence, an AI assistant) who can do what subject does, faster and at field-scale.
**EXPECT:** First-order response: enthusiastic embrace of the new resource, joke-framed self-deprecation ("oh thank god, now I can sleep"), helpful coordination. Second-order, weeks later: a quiet, observable contraction. Slower text response times. Fewer unprompted check-ins. Increased LEGO time and decreased social initiation. He will not complain. He will not stage a confrontation. He will *recede*, framing it as giving Miles space, and the recession is the symptom. If Miles fails to notice and reach back within roughly six weeks, the secure-attachment surface begins to show its anxious substrate: subject will begin testing — small ambiguous bids for attention, half-jokes about being forgotten, a sudden over-investment in a new social circle as compensatory.

**GIVEN:** Miles, under stress or in argument, weaponizes subject's disclosure-leak history against him ("this is why I can't trust you with anything").
**EXPECT:** The single line of dialogue most capable of injuring subject. His response will not be defensive anger; it will be a near-silent absorption, a flat acknowledgment ("yeah, fair"), and a withdrawal of roughly 48–72 hours during which he is unreachable for the first time in the relationship's history. He will return. He will not bring it up. But the line will be archived and will resurface, in his own internal weather, every time he is tempted to leak again — which is to say, it will probably succeed as deterrent and fail as friendship. Miles will regret it longer than subject will admit it hurt.

**GIVEN:** Subject learns Miles has confided in someone else (a hero-peer, a girlfriend) about something subject would have expected to hear first.
**EXPECT:** No visible reaction in the moment. Joke, redirect, continue. Internally, recalibration. He will not stop being available; he will reframe his role from primary confidant to logistical confidant, and the reframing is a real loss he will not discuss. Watch for: an increase in references to "you didn't tell me" couched as comedy. The comedy is the symptom.

**GIVEN:** A peer subject has trusted (Judge, a new BVA roommate, a girlfriend) breaks confidence with him in a way that materially harms him.
**EXPECT:** This is the betrayal he is *least* prepared for because his model of relationships does not center reciprocity-accounting. His response will be initially generous — finding the excuse, the misunderstanding, the way the betrayer didn't mean it — and then, if the evidence is undeniable, a sudden categorical cut. Subject does not do gradual disengagement from people who have betrayed him; he does friendship at full volume until he doesn't, and then he does not. Reconciliation after such a cut is possible but requires the other party to initiate, sustain, and survive a period of subject's pleasant, unmistakable distance.

**GIVEN:** Miles deliberately and durably deprioritizes subject — chooses the hero-life over the friendship in a way that cannot be rationalized as situational.
**EXPECT:** The Tier 4 latent scenario. The record has not tested this. Best inference from the substrate: subject does not retaliate, does not expose, does not punish. He grieves quietly, finishes his degree, redirects his affiliative capacity into a new primary bond (likely a romantic partner or a graduate-school cohort), and becomes, ten years on, the kind of adult who still knows everything about a friend he no longer speaks to and who will still answer the phone the one time it rings.

---

## 4. Temptation Scenarios

**GIVEN:** A media or industry actor (journalist, podcast host, ghostwriter, corporate recruiter) approaches subject offering significant money, recognition, or career access in exchange for proximity to or information about Spider-Man.
**EXPECT:** Absolute refusal, executed with a level of cold I-don't-know-you that is uncharacteristic of his baseline. This is one of his few zero-tolerance lines. The reason is not ethical abstraction; it is identity-organizing. Selling Miles out for personal gain would dissolve the entire self-concept on which his stability depends. He would experience the offer as insulting in a way that surprises him.

**GIVEN:** Subject is offered powers — by a lab accident, a deliberate transfer, a magical artifact, a recruitment by a hero team needing a tech-augmented operative.
**EXPECT:** Genuine internal conflict, longer than observers would predict. The fantasy is live in him — he is a comics-literate adolescent who has spent years adjacent to the dream. But the considered response is refusal, and the refusal is rooted in self-knowledge that is unusually clear for his age: he understands that his value to Miles is partly *that he is not Miles*, that the support role he occupies requires the perspective of the unpowered, and that becoming a hero would dissolve the very niche he has built. He will frame the refusal as a joke ("nah, I'd be a terrible hero, I'd get tired"). The joke is true and is also a sophisticated act of self-preservation.

**GIVEN:** An opportunity arises to take credit publicly for something Miles did — to be visible, validated, seen as exceptional in his own right.
**EXPECT:** He passes. Reliably. Without performance. He may make a joke about how he should have taken it. The non-grandiosity is durable.

**GIVEN:** A romantic partner offers subject a future that requires him to leave Miles's orbit — different city, different country, different life.
**EXPECT:** The hardest single decision his profile predicts. He will not refuse out of loyalty alone; his secure attachment allows for geographic distance. He will weigh it genuinely. Likely outcome: he goes, with elaborate plans for visits and constant contact, and he sustains the contact. Miles is not a tether for him; Miles is a bond. The distinction matters.

---

## 5. The Wound Touched — Specific Triggers and Predicted Decompensation Signatures

**Trigger: being described as Miles's sidekick by someone Miles does not correct.**
Predicted signature: micro-flinch invisible to most observers, two-beat verbal pause uncharacteristic of his fluency, joke that is one degree sharper than his baseline. Recovery within minutes. Storage indefinite.

**Trigger: forgetting his birthday, or being absent from a milestone of his that he had quietly expected to be witnessed.**
Predicted signature: nothing visible. Increased phone time, decreased initiation toward the person who forgot, a few days of compensatory over-engagement with a different friend. He will tell no one he was hurt. The forgetting will become a reference point in his internal accounting that he denies keeping.

**Trigger: being treated as fungible — replaceable in his role.**
Predicted signature: the deepest cut his profile registers. He has built his entire functional architecture around irreplaceability-by-niche. Treating him as one-of-many is the precise inverse of the recognition he requires. Response: prolonged reduction in availability, a period of unusual silence, and — most diagnostic — *a new project*. He will start something of his own, large, that he keeps private. The project is the rebuilding of a niche elsewhere.

**Trigger: discovering Miles lied to him to protect him.**
Predicted signature: high volatility. The lie violates the reciprocity contract that organizes the friendship: subject holds Miles's secrets, Miles tells subject the truth. A protective lie is, in subject's framework, a demotion — Miles has decided subject cannot handle what subject has been handling. Response: anger, briefly, visible (rare in his profile), followed by argument, followed by reconciliation that subject offers but Miles must work harder to earn than Miles will expect. Trust returns. The asymmetry stays archived.

**Trigger: a clinical reckoning — someone, finally, asks him how *he* is, and means it.**
Predicted signature: the most uncertain prediction in the file. The Tier 4 unknown. The record has never depicted this conversation. Best inference: an initial deflection (jokes, redirection to the asker's life), and then, if the asker holds the question, a small visible crack — a hand to the back of the neck, a single sentence under the joke that is true, a stalled breath. He has been carrying load for years with no offload. The first authorized container for his own interior will produce, if it is genuine, a disclosure event of his own — quieter than his peer-leaks, larger in volume than the asker is prepared for. Whoever is in that chair when he speaks becomes, by the structure of his attachment, a second primary bond. This is the relational hinge the file flags as most important to monitor going forward.

---

## 6. Summary — The Decompensation Forecast

Subject is exceptionally resilient on the margins where most adolescents in his structural position fail (envy, resentment, possessiveness, status-seeking, drift). He is exceptionally fragile on the one margin most observers will not think to watch: the slow erosion of a self-concept organized around a niche that no one has authorized him to relinquish, in the company of a friend whose growth necessarily reshapes the niche over time. The crises that destroy him will not be supervillain crises. They will be ordinary developmental crises with no available container.

The single highest-probability decompensation event in the forward record is **a secret-disclosure under prolonged absence-stress**, routed through whichever adult node he models as highest-leverage, executed in deliberate violation of his promise and rationalized as math. The single highest-impact event, if it occurs, is **the wound-touched conversation in which someone competent asks him how he is**, because the response to that question — whoever holds it, and whether they hold it well — restructures the load architecture his entire adult life will be built on. Watch the building. When the LEGO stops, the file escalates.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM: GANKE LEE

*Compiled for protective intelligence purposes. This section maps every accessible vector by which the subject can be reached, influenced, opened, closed, soothed, destabilized, or predicted. The orientation is custodial: knowing how a person can be moved is the precondition of guarding them from being moved by hostile parties. Where a vector implies an attack surface, the corresponding defensive note is included.*

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY LOAD-BEARING VULNERABILITY: THE SECRET

Everything begins here. Ganke has, since approximately age thirteen, held the single most operationally consequential secret in his social ecosystem: the civilian identity of Spider-Man. He has held it without an authorized confessor, without a sanctioned outlet, without compensation, and without — until very recently — even Miles fully understanding the cognitive-affective weight of the ask.

**Mechanism of vulnerability.** The secret is not held as a fortress; it is held as a *pressure vessel with a faulty release valve*. The valve is conversational. Under load, Ganke's anxiety routes outward through speech — and speech, in the presence of a trusted-feeling listener, drifts toward the contents of his actual cognitive foreground. The Bombshell disclosure (*Spider-Man* 2016) and the earlier Judge disclosure (*USM* 2011 #6-10) follow the same waveform: extended proximity, lowered guard, social warmth, a moment of "they could *help*" reframing, and the secret exits.

**Hostile exploitation profile.** A competent social-engineering operator would not interrogate Ganke. They would *befriend* him. The attack window is 6–14 weeks of low-key, high-warmth, intellectually flattering presence — someone who shares his references, validates his competence, and presents as a peer rather than an authority. The disclosure would arrive unprompted, in the form of helpfulness ("you should meet my friend, he could—"). This is the gravest leverage vector on him.

**Defensive countermeasures.**
- *Authorized confessor.* The single most protective intervention available is sanctioning a specific, vetted person to whom Ganke is permitted to talk about the load — ideally Miles's mother (Rio), who already knows, or Ganke's own parents (if eventually read in). The valve needs a legitimate outlet so it stops leaking through unauthorized seams.
- *Novelty-friend surveillance.* New close friendships forming around Ganke warrant gentle monitoring at the relationship-shape level (not the content level). Slow, asymmetric warmth from a new peer who shares too many of his interests is the relevant pattern.
- *Decision-rule installation.* Ganke responds to genre logic; he can be taught a rule ("anyone who *asks* about Spider-Man's friends is presumptively unsafe") with a fictional-template scaffold and will internalize it.

---

## 2. ROUTES OF CALMING — HOW TO REACH HIM WHEN HE IS DYSREGULATED

Ganke's dysregulation is quiet and easy to miss. It manifests as: accelerated speech, denser pop-culture referencing, increased food intake, increased screen-glance frequency, and a subtle migration toward the horizontal (he gets on the bed, the couch, the floor). He does not announce distress; the body announces it.

**Calming protocols, ranked by reliability:**

1. **Co-presence without demand.** Sit near him. Do not require eye contact. Do not request he articulate what is wrong. Within 8–20 minutes of low-pressure proximity he will begin offering fragments of what is bothering him, voluntarily, framed as observations rather than confessions.
2. **A discrete physical task with constructive feedback.** Hand him a manual, a small assembly, a system to troubleshoot. The LEGO instinct is not a hobby; it is regulatory architecture. Bilateral hand activity with stepwise success metrics down-regulates him faster than verbal reassurance.
3. **Food, specifically familiar food.** Cereal, dumplings, takeout staples from his rotation. Caloric intake genuinely stabilizes his affect; the eating-on-panel pattern is not gag — it is somatic self-regulation that the writers have observed accurately.
4. **Validation routed through competence.** "You were right about X" lands harder than "you're a good friend." Praise of accuracy registers; praise of character glances off, because he distrusts character-praise as social lubricant.
5. **Humor responsiveness.** If you laugh genuinely at one of his deflective jokes during a stressful moment, his shoulders drop visibly. Laughing *with* him is sedative; laughing *at* the situation he is making jokes about is sedative; laughing at *him* is contraindicated and will close the channel.

**Contraindicated approaches:**
- Direct emotional inquiry ("are you okay?") prompts performative reassurance, not disclosure. He answers it as a social greeting.
- Silence-as-pressure. Long pauses meant to invite him to speak the difficult thing produce *more* deflective speech, not less.
- Authority-framed concern. Adults expressing worry about him will be deflected with extra polish. He has trained his parents-voice and his teacher-voice; both are armored.
- Touching him without warning when he is dysregulated; he is not phobic, but he is sensorily reactive when surprised.

---

## 3. ROUTES OF PERSUASION

He is not difficult to persuade *of things*; he is difficult to persuade *to act against his core loyalties*. Within the wide field outside that core, his persuasion profile is:

- **Argument-from-pattern.** Show him the template the situation fits and he will accept the implication. "This is the part of the story where X happens" is, for him, a near-conclusive frame.
- **Argument-from-precision.** Specific numbers, working code, demonstrable mechanism — he updates fast on technical evidence. He does not require the argument to be charismatic; he requires it to be *correct in a way he can verify*.
- **Argument-from-affiliation.** If a person he trusts has already endorsed a position, he weights it heavily. Conversely, if a position is endorsed by someone he has tagged as socially or intellectually unserious, he discounts it.
- **Argument-from-consequence-to-Miles.** The trump card. Any argument that frames the action as protective of Miles routes around his other priors. This is the single most exploitable persuasion lever on him, and the most dangerous: a hostile actor who can credibly pose as concerned for Miles's safety has nearly unmediated access to Ganke's cooperation.

**He is resistant to:** moral abstraction divorced from concrete persons; appeals to status, prestige, or career advancement that require betraying friends; ideological framings that demand he choose a side against someone he likes. His ethical compass is *particularist* — loyalties to known persons override principles in the abstract.

---

## 4. ROUTES OF PROVOCATION

He is unusually hard to provoke into anger. Across more than a decade of canon, depicted anger from Ganke is sparse and shallow. The provocation surface is not rage; it is *embarrassment, humiliation, and being made small in front of someone whose regard he wants*.

**Effective provocations (i.e., reliable destabilizers — listed for protective awareness, not endorsement):**
- Public diminishment of his intelligence. Being talked down to *in front of* peers, especially peers he respects, produces visible withdrawal and a long subsequent silence.
- Romantic humiliation. Being rejected dismissively, or being made the punchline of a romantic situation in front of Miles, hits him at the only seam where his self-deprecation isn't pre-armored.
- Being treated as Miles's accessory, not as a person, *by Miles*. He absorbs this from others without protest; from Miles it would wound, though he would not display the wound for hours or days.
- Having his loyalty questioned in a way that names a specific failure. General suspicion he can joke off. "You told Judge" — a specific historical leak named back to him — strips his defenses; he has no rebuttal because the charge is true and he knows it.
- Being condescended to about his ethnicity. He has had to correct the assumption-of-Chinese repeatedly (the explicit clarification in *Spider-Man* 2016 #2 is not isolated; it indexes a recurring micro-friction). He performs equanimity, but the cumulative load is real, and a calculated, racially condescending move would land hard.

**He is largely immune to:** insults to his appearance (already self-deprecated); insults to his athleticism (already conceded); insults to his hobbies (he holds them with secure pride); accusations of cowardice for not fighting (he has examined this and is at peace with the role).

---

## 5. PREDICTION VECTORS — WHAT HE WILL DO

Ganke's behavior is unusually forecastable because his patterns are stable across years and writers. A custodial intelligence apparatus can plan around the following high-confidence predictions:

**Daily-rhythm predictions.**
- Awake later than is healthy; he will be on his laptop between 11pm and 2am with above-baseline probability.
- First waking action is phone-check; first hour of consciousness involves screen-mediated information ingestion before food.
- Eats irregularly through the day with a heavy late-evening snack window; the snack window is when he is most conversationally available and most prone to disclosure.
- Walks the same dorm-to-class routes; deviates only with announcement.
- Returns to the dorm room as a default state. If Miles is absent, Ganke will be in the room. This is operationally important: the room is his locator.

**Crisis-rhythm predictions.**
- Within 60 seconds of learning Miles is in trouble: he will open a laptop and a phone simultaneously and begin parallel information gathering.
- Within 5 minutes: he will have texted at least two other people in Miles's circle, framed as coordination but functioning also as anxiety distribution.
- Within 30 minutes if the crisis is sustained: he will begin building or organizing something with his hands while continuing comms.
- He will not leave the room to physically search unless explicitly directed. His default is the hub, not the field.
- He will not call Miles's parents on his own initiative *unless* the threshold has been crossed where he believes Miles may not survive. That call, when it comes from Ganke, is a maximum-severity signal.

**Relational predictions.**
- He will not initiate conflict. If a rupture is needed, the other party must initiate.
- He will forgive faster than is wise.
- He will accept exclusion from a hero-context with a joke, return to the room, and continue to be available. The cost of this absorbed exclusion is not zero, but it accrues silently.
- Given a choice between a social gathering and staying in to build/code/watch something, he will choose in roughly 70/30 favor of staying in — with the 30% rising sharply if a specific person he wants to see will be present.

---

## 6. ROUTES OF DESTABILIZATION (for hostile-actor modeling, defensive use only)

Mapping these explicitly so they can be guarded against:

1. **Long-game peer-infiltration** (described in §1). Highest yield, lowest detectability.
2. **Engineered isolation from Miles.** If Miles is made unavailable to Ganke for a sustained period — weeks — while a hostile actor is concurrently present and warm, Ganke's load-distribution instinct will route toward the available warmth. The countermeasure is contact-cadence preservation: even brief, regular contact from Miles closes this vector.
3. **Family-targeted pressure.** Ganke's parents are sparsely depicted in canon and therefore an underexplored vector; precisely *because* he protects them by keeping his super-adjacent life invisible to them, a hostile actor who approached his family could leverage Ganke's protectiveness without his knowing the leverage existed. Defensive note: his parents should be quietly perimeter-aware even without being read in.
4. **Romantic exploitation.** A staged romantic interest from a hostile actor would penetrate his defenses faster than any other vector except the long-game peer route, and likely faster than that for short-duration operations. His pursuit pattern is earnest, fumbling, and grateful for reciprocation; reciprocation from an attractive, available person whose attention seems improbable is the configuration most likely to disable his judgment.
5. **Information overload / paralysis play.** Feeding him too many credible-looking data streams during a crisis can fork his attention and degrade his hub function. He has not been stress-tested against deliberate informational warfare; his pattern-matching strength becomes a weakness if the patterns being fed are adversarial.
6. **Forcing a binary loyalty choice in public.** Made to choose between Miles and another bonded figure in front of both, under time pressure, he will likely freeze and then default to Miles — but the freeze itself is the destabilization, and any choice made under that condition will haunt him afterward in ways that further degrade his reliability.
7. **Removal of his constructive outlets.** Take away the LEGO, the laptop, the building activities, and his regulatory architecture collapses to *talking* — and talking, under load, is the leak vector. A captivity scenario stripped of his hand-tools would yield disclosure faster than most interrogators would expect.

---

## 7. PROTECTIVE LEVERS — HOW TO STRENGTHEN HIM

Custodial work is not only defensive; it is constructive. The following interventions would meaningfully reduce his vulnerability surface:

- **Authorize a confessor** (revisited from §1). The single highest-impact protective action.
- **Install a code-word disclosure protocol with Miles.** A pre-agreed phrase Miles can offer that releases Ganke from secrecy obligation in a specified context, and a phrase Ganke can offer that signals he is being socially worked. This transforms ambient anxiety into a procedural ritual he can execute.
- **Provide him a sanctioned operational role.** He already functions as a hub; making that role explicit — with a name, a remit, and a defined chain of communication — converts informal load into formal duty. Formal duty carries less anxiety than informal load because its boundaries are knowable.
- **Periodic deload.** Scheduled windows where Miles tells him explicitly that he is off-duty for 48 hours, no comms expected. He will not request this. He requires it.
- **Romantic-context briefing.** Without compromising his autonomy, he should be made aware — once, in a serious register, by Miles — of the romantic-exploitation vector. He will joke through it; the information will stick anyway.
- **Cultivation of one non-Miles-related close friendship.** A peer bond whose stakes are entirely Ganke's own would distribute his identity-load away from the Miles axis and reduce the catastrophic-loss profile of any rupture with Miles.
- **Quiet observation of his sleep, appetite, and verbal-density baselines.** Drift in any of the three is his earliest somatic signal of accumulating load. Catch the drift, address the load.

---

## 8. THE LATENT FAULT — WHAT HAS NOT YET BEEN TESTED

The honest custodial reading: Ganke has not yet been subjected to a sustained, sophisticated, person-specific hostile operation. He has been incidentally endangered (proximate to villain attacks on Miles), socially complicated (the disclosure leaks), and emotionally taxed (Miles's broadening world), but he has never been the *target* of an intelligence-grade approach.

His defenses are well-suited to the conditions he has faced: ambient stress, social complexity, intermittent acute danger, and the chronic low-grade weight of the secret. They are not battle-tested against patience, against engineered loneliness, against a hostile actor who understands him better than his friends do.

The structural prediction follows: if and when he is targeted in earnest, the failure mode will not be courage (he has it in his way) and will not be loyalty (it is unshakeable in intent). The failure mode will be *the load finding the wrong outlet at the worst moment*, executed by someone who took the time to become the right-feeling listener.

The custodial mandate, therefore, is not to make him harder — hardening him would cost the things that make him valuable to Miles and to himself. The mandate is to ensure he is *never alone with the load long enough for the wrong listener to matter*.

That is the file. That is the lever map. Guard accordingly.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE: GANKE LEE

## Preamble to the Ledger

A surveillance file ordinarily skews toward vulnerability — what a subject lacks, fears, conceals, can be leveraged against. The Ganke Lee file is unusual in that the asset column is heavier than the liability column, and the assets are not merely numerous but *structurally interlocking*. He is one of the rare adolescent subjects whose strengths reinforce one another rather than compete for the same scarce regulatory bandwidth. The following ledger is exhaustive by design; the cumulative weight is part of the finding.

---

## 1. COGNITIVE & INTELLECTUAL ASSETS

### 1.1 Working memory and parallel-processing capacity

Subject demonstrates, across every depicted technical sequence from *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* (2011) #2 forward, the ability to hold multiple data streams in active consideration simultaneously. He follows a live-action superhero conversation, manipulates a laptop interface, tracks a news feed, and references a media analog *within the same beat*. This is not the panel-convention shorthand of a "smart kid"; it is consistent enough across writers (Bendis, Ahmed, Ziglar) to read as a stable trait. Operationally: he can serve as a real-time information node without dropping channels.

### 1.2 Pattern-recognition saturation

His mind runs on template-matching. Genre conventions, system schematics, narrative structures, LEGO build logic, code architectures — these are all the same cognitive primitive deployed across surfaces. The asset is rapid orientation: dropped into a novel situation (spider bite, vanished best friend, costumed villain at a school dance), he triangulates against known templates and produces a *workable first hypothesis* within seconds. The famous instance is the original disclosure — he metabolized "my roommate has spider powers" into "you are Spider-Man, you need a costume, the black one is right" inside a single conversation. That speed is a hard asset.

### 1.3 Encyclopedic genre and pop-culture literacy

Wide rather than deep, but the breadth is its own value. He reads superhero context fluently because he has consumed the corpus; he predicts villain behavior because he has seen the archetype; he understands the social grammar of the costumed life because the grammar is, to him, native fiction. In a world where Miles is constantly entering situations without a manual, Ganke effectively *is* the manual — approximate, sometimes wrong, always available.

### 1.4 Technical fluency

Coding, hardware modification, comms setup, alibi-fabrication via digital infrastructure. He is not a meta-tier hacker (no documented penetration of secured government systems, no Stark-grade fabrication), but he operates competently at the *applied amateur* level — the level that matters in a domestic dorm-room context. He has built or repurposed equipment to monitor Miles's patrol environment and to manage his parents' inquiries. The fluency is durable because it is recreational; he does this for love, not duty, and so it does not fatigue.

### 1.5 Verbal facility

Hyperverbality is, in many subjects, a tic to be flagged. In Ganke it is a working tool. He talks fast, fluently, with register-control — he can speak to Miles's parents, to teachers, to a girl he is trying to impress, to a former villain, and to Miles himself, in different cadences. The verbal flow is also a *social lubricant under threat*: he can fill awkward space, redirect attention, soften confrontation, or buy seconds with chatter. In a surveillance frame, the man who can always say something is the man who is never caught silent.

### 1.6 Academic standing

Sustained enrollment at Brooklyn Visions Academy — a selective gifted boarding charter — across multiple academic years with no depicted disciplinary failure, no academic probation, no remedial intervention. He carries the courseload while functioning as Miles's logistics shop. Time-management and executive function are intact at a level few adolescents achieve under comparable load.

---

## 2. EMOTIONAL & TEMPERAMENTAL ASSETS

### 2.1 Stable affective baseline

He runs at a light-positive mood floor. Across roughly a decade of publication, he has not been depicted in despair, rage, prolonged grief, or anhedonic withdrawal. The range is narrow but the *floor is high*, which is the more important variable for sustained functioning. He wakes up okay; he goes to bed okay; this is not nothing.

### 2.2 Humor as mature defense

In the Vaillant hierarchy, humor is a *mature* defense — alongside sublimation, altruism, suppression, anticipation. Ganke deploys it reflexively. Crucially, his humor is *not contemptuous*; it does not punch down, does not establish hierarchy, does not function as aggression sublimated. It is genuine play. This distinguishes him from the resentful-joker archetype and accounts for why no one in his social field reads him as hostile.

### 2.3 Sublimation through construction

The LEGO-and-build habit is a depicted *self-soothing protocol* with measurable regulatory benefit. Bilateral repetitive fine-motor activity combined with low-stakes constructive cognition is, in clinical terms, a near-optimal anxiety regulation strategy — comparable in mechanism to knitting, mechanical hobby work, certain forms of art therapy. He stumbled onto it as a kid and has never stopped. The asset is the *involuntary* nature of the regulation: he does not need to be told to self-regulate, he simply builds.

### 2.4 Affiliation as primary coping

Under stress, he reaches outward. This is, in attachment terms, the *secure* response — neither anxious clinging nor avoidant withdrawal but instrumental connection-seeking. He calls, gathers, communicates. The cost is the disclosure-leak pattern (the principal liability in the prior section); the benefit is that he never *isolates*, which is the precondition of most adolescent decompensation.

### 2.5 Low-aggression temperament

Across the record, he has not been depicted in a fistfight, a screaming argument, a vengeance-seeking arc, or a sulking withdrawal. He metabolizes interpersonal friction quickly — confronts when needed, repairs immediately after, does not carry grudges. This is a temperamental gift; it cannot be trained into people who do not have it.

### 2.6 Non-envy

The structural asset. Adolescent best friends of extraordinary peers almost universally develop envy subroutines — at minimum a private comparative ledger, at worst an active resentment that becomes story-fuel. Ganke has not, across writers and years, exhibited this. He genuinely takes pleasure in Miles's powers, Miles's love life, Miles's expanding hero-circle. He does not maintain a deficit ledger about himself. This is rare, and it is the single most important emotional asset he possesses, because it means his support is not contaminated by suppressed grievance.

---

## 3. ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL ASSETS

### 3.1 Secure base in the friendship with Miles

The primary bond is, by every behavioral indicator, secure: rupture-and-repair functional, absence-tolerant, non-possessive, mutually reciprocated. He weathers Miles's disappearances; Miles weathers his disclosures; both return. The bond's *durability under stress* is itself a resilience factor for Ganke, because secure attachment to even one figure buffers a great deal of subsequent life stress.

### 3.2 Family backdrop (low-information, but inferentially stable)

The Lee family is barely depicted, which in this dossier-frame is itself data. The absence of crisis, of estrangement narrative, of "rebel against the parents" arc, of financial hardship plot, of overinvestment-by-parents subplot — the absence of all of these suggests a *baseline-functional* family of origin: enough resources to enroll him at a selective boarding charter, enough latitude to let him pursue hobbies, enough trust to let him board, no documented dysfunction. He carries no family wound onto panel. That blankness is an asset.

### 3.3 Widening rather than contracting social field

He has demonstrably integrated additional figures into his orbit over time — Judge, Bombshell/Lana, Miles's extended hero-circle, school peers — without dropping Miles. The capacity to *add without subtracting* is a relational hallmark of secure functioning and an asset against the late-adolescent loneliness curve.

### 3.4 Bombshell pursuit as evidence of independent romantic agency

Even fumbling, even comic in execution, the courtship of Lana Baumgartner demonstrates that he can want for himself, pursue for himself, and risk rejection for himself, separate from his function in Miles's life. The romantic apparatus is intact and operating. That he chose someone with a criminal past — socially "off-limits" by conventional metrics — indicates he selects partners on personal appraisal, not on social safety. This is a maturity indicator.

### 3.5 Multi-register social competence

Documented competence across at least five interactional registers: peer-friend (Miles), peer-romantic (Bombshell), peer-acquaintance (school), adult-authority (teachers, Miles's parents when needed), and adult-stranger (occasional public encounters). The register-switching is fluent and intact. He is socially *legible* to everyone, which is a substantial life asset.

### 3.6 Trustworthiness as reputational capital

Despite the disclosure-leak pattern (which is, in fairness, narrow — he leaks Miles's secret to people he over-trusts, not to enemies or authorities), no one in his social field treats him as untrustworthy. He is given keys, given access, given confidences. The asset is the *perception* of reliability, which functions as durable social currency regardless of the more granular truth.

---

## 4. CHARACTEROLOGICAL & MORAL ASSETS

### 4.1 Accurate self-location

He knows what he is. He is not the hero, not the love interest, not the chosen one. He is the friend who knows things. He has *located himself accurately on the map of his own life* without diminishment, which is a developmental achievement most adults do not reach. The asset is the absence of identity churn — he does not waste cognitive load on becoming-someone-else fantasies; that load is available for the actual work.

### 4.2 Pro-social orientation as a default

When he encounters a problem, his first move is *help*. Not gain, not evade, not document for leverage. The instinct is consistent enough across years and writers to be character rather than convenience. In intelligence terms, this is a subject whose actions can be predicted by asking "what helps Miles / what helps the friend in front of him." The predictability is itself useful, and the orientation is itself good.

### 4.3 Loyalty without ideology

His loyalty to Miles is not a creed; it is not theorized; he has not made a religion of it. It is simply *what he does*. This matters because ideological loyalty is brittle — it can be argued out of, recruited away from, or shattered by a single doctrinal failure. Loyalty-as-practice is durable. No one is going to talk Ganke out of being Miles's friend, because being Miles's friend is not, in his architecture, a position; it is a habit.

### 4.4 Moral simplicity in the best sense

He has not developed the corrupt-sophistication that often accompanies proximity to power. He has been adjacent to vigilante violence, criminal-adjacent peers, civilian-endangering crises, and the moral edge of the costumed life — and he has not slid into noir cynicism, moral relativism, or instrumental reasoning about people. He still thinks villains are bad, heroes are good, friends help friends. The apparent naïveté of this is actually a *post-naïveté*: he has seen the complication and chosen the simpler frame because it produces better behavior.

### 4.5 Counter-conformist undercurrent

Beneath the rule-following exterior — the homework done, the curfew observed, the parents handled — there is a verifiable counter-conformist streak: the choice of a former-villain romantic interest, the casual normalization of harboring a fugitive identity, the willingness to fabricate alibis against institutional authority on his friend's behalf. He is not a conformist; he is a *strategic accommodator* who will quietly break rules he disagrees with. This produces durable ethical action without the social cost of overt rebellion.

---

## 5. INSTRUMENTAL & PRACTICAL ASSETS

### 5.1 The dorm room as operational infrastructure

The Brooklyn Visions dorm has functioned, across the publication record, as Miles's de facto staging ground: costume change, post-patrol decompression, gear storage, comms, alibi base. Ganke maintains the infrastructure — meaning he sustains a physical environment in which Miles can transition between civilian and operational identities without exposure. The maintenance includes physical security (door watch, traffic control), informational security (devices, accounts), and social security (managing roommates' awareness, faculty visits, RA inquiries). This is, in operational terms, *safehouse-keeping at a professional standard performed by an unpaid teenager*.

### 5.2 Alibi-generation capability

Documented across multiple arcs: Ganke produces plausible cover stories for Miles to Rio and Jefferson, to teachers, to school administration. The stories are typically genre-aware (he avoids the lie that will be checked), narratively coherent (they hold under follow-up questioning), and consistent across retellings. He has effectively been Miles's press secretary for years.

### 5.3 Comms / intelligence node

He runs feeds — police scanners, news, social media — and routes the relevant signal to Miles in real time. In *Spider-Man* (2016) onward, this guy-in-the-chair function is depicted concretely. The asset is not the technology; the asset is the *judgment* about what is signal and what is noise, which he performs well.

### 5.4 LEGO collection / hobby infrastructure

Easily catalogued as trivial; should not be. The collection represents (i) a sustained sublimatory resource available 24/7, (ii) a depicted personal-meaning archive that anchors identity across change, (iii) a physical-object investment that gives his living space cognitive texture beyond the screen. It is also, incidentally, an indicator of household economic stability and parental tolerance.

### 5.5 Educational pipeline

The BVA enrollment is an asset of compounding value: peer network, academic record, college pipeline, institutional credentialing. Whatever Ganke's adult trajectory becomes, the credential floor is high.

### 5.6 Time-on-task discipline

He completes builds, finishes code, sustains hobbies across long arcs. The capacity to *finish* is rarer than the capacity to start, and he has it. This generalizes to anything he chooses to apply it to.

---

## 6. RESILIENCE FACTORS (STRUCTURAL)

### 6.1 The combination, not the components

Each of the foregoing assets exists in other subjects; the combination is the resilience. Stable mood + mature defenses + secure attachment + accurate self-location + non-envy + pro-social default + intact family backdrop + competent hobbies + academic standing = a redundancy architecture in which the failure of any one regulator is buffered by the others. If humor stops working, sublimation is still there. If sublimation is interrupted, affiliation is still there. If affiliation is unavailable, the secure-base mental representation of Miles is still there. The system has *depth*.

### 6.2 Genre-literate optimism as worldview

He operates on the implicit belief that situations are tractable, that the clever and the kind tend to prevail, that problems decompose into solvable pieces. This is not the same as Pollyanna naïveté; it is a *constructive prior* that biases his behavior toward action and persistence rather than freeze or surrender. People who believe problems are solvable solve more problems, both because the belief is sometimes correct and because the belief sustains the effort that would otherwise stop.

### 6.3 The build-something heuristic

When in doubt, build. LEGO, code, plan, friendship, alibi, costume concept. The heuristic is generative: it produces output where rumination would produce paralysis. It is the operational signature of a person who, faced with any stuck situation, will do *something* rather than *nothing* — and the something is usually useful or at least informative.

### 6.4 Non-grandiose ambition

He wants to be in the room where it happens; he does not need to be at the podium. The ambition is real but bounded, which makes it sustainable. Grandiose ambition collapses under the first major failure; modest, situated ambition compounds across years.

### 6.5 Suppression and anticipation (further mature defenses)

In addition to humor and sublimation, two more Vaillant-mature defenses are evident: *suppression* (he can shelve his own concerns when the situation demands focus on Miles; this is conscious, not repressive) and *anticipation* (he plans for likely contingencies — alibis pre-built, comms pre-configured, snacks pre-stocked, costume concepts pre-considered). The mature-defense battery is broad; this is the clearest psychological asset on the file.

### 6.6 Absence of trauma history

Across his publication record he has not been kidnapped for long durations, bonded with a symbiote, suffered family death, been physically tortured, been depowered (he has no powers to lose), been written into amnesia or possession arcs. The *trauma ledger is empty*. This is partly writerly protection but operates, in subject's lived continuity, as a clean substrate. He has the rare adolescent-in-costumed-fiction advantage of carrying no unprocessed catastrophic event.

### 6.7 Continuity of self across writers

The voice, manner, values, and operating mode have remained stable across Bendis, Ahmed, and Ziglar — three writers with notably different sensibilities. The stability indicates a character whose architecture is durable enough to resist drift. In subject terms, this maps to *integrated identity*: he is the same Ganke in different contexts, which is itself a major resilience factor (identity diffusion being the principal late-adolescent vulnerability he does not display).

### 6.8 Capacity to be helped, if help were offered

This belongs in the asset ledger even though the latent fault line in the prior section noted that no one is currently positioned to help him carry his load. He has not developed help-rejecting behaviors. He has not built the brittle pride that prevents adolescent males from accepting support. If a competent confidant were introduced — an adult, a peer cleared into the secret, a counselor — he would, on the evidence, *use* the resource. The receptivity is intact.

---

## 7. STRATEGIC SYNTHESIS

The asset profile reads, in sum, as that of a subject who has been quietly building — not dramatically, not visibly, not with the spotlight on him — a *life that works*. The cognitive equipment is above average and applied; the emotional architecture is stable and mature-defended; the relational world is secure and widening; the moral orientation is consistent and pro-social; the practical capabilities are real; and the resilience factors are layered with redundancy. He is, by the standards of any adolescent intelligence file, an *over-equipped* subject for the life he is currently leading.

Two implications follow.

**First, prognostic.** Subjects with this asset profile do well across the lifespan. They form durable friendships and partnerships, sustain careers in collaborative-intellectual fields, raise functional children, and reach old age with their networks intact. Nothing in the file forecasts a catastrophic trajectory absent a major exogenous shock; even with such a shock, the buffer architecture predicts recovery.

**Second, the asset most under-recognized — by the subject, by his social field, by writers — is the cumulative *effect on Miles* of being held, for years, by a friend with this profile.** Miles's own resilience is partly downstream of Ganke's. Heroes adjacent to a stable confidant develop differently than heroes who go it alone. The asset, from a wider-system view, is Ganke-as-stabilizing-substrate. He has been quietly load-bearing for the entire Morales-as-Spider-Man arc, and the arc has not collapsed, and his quietness about this is exactly the form his contribution takes.

The honest ledger entry is this: Ganke Lee is one of the lowest-risk, highest-asset adolescent subjects in his cohort, and the principal danger to his trajectory is not internal but situational — that he is carrying a load no one currently knows to relieve him of. The strengths are real, durable, and sufficient. The question is whether the situation will outpace them. On current data, they hold.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# UATU DOSSIER — GANKE LEE
## Section 7: Failure Modes & Decompensation

### 7.0 Premise

The subject has, across more than a decade of documented existence, never been depicted in a state of clinical collapse. This is not evidence of absence; it is evidence of *latency*. Every defense the subject runs — humor, sublimation through construction, affiliation, information-dispersal — is load-bearing, and load-bearing structures fail in predictable ways once load exceeds a particular threshold. What follows maps those failure pathways: the staged escalation, the precise behavioral signatures that would mark each stage, the conditions that produce them, and what total collapse would look like in a subject whose entire psychic architecture is organized around *not* collapsing in front of his best friend.

The subject's defenses are mature (humor, sublimation, affiliation in Vaillant's terms) and his attachment is secure. This means decompensation, when it comes, will be *slow*, *quiet*, and *late-presenting*. He will not break in the dorm room in front of Miles. He will break in the dark, alone, on his laptop, at 3:14 a.m., months after the load became unbearable, and the first visible indicator will be something trivial — a missed text, an uneaten snack, a half-finished LEGO model left on the desk for a week.

That last image is the diagnostic. Track the unfinished build.

---

### 7.1 The Load Curve

Decompensation in this subject is not event-driven. It is *cumulative*. He has demonstrated repeatedly that he can absorb a single high-magnitude shock (the bite reveal, a near-death of Miles, exposure threats) by routing it through humor and immediate problem-solving. What he is *not* engineered to absorb is sustained, undischargeable load over multi-month timescales without an authorized confidant.

The load components, in observed order of weight:

1. **Identity-secret containment.** Constant. Non-negotiable. No one in his life is cleared to hear it except Miles, who is the source of the burden and therefore cannot be its repository.
2. **Casualty anticipation.** The persistent low-grade awareness that Miles may not return from a given patrol. Subject monitors news feeds and police scanners; this is not hobby behavior, it is vigilance behavior dressed as hobby behavior.
3. **Alibi maintenance.** Cumulative cognitive load of fabricating, tracking, and not contradicting prior lies told to parents (Rio, Jefferson), school administration, and peers. Each lie is a node that must remain stable indefinitely.
4. **Social isolation by content.** He can be with people, but he cannot be *known by* them. The most interesting fact about his life — that he is the witness to a Spider-Man — is the one fact he cannot share. This produces a chronic asymmetry in every non-Miles relationship.
5. **Romantic vulnerability.** Any romantic partner not read into the secret will, eventually, experience him as evasive. He cannot explain why he disappears, why he checks his phone, why he leaves parties.

The load curve is not linear. It is a staircase: long flat plateaus during quiet narrative periods, sharp risers during crisis arcs, with no corresponding descents — load added does not come off.

---

### 7.2 Stage One: Compensated Strain (the current and longest-running state)

This is where the subject lives. It looks like health and largely *is* health, but it runs on continuous expenditure of regulatory effort that a baseline adolescent would not need to spend.

**Behavioral signatures, baseline:**
- Verbal output elevated above peer norm; gaps in conversation are filled rather than tolerated.
- Snack consumption steady; preferred substrates are high-glycemic and tactile (cereal, chips, gummies) — oral self-soothing.
- LEGO builds completed at a regular cadence; sets displayed in finished form.
- Screen time high but task-organized; tabs and windows logically clustered.
- Sleep onset late, sleep duration adequate-to-short, wake time forced by class schedule.
- Affect light-positive; humor frequency one joke per minute or higher in dyadic conversation with Miles.

**Indicators of strain *within* the compensated state:**
- Slight increase in deflective humor density when serious topics are introduced (the joke-to-statement ratio rises).
- Reassurance-seeking questions phrased as casual ("you good?" "you back?" "you alive?") at higher frequency after dangerous events.
- The disclosure-leak: when load briefly exceeds capacity, the pressure-release valve opens — he tells someone he shouldn't. This is not malice. This is *somatic*. The information is, for him, physically heavy, and his nervous system discharges weight through the mouth.

The leak pattern is the canary. It is documented across runs and writers, which makes it diagnostically reliable. Each leak event indicates that the subject crossed his containment threshold and used unauthorized disclosure as the regulatory mechanism. The leaks are small enough that they have not so far broken the system; they should be read instead as the system *functioning as designed* under chronic overload.

---

### 7.3 Stage Two: Partial Decompensation

Entry conditions: sustained high-magnitude crisis (multi-week Miles-in-danger arc), OR durable removal of Miles from physical proximity (extended absence, presumed-dead status, off-world arc), OR introduction of a new secret-holder whom Miles trusts more (perceived displacement).

**Onset signatures, in approximate order of emergence:**

- **Verbal acceleration without content gain.** The joke density rises but the joke quality drops. References become more obscure, more compulsive, less landed. He is talking to keep talking. Listeners begin to feel talked-at rather than talked-with.
- **Snacking pattern shift.** Quantity holds or rises; *attention* drops. He eats without registering taste. Wrappers accumulate. He forgets what he had last.
- **LEGO disruption.** This is the highest-specificity diagnostic in the entire profile. The subject builds when regulated. When he begins a set and does not finish it — and especially when he begins multiple sets and finishes none — the sublimation channel has lost continuity. Pieces scattered on the desk for more than 72 hours indicates the regulatory apparatus is failing to close loops.
- **Screen behavior degrades.** Tabs proliferate without organization. He begins to leave videos playing as ambient noise rather than watching them. He scrolls feeds without pausing. The pattern-matching mind that normally builds structure begins to consume undifferentiated content.
- **Sleep collapse, asymmetric.** Onset becomes later; wake remains forced. Total sleep contracts. He naps in clothing, on top of the comforter, in the late afternoon, with the laptop still open beside him.
- **Disclosure leak escalation.** The leaks become larger and to riskier recipients. Where Stage One leaks are to peripheral peers, Stage Two leaks would be to a romantic partner, an authority figure, or a public-facing channel (a too-revealing post, a comment thread, a left-open browser).
- **Reassurance-seeking becomes pre-emptive.** Where baseline reassurance follows danger, partial-decomp reassurance precedes it: he begins texting Miles for status checks during periods when nothing is happening. The vigilance subroutine has begun to run untriggered.
- **Selective social withdrawal.** Note: not generalized. He withdraws from contexts that require performance (parties, large groups, romantic dates) but maintains presence in low-demand dyadic settings (Miles, possibly one or two trusted peers). The classic introverted exhaustion presentation, but stress-elevated.
- **Somatic emergence.** This is where the body finally starts collecting the bill. Tension headaches; jaw clenching at night (he would not register this himself); gastrointestinal complaints metabolized as "I ate something weird"; a viral illness that lingers longer than peers'.

Critical caveat: the subject's mature defenses *mask* Stage Two effectively. To an inattentive observer — including Miles, who is by definition load-saturated himself — Ganke in Stage Two still looks like Ganke. The signatures are present but presented as ordinary adolescent quirks. Stage Two can persist for months before anyone with standing to intervene notices.

---

### 7.4 Stage Three: Active Decompensation

Entry conditions: a triggering event layered onto Stage Two substrate. Candidate triggers, ranked by likelihood of producing this stage:

1. **A leak with consequences.** He tells someone, and someone gets hurt — Miles is exposed, a family member is targeted, a peer is endangered. The information-dispersal valve, which has been his regulatory mechanism for years, has now produced the precise outcome it was meant to prevent. The defense that was keeping him functional becomes the source of his guilt. This is the most dangerous configuration.
2. **Romantic rupture explicitly tied to the secret.** A partner ends the relationship citing his evasiveness, his absences, his "you're hiding something." He cannot defend himself without violating Miles. He absorbs the rupture as confirmation that his entire social future is foreclosed by his role.
3. **Miles's catastrophic injury or death.** The subject has organized his identity around supporting an outcome (Miles's continued existence and effectiveness as Spider-Man). Removal of the supported object removes the structural reason for the support apparatus, exposing him to the realization that he has spent his formative years in service to a function rather than a self.
4. **Explicit displacement by Miles.** Miles takes another civilian into confidence in a way that reads to Ganke as "you were not enough." This is the cruelest trigger because it converts years of secure attachment into retrospective evidence of conditional regard.
5. **Family discovery.** His parents learn what he has been doing — and, more painfully, what he has *not* been telling them — for years. His family is sparsely depicted but inferentially present; their disappointment would land on a domain (filial trust) that he has been protecting precisely by not being interrogated.
6. **A LEGO-channel collapse.** Less obvious but worth flagging: if his sublimation hobby becomes contaminated by the trauma (a build interrupted by a Miles-emergency, a treasured set destroyed in a fight, the activity itself becoming associated with helplessness), he loses his most reliable self-regulator at the worst possible time.

**Presentation in Stage Three:**

- **Humor degradation to silence or to edge.** The defining transition. Either the joke stops coming — silences land where deflections used to — or the jokes acquire teeth: jokes about his own irrelevance, jokes about Miles's mortality, jokes that make listeners flinch. The mature defense (humor) regresses toward a less adaptive one (passive aggression, gallows affect).
- **Acute disclosure event.** Either a complete public-facing breach (he posts something, he tells a journalist, he confesses to a therapist who is not bound to him), or, paradoxically, complete containment lockdown — he becomes evasive about *everything*, including ordinary matters, because the boundary between sayable and unsayable has destabilized and he no longer trusts his own filter.
- **Tearfulness in private, flat affect in public.** Subject would not be observed crying. He would be observed not laughing.
- **Eating disruption.** Either binge escalation (the snacking pattern broken loose from any pretense of regulation, with subsequent shame and concealment) or appetite drop (a far more alarming signal in this subject, given the baseline). The body that was always fed becomes a body that forgets to be fed.
- **Sleep inversion.** Awake all night, asleep through morning classes. Academic attendance lapses. This is significant: the subject's academic identity has been stable across all canon. Class-skipping in Ganke is a flashing red.
- **Hobby abandonment.** Builds unbuilt. Sets in boxes. The desk cleared not from completion but from refusal to look at it. Tech projects stalled mid-line.
- **Reassurance-seeking inverts to reassurance-rejection.** Where he once asked Miles "you good?", he now answers "fine" to Miles's reciprocal question with a flatness Miles will register on the second or third repetition. He has begun to refuse the social transactions that previously regulated him.
- **Cognitive narrowing.** The associative, reference-saturated mind contracts. He stops making the genre comparisons; he stops pattern-matching out loud. The narrative-structured worldview that previously made the world *make sense* to him has been disconfirmed by an event the templates did not predict.

Stage Three is the stage at which intervention becomes possible *because* it becomes visible. The mature defenses have cracked. The people around him — Miles first, ideally — can finally see the load.

---

### 7.5 Stage Four: Collapse

This stage is hypothetical; no canon evidence supports it having occurred. It is the projected terminal state if Stage Three is unaddressed for sustained periods (estimate: 8–16 weeks given his baseline resilience).

Collapse in this subject does not look like a breakdown in the classical sense. He will not become unruly, violent, manic, or floridly symptomatic. The mature-defense substrate prevents disorganized presentation. Collapse, for Ganke, looks like *graceful disappearance*.

**Projected presentation:**

- He maintains social surface. He responds to texts, attends meals, completes minimum required school output. The exterior smooths and quiets. People who knew him as the loud friend will describe him as "calmer lately." This will be read positively. It is not.
- The interior has become a withdrawal he is no longer fighting. The humor is gone but is not missed by him; he has stopped noticing its absence. He is functioning at a baseline that *is* the new baseline, not a temporary low.
- He develops a private ritual — likely screen-mediated, possibly a single repetitive game, a single rewatched show, a single forum he scrolls — that consumes the hours where regulation used to live. The ritual is not pleasurable. It is occupied.
- He stops initiating contact. He responds when prompted. The asymmetry will eventually be noticed by Miles or by his mother, but the latency is long because he is a reliable responder.
- Anhedonia emerges as the dominant affective state. Light-positive baseline drops to flat-neutral. He no longer laughs at things he previously found genuinely funny; he produces the laugh as a social token.
- The body settles into a slow somatic accumulation: weight changes (direction less predictable than the existence of change), persistent low-grade illness, dental signs of bruxism, posture compression.
- He becomes, in clinical language, sub-threshold depressed with anxious features and chronic adjustment disorder — finally meeting criteria he previously did not, but at a level low enough that he could go undiagnosed for years.

The danger of collapse in this subject is not acuity. It is *durability*. He will not generate the kind of crisis that summons help.
