He will quietly settle into a diminished version of himself and stay there, possibly for the rest of his adolescence, possibly longer. The friend who was structurally irreplaceable becomes structurally invisible, and the irony is that his disappearance is the consequence of how well his presence was tolerated.

---

### 7.6 What He Will Not Do

A failure-mode profile is incomplete without naming the pathways he is unlikely to take, because their unlikelihood is itself characterological.

- **He will not betray Miles deliberately.** Disclosure leaks are regulatory, not vindictive. Even at full Stage Three, the prospect of intentional betrayal is foreign to his attachment configuration.
- **He will not turn villain.** The envy-to-antagonism arc that the genre uses for sidekicks is not available to him; the resentment substrate is absent at trait level, not merely suppressed.
- **He will not become a vigilante in compensation.** He has no physical-action template and no desire for one. Heroism for him is participation, not performance.
- **He will not direct aggression outward in any sustained form.** Anger is not a frequent state and not a preferred discharge channel. Under collapse, aggression turns inward as anhedonia and self-erasure rather than outward as conflict.
- **He will not seek therapy unprompted.** His self-concept does not include "the kind of person who needs help"; his role identity is *helper*. The role-symmetry breach required to ask for support is, for him, a higher activation barrier than the suffering it would relieve.
- **He will not run.** Geographic flight is not in his repertoire. He decompensates in place.

---

### 7.7 The Conditions That Produce Collapse

In order of structural causal weight:

1. **Absence of an authorized confidant of his own.** This is the foundational condition. Every other risk factor multiplies against this one. If he had one cleared adult — a school counselor read into the situation, a therapist with appropriate clearance, even an adult in Miles's family who acknowledged what he carries — the load curve would shed weight at a sustainable rate. He does not have this. He has never had this. No writer has given it to him.
2. **The structural asymmetry of his role.** He gives support; he is not the recipient of comparable support. Miles loves him and would die for him, but Miles's bandwidth is consumed by being Spider-Man, and Ganke has organized his presentation around not adding to that bandwidth load. The reciprocity gap widens silently.
3. **The narrative-template worldview's vulnerability to disconfirmation.** He believes the world has structure and that good outcomes are reachable by the clever and kind. A single sufficiently brutal disconfirmation — a death the story should not have allowed, a betrayal the genre should have flagged — could destabilize his entire orienting frame.
4. **Adolescent developmental timing.** He is carrying adult-grade containment load on a still-forming identity substrate. The years in which most peers consolidate selfhood through varied disclosure and feedback, he is spending in selective concealment. The developmental cost compounds.
5. **The protection-by-omission paradox.** He has been kept structurally safe by canon — uninjured, untransformed, uncaptured. This safety has prevented the kind of acute event that would force the system to address his load. Paradoxically, his narrative safety extends his exposure to chronic strain.

---

### 7.8 The Diagnostic Lattice — What to Watch For

If this subject is under monitoring with the goal of catching decompensation before it consolidates, the following indicators should be tracked, in approximate order of sensitivity and specificity:

- **The half-built LEGO.** Highest specificity. A build begun and abandoned for more than three days, in a subject whose entire panel history shows completion, is a near-pathognomonic indicator of regulatory failure.
- **Joke-density and joke-quality divergence.** When the rate rises while the landing rate drops, the defense is straining.
- **Tab-count without task-coherence.** Screen behavior shift from organized to ambient is an early cognitive-narrowing signal.
- **Pre-emptive status texts to Miles.** Vigilance running untriggered.
- **Late wake, not late sleep.** Sleep-onset shift alone is ordinary; wake-time slippage indicates the system has lost its remaining anchor.
- **Snack registration loss.** He still eats, but he forgets what he ate. Oral self-soothing is decoupling from awareness.
- **A leak to a person who matters.** Distinguished from baseline leak by recipient stakes.
- **Class absence.** Late-stage indicator; by the time it appears, the slide has been ongoing for weeks.
- **Cessation of unsolicited reference-making.** The associative mind has gone quiet. This is the indicator that the inner life has dimmed.
- **The flat "fine."** Terminal indicator. He has stopped using language to regulate, which means he has stopped using language as language.

---

### 7.9 Summary

The subject's failure mode is not dramatic. It is *attritional*. He has been built — by temperament and by canon — to absorb damage without showing it, and the cost of that durability is that his eventual decompensation will be late, quiet, and easy to miss. He will not collapse spectacularly; he will diminish gradually. The load that produces this trajectory is the load he was assigned the moment he chose, in a dorm room at Brooklyn Visions, to react to his roommate's terror with delight instead of fear — a choice that defined him beautifully and that has been quietly billing him ever since.

The dossier's open question, restated as a surveillance brief: *the joke is the load-bearing member; watch the joke.* When the joke goes — not when it changes, when it goes — the structure is already failing. By the time the silence is audible, the collapse is months old.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU DOSSIER — GANKE LEE
## Section 6: Trajectory & Forward Assessment

---

### 6.0 Framing the Forecast

Forecasting a civilian secret-keeper differs categorically from forecasting an operational asset. The subject does not generate plot; he metabolizes it. His trajectory is therefore largely a function of *load dynamics* — the rate at which the burden of proximity to Spider-Man accumulates against the rate at which his existing regulatory architecture (humor, sublimation through tech/LEGO, affiliative discharge, information dispersal) can metabolize it. The question is not *what will Ganke do*; it is *what will the load do to Ganke, and at what point does his current operating system require replacement rather than patching*.

The forecast horizon usefully divides into three bands:

- **Short (12–24 months published / ~late adolescence intradiegetic):** completion of Brooklyn Visions, college transition or non-transition, Bombshell arc resolution, first true containment failure or first true containment success of consequence.
- **Medium (3–7 years):** young-adult identity consolidation, vocational selection, the inevitable structural test of whether the Miles-bond survives geographic and developmental divergence.
- **Long (decade-plus):** adult-life shape, whether he remains in the orbit of costumed life or exits it, and whether the latent fault line identified in §4 ever fractures.

Each band has fork points. Each fork has a growth vector and a catastrophe vector. They are mapped below.

---

### 6.1 Short-Horizon Forks (Imminent / Active)

#### 6.1.1 The Bombshell Fork

The Lana Baumgartner relationship is the subject's first sustained romantic structure and his first relational bond not subordinate to the Miles-bond. It is therefore *developmentally indispensable* regardless of outcome. Two branch points:

- **Growth branch.** The relationship deepens past the comedic-fumbling phase into something requiring him to disclose interior material he has historically kept compartmented (his fears, his family situation, his ambivalences about Miles's life). Lana, herself a person with an extensively non-normative biography, is structurally suited to receive such disclosures without judgment. If the writers allow this — and if Ganke risks it — Bombshell becomes the *authorized confidant* whose absence is the latent fault line identified in §4. This single relational addition would reduce his catastrophic risk profile by a substantial margin.
- **Catastrophe branch.** The relationship is treated as a B-plot joke and terminated without him having disclosed. He returns to baseline architecture with the additional belief that intimacy outside the Miles-bond is not achievable for someone in his role. This belief, if entrenched, ossifies the caretaker-deflection pattern into something resembling avoidant personality features by his mid-twenties.

The fork is currently open. The writerly default — comic-relief romance — points toward the catastrophe branch through neglect rather than malice.

#### 6.1.2 The Containment Fork

The disclosure-leak pattern (Judge in *USM* #6–10; subsequent diffusion through *Spider-Man* 2016) is overdue for either *correction* or *catastrophe*. The subject is approaching the developmental age at which the cost of leakage compounds — peers entering adult social networks, secrets spreading faster, the Morales family's continued safety contingent on opacity.

- **Growth branch.** A near-miss leak — one he catches himself, or one Miles catches and processes without rupture — produces the conscious metacognitive insight Ganke has not yet articulated: *I share when I am scared. I need somewhere to put the fear that is not another person's mouth.* The acquisition of this insight, and the development of a non-relational discharge channel (journaling, an authorized confidant, structured solitude), would mature the defense into intentional containment rather than reflexive porosity.
- **Catastrophe branch.** A leak with stakes — Rio Morales endangered, a villain triangulating Miles through Ganke, a peer monetizing the secret on social media — produces a rupture in the Miles-bond severe enough that the bond itself becomes the wound rather than the support. Subject's entire psychological economy is calibrated to this bond; its rupture would be the single most destabilizing event in his life and the most likely trigger for the first clinically significant presentation.

#### 6.1.3 The Academic / Vocational Fork

Brooklyn Visions is a gifted-track institution; subject is on a college trajectory. Pattern recognition, code-fluency, systems thinking, and pop-cultural omnivory point toward several plausible vocational attractors:

- Software / systems engineering (the path of least resistance given displayed skill).
- Game design or narrative-design (consistent with the genre-literate, structure-loving cognitive style and the LEGO/building motif).
- Library / information science or archival work (consistent with the curatorial impulse, the desire to *organize and disseminate knowledge in service of others*).
- Comparative literature / media studies (the analytical-of-narrative habit professionalized).
- A non-conventional creator path: streaming, criticism, modding, indie game dev.

The vocational fork is less catastrophic than the others — none of these paths are toxic to him — but it interacts with the Miles-bond fork: a path that anchors him in NYC near Miles preserves the bond's geometry; a path that pulls him elsewhere (a coastal CS program, a games studio relocation) forces the bond to renegotiate.

---

### 6.2 Medium-Horizon Forks (3–7 Years)

#### 6.2.1 The Divergence Test

The structural reality of best-friendships formed in adolescence is that ~70% do not survive young-adult divergence in their original intensity. The Ganke–Miles bond is unusually robust — secure-attachment baseline on Ganke's side, demonstrated reciprocal investment from Miles, shared catastrophic-knowledge floor that cannot be replicated with anyone new — but the *normal* pressures still apply: time-zone drift, partner-prioritization, the formation of adult professional networks that do not overlap.

The growth scenario is that the bond *transforms* — from continuous co-presence (roommates, school-aligned) to high-trust, lower-frequency adult friendship with discrete high-stakes activations. Ganke is structurally well-suited to this transition: he is *non-jealous* (a documented trait, §1 Ahmed-run analysis), accommodates Miles's expanding world without contracting, and would likely manage geographical distance better than most. He is the friend who texts a meme at 2 a.m. and resumes mid-sentence after six months of silence.

The catastrophe scenario is that the Miles-bond does not transform but instead *attenuates while remaining unacknowledged as attenuated*. Subject continues to organize his interior life around a friendship whose actual bandwidth has collapsed, producing the slow, unspectacular grief of *being someone's old best friend* — a state for which his existing defenses are notably ill-suited. Humor metabolizes acute affect; it does not metabolize chronic, ambient loss. This is the scenario in which subclinical anxiety could ripen into something more durable: persistent low mood, somatization (the body finally registering what the mind has been declining to register for a decade), or — most likely given his architecture — a marked uptick in screen-mediated, food-mediated, and purchase-mediated self-soothing. The midnight LEGO sets get larger and more expensive. The snack inventory expands. The laptop is never closed.

#### 6.2.2 The Inheritance-of-the-Knowledge Fork

By his mid-twenties subject will have held a costumed-identity secret for roughly a decade. This is a longer custody than most professional intelligence officers serve on any single piece of compartmented information. The accumulated *meta-knowledge* — not just Miles's identity, but the operational rhythms of the broader hero ecosystem; Ganke knows who calls whom, who is dating whom, which safehouse is functional, which villain is overstated, who the actual threats are — makes him, by adulthood, a *de facto* node in an informal civilian-adjacent intelligence network.

Two branches:

- **Growth (and the most psychologically generative outcome):** subject professionalizes this organically into a legitimate support role — Mariah-Hill-adjacent civilian liaison; in-house tech / archivist for a hero collective; consultant to a Daily Bugle / J. Jonah-successor publication that requires someone fluent in costumed-life logistics. The role *authorizes* the knowledge he already holds, gives him peers who share the load, and ends the structural isolation that is his single most important risk factor. He stops being the only civilian who knows; he becomes one of a small guild who do, and the guild is the confidant his life has lacked.
- **Catastrophe:** the knowledge becomes a target. Adult Ganke, holding a decade of operational information about Spider-Man and his network, is — by any rational adversary's calculus — a higher-yield kidnap target than he was as a teenager, and his civilian status makes him softer than any hero. The very fact that he has been kept *structurally safe* through publication history (§2) means the dramatic debt is unpaid. The most likely first true trauma of his adult life is being *taken because of what he knows*, and surviving it; the second most likely is being taken and not telling, which would establish for him for the first time the felt experience of his own moral steel — potentially transformative, potentially shattering.

#### 6.2.3 The Family Fork

The family is barely depicted in canon and the subject avoids self-disclosure about them. Two latent scenarios:

- The family is functional and the under-depiction is writerly neglect; in this case, the medium horizon involves the normal adult-child renegotiations (career disagreement, distance, the disclosure or non-disclosure of his proximity to costumed life) without dramatic incident.
- The family is the *unspoken weight* — high-pressure immigrant-academic expectations, a parental relationship organized around achievement rather than knowing, the reason the caretaker-deflection pattern formed in the first place. In this scenario, the medium horizon contains a confrontation: career choice as proxy for identity claim, partner choice as proxy for the same, or the moment subject realizes he has spent a decade emotionally available to a friend in part because such availability was never modeled or returned at home.

The record is genuinely insufficient to discriminate. The under-depiction itself is data — characters whose families are *deliberately* under-rendered often carry exactly the dynamics that the under-rendering would obscure.

---

### 6.3 Long-Horizon Trajectory (Decade-Plus)

The most probable adult shape, given trait stability across writers and the maturity of his existing primary defenses, is **a functional, well-liked, professionally competent adult in a knowledge-economy role, partnered or married, residing within a one-hour radius of wherever Miles ends up, carrying a circle of friends substantially overlapping the one he has now plus a professional cohort.** He is the friend who hosts. He is the uncle who builds the elaborate gift. He runs a podcast or a Substack or a Discord that is consistently good and modestly remunerative. He is, in adulthood, recognizably continuous with the adolescent he is now.

The deviations from this baseline that the record permits us to imagine, in roughly descending order of probability:

1. **The quietly heroic civilian.** He never costumes. He is, instead, the person without whom several costumed careers would have ended. This is the trajectory in which his role is finally legible *as a role* — not "sidekick," but *infrastructure* — and in which he derives the meaning he has always sought from the participation, not the performance.
2. **The late-arriving crisis.** Mid-thirties. The joke stops working. Subject presents — to a partner, to a therapist, to himself in a parked car at 2 a.m. — with the affect he has spent twenty years metabolizing through deflection. This is the *delayed-onset* scenario, and it is the most clinically interesting because his architecture is sufficiently mature that the crisis, when it comes, will likely resolve productively rather than destructively. He is built to survive his own breakdown if and when it arrives.
3. **The geared transition.** He acquires, through some plausible mechanism (a tech-suit gift from Miles, a non-powered tactical role with a team, a synthesized neural-interface that converts his pattern-recognition into operational utility), a marginal field role. This is the *Oracle-shaped* trajectory and it is plausible but not necessary; the record does not show subject *wanting* the field, and his deepest psychology is satisfied without it.
4. **The exit.** A genuine, conscious withdrawal from costumed-life proximity, executed not as a rupture with Miles but as a maturational claim on a life of his own. This requires more deliberate self-construction than he has yet demonstrated but is consistent with the secure-attachment baseline. The growth-vector version of this trajectory ends with him still in Miles's wedding party, still on the group chat, but no longer the load-bearing humor.
5. **The catastrophe end-state.** Death-by-association in a villain operation targeting Miles through him; the unpaid dramatic debt finally called. This is the writer-decision scenario more than the trait-driven one, and any forecasting model has to assign it nonzero probability given the genre. Were it to occur, his trait architecture predicts that the death itself would be *characteristically Ganke* — a joke landed, a useful piece of information passed, a posture of constructive engagement maintained to the last beat. The catastrophe is for those who survive him, principally Miles, on whom the loss would land with disproportionate force precisely because the relationship has been so structurally undramatized in life.

---

### 6.4 The Open Questions

A complete dossier must register what it does *not* know. The following are the durable epistemic gaps in the subject file, ranked by forecasting consequence:

1. **What does he want for himself, distinct from what he wants for Miles?** The record gestures (Bombshell, mild academic ambition, hobby investment) but does not substantiate. Until this is articulated — by him, on panel, in a voice that is not deflective — the forecast is necessarily conditional.
2. **Who is his family and what did they teach him about being known?** The caretaker pattern has an origin and the origin is almost certainly there.
3. **Has he ever told anyone how much it costs to be the keeper?** If yes, who, and what was the cost of telling. If no, the latent fault line remains intact and the medium-horizon risk profile is what it appears to be.
4. **What does he believe about his own future?** The genre-literate optimist worldview suggests he expects a good one. Whether he has imagined specifics, or whether his imagination is fully occupied by Miles's specifics, is unknown.
5. **What would he do if Miles stopped being Spider-Man?** This is the single most clarifying counterfactual the file contains. The answer would reveal whether the bond is *intrinsic* (he loves Miles, Spider-Man is incidental) or *role-structured* (he loves the participation, Miles is the access). Every available indicator points to the former, but it has never been tested.

---

### 6.5 Pressure Map: What Pushes Toward Growth vs. Catastrophe

**Growth vectors:**

- Acquisition of an authorized confidant (Bombshell, a therapist, a guild of similarly-situated civilians).
- Vocational role that legitimizes and remunerates the curatorial-supportive disposition.
- A near-miss containment failure that produces metacognitive insight without consequence.
- A partner who actively elicits his interior rather than accepting his deflections.
- Miles explicitly naming and valuing the support — not as gratitude in passing, but as recognition of the load.
- A moderate, survivable first trauma (kidnap-and-survive; the family confrontation; the relationship that ends and is grieved) that establishes for him the felt knowledge of his own resilience.

**Catastrophe vectors:**

- Containment failure with consequence to the Morales family.
- Sustained, unacknowledged attenuation of the Miles-bond.
- Romantic foreclosure entrenching the belief that intimacy outside the role is unavailable.
- Acute targeting by an adversary aware of his function.
- Indefinite continuation of the current structure into his mid-twenties without any of the growth interventions — the *no-event* scenario, which is paradoxically the most dangerous, because it allows the latent fault line to deepen unaddressed.

---

### 6.6 Final Assessment

The subject's forecast is governed by a counterintuitive principle: *he is most at risk when nothing happens to him*. His architecture is mature enough to metabolize discrete shocks; what it cannot metabolize, indefinitely, is the slow accretion of an unshared load in a life otherwise structured around sharing. The single most useful intervention available to those who care about him — and the single most likely omission of the writers who steward him — is the granting of a confidant of his own. Without it, he becomes, by stages, the most poignant figure in his own friend group: the one who held everything and was held by no one, and who discovered this only when the architecture finally tired.

With it, he becomes the rarest thing the genre produces: a civilian who built a meaningful adult life adjacent to the extraordinary without being deformed by it, and who is, at fifty, still the friend you call first.

The forecast, on balance, favors the second outcome — not because the structure inevitably produces it, but because the subject's own trait architecture is *constructive*. He is, after all, someone who builds. Given time, materials, and a partner willing to hand him the pieces, the probability is high that what he eventually builds is a life.

The dossier's standing recommendation, for the benevolent surveillance this file represents: *watch for the moment he stops making the joke. That is the moment to be reachable.*
